Rulings on Exchange of Dirhams and Dinars (Sarf)
Multiple rulings on deferment and addition in gold/silver exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi rulings on sarf involving unequal quantities with additional items, mixed coins, and custom-based measurement.

Core Idea
In sarf, equality is required, but extra items or predominant alloy can legitimate excess.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents several key rulings on the exchange (sarf) of silver dirhams and gold dinars. These rulings illustrate important exceptions and clarifications regarding the prohibition of riba in currency exchange. Understanding these cases will deepen your grasp of how Hanafi fiqh handles real-world transactions where coins are not pure or where additional items are included.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
The first example: selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and a dinar. The sale is valid because the dinar is an additional commodity that compensates for the shortfall in silver. Note that the exchange involves both gold and silver, so the ruling on riba applies separately to each element.
The additional item must be of a different genus or reach the value of the missing silver.
2
Analyze the second ruling
A debtor sells a dinar to his creditor for ten dirhams owed, then they mutually agree to exchange the dinar for the ten dirhams. This is valid because the initial sale and subsequent exchange are separate transactions, avoiding any prohibited deferment or excess.
The sale of the dinar for debt is a separate contract; the later exchange is a new transaction.
3
Understand the third ruling
Exchanging one good dirham and two mixed dirhams for two good dirhams and one mixed dirham is valid. The excess is allowed because the mixed dirhams are not considered pure silver, so they belong to a different category.
Mixed dirhams (makhshushah) have predominant alloy, so they are not subject to ribawi rules for pure silver.
4
Grasp the principle of predominance
When alloy predominates in a gold or silver coin, it is no longer treated as a ribawi commodity. Thus, selling such coins of the same type with excess is permissible.
If silver or gold predominates, the coin retains its ribawi status and equality is required.
5
Learn the role of custom
If dirhams are customarily traded by weight, then all transactions (sale, purchase, loan) are by weight. If traded by count, then by count. This prevents ambiguity and matches the common practice.
Custom ('urf) is a recognized basis for ruling in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گیارہ دراہم کی دس دراہم اور ایک دینار کے ساتھ بیع کا حکم: چاندی کی چاندی کے بدلے سونے کی سونے کے بدلے ان میں سے ایک کم ہے اور کم کے ساتھ کوئی دوسری چیز بھی ہے جو بقیہ چاندی کی قیمت کو پہنچ جاتی ہے تو بیع جائز ہے۔ جس کے دوسرے پر دس درہم تھے اس نے قرض خواہ کو ایک دینار دس درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا اور دینار دیدیا اور باہمی رضا مندی سے دس درہم کے ساتھ بدلہ کر لیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ ایک درہم صحیح اور دو درہم غلہ کی دو درہم صحیح ایک درہم غلہ کی بیع جائز ہے۔ جس چیز کا سونے چاندی میں غلبہ ہے اس کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ سونے چاندی میں کھوٹ غالب ہو تو دراہم ودنانیر کے حکم میں نہیں۔ دراہم مخشوشہ اپنی جنس کے ساتھ تفاضلاً بیچنا جائز ہے۔ دراہم کا رواج وزن کے ساتھ ہو تو بیع و شراء استقراض وزن کے ساتھ ہوگا۔ اگر عدد و شمار سے رواج ہو تو شمار سے ہوگا۔
The ruling on selling eleven dirhams with ten dirhams and a dinar: Silver for silver, gold for gold. One of them is less, and along with the less there is another item that reaches the value of the remaining silver, then the sale is valid. Someone who had ten dirhams due from another person sold a dinar to the creditor in exchange for ten dirhams, gave the dinar, and mutually agreed to exchange it for ten dirhams — this is valid. The sale of one good dirham and two mixed dirhams for two good dirhams and one mixed dirham is valid. Consideration is given to that which predominates in gold and silver. If the alloy is predominant in gold or silver, it is not in the ruling of dirhams and dinars. Selling mixed-minted dirhams (makhshushah) with their own genus with excess is permissible. If dirhams are customary by weight, then sale, purchase, and loan are by weight. If they are customary by number, then by number.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings regarding the exchange (sarf) of dirhams (silver coins) and dinars (gold coins). The first ruling addresses a case where the quantities are unequal but an additional commodity makes up the difference, thereby avoiding riba. The second example involves a debt settlement where a dinar is sold for dirhams. The third allows exchanging good and mixed dirhams in a way that avoids forbidden excess. The fourth clarifies that when a coin is predominantly alloy, it is not treated as a pure gold or silver coin, and selling mixed coins of the same type with excess is allowed. The final ruling explains that the method of counting or weighing depends on local custom.

Key Terms
دراہم (dirham): Silver coins used as currency; the unit of currency in the text.
دینار (dinar): Gold coin; a unit of currency.
دراہم مخشوشہ (darahim makhshushah): Dirhams that have been mixed with alloy (debased, not pure silver).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid ruling from this lesson?
A) Selling pure silver dirhams for pure silver dirhams with any excess is always forbidden.
B) Selling mixed dirhams (makhshushah) with their own genus with excess is permissible.
C) The method of counting for dirhams is always by weight regardless of custom.
D) The exchange of a dinar for multiple dirhams is always invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits exchange of gold/silver with difference in quantity when a separate commodity balances the value, or when the coin is predominantly alloy, and custom defines the measure.

Rulings on Fulus (Copper Coins) When Currency Becomes Obsolete
Rules for transactions when fulus lose currency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each type of transaction (sale, loan, exchange) involving fulus when they suffer a market slump and apply the principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
A sale using fulus becomes void if the currency fails; value stability is an implicit condition.

In this passage, we explore how Hanafi fiqh handles transactions when the medium of exchange—fulus (copper coins)—loses its market value. The key insight is that the validity of a sale depends not only on the agreement but also on the ongoing usability of the currency. Understanding this rule protects both parties from unfair loss when currency collapses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction type
Read each scenario in the passage: sale of goods with mixed dirhams, sale with fulus, loan of fulus, purchase with fulus for a specific value, and money-exchange transaction. Note the object (fulus or dirhams) and the action (sale, loan, exchange).
The passage uses 'رائج' (current) to indicate currency in use.
2
Identify the condition triggering invalidity
The condition is 'کساد بازاری' (market slump) meaning the fulus lose their tradeability and people stop dealing with them. Once this occurs, the transaction is affected.
This is an external event that invalidates the basis of the contract.
3
State the ruling for each scenario
For sale (with fulus or mixed dirhams), the sale is void (باطل). For a loan, the debtor must repay the equivalent number of fulus (مثل واجب). For a purchase for half a dirham's worth of fulus, the buyer owes the current value of half a dirham in fulus. For the money-changer, the exchange of fulus is valid but the remainder (short dirham) is void.
The ruling differs based on whether the transaction is an exchange (mu'awada) or a debt (dayn).
4
Extract the general principle
The perpetuity of currency value is an implicit condition (shart) in contracts involving fulus. When that condition fails, the contract becomes void or is adjusted to preserve justice.
This principle prevents one party from gaining unjustly from currency collapse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دراہم مغشوشہ کے عوض سامان خریدا پھر وہ کساد بازاری کا شکار ہو گئے اور لوگوں نے اس کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنا چھوڑ دیا تو بیع باطل ہے۔ فلوس کے عوض بیع کا حکم: رائج فلوس کے عوض بیچی پھر وہ کساد بازاری کا شکار ہو گئے تو بیع باطل ہے۔ رائج الوقت فلوس کے ساتھ قرض لیا وہ کساد بازاری کا شکار ہو گئے اس کی مثل واجب ہوں گے۔ کوئی چیز نصف درہم فلوس کے بدلے خریدی تو مشتری پر اس قدر فلوس واجب ہوں گے جن کو نصف درہم کے عوض بیچا جاتا ہے۔ صراف کو ایک درہم دیا اور کہا کہ اس کے نصف کے بدلے فلوس اور دوسرے نصف کے بدلے نصف درہم ایک حبہ کم دو۔ فلوس میں بیع جائز اور بقیہ میں باطل ہے۔
Goods were purchased in exchange for mixed dirhams, then those dirhams suffered a market slump and people stopped dealing with them, so the sale is void. The ruling of sale in exchange for fulus: He sold in exchange for current fulus, then they suffered a market slump, so the sale is void. He borrowed current fulus, then they suffered a market slump; its equivalent is obligatory. He bought something for half a dirham's worth of fulus, then the buyer owes as many fulus as are sold for half a dirham. He gave a dirham to a money-changer and said: 'Give me fulus for half of it, and for the other half give half a dirham less one habbah.' The sale is valid for the fulus and void for the remainder.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage deals with fulus (copper coins) and dirhams that are mixed with alloy (maghshusha). The key principle is that if the currency loses its marketability (cashad bazari), the sale becomes void because the countervalue is no longer valid. If one purchased goods with such coins and they later become obsolete, the sale is annulled. Similarly, if one loans fulus and they become obsolete, the debtor must repay the equivalent value at the time of repayment. In the case of a money-changer, if the transaction involves two different exchanges (fulus and dirham) with an unequal balance, the valid part is the fulus exchange, while the remainder is void because it involves a deficient quantity without compensation.

Key Terms
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as currency, typically of low value.
کساد بازاری (kasdad bazari): Market slump or loss of currency value/tradeability.
حبہ (habbah): A small weight unit, often a grain; here a fraction of a dirham.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person buys goods in exchange for the current fulus, and then the fulus suffer a market slump (become worthless), what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid and the buyer must pay the original fulus.
B) The sale is void because the fulus are no longer currency.
C) The sale is valid but the buyer must pay the equivalent value of the goods.
D) The seller has the option to rescind the sale.

Key Takeaway
A sale using fulus becomes void if the fulus lose their currency, while a loan of fulus requires repayment of the equivalent amount.

Rights of Upper and Lower Apartment Owners and Alley Access
Ruling on vertical property and alley branching rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the rights of lower apartment owners to install structural elements and on when owners of a first alley may open a door into a branch alley.

Core Idea
Lower owner may install beams/lights; first alley cannot open door into dead-end rectangular branch, but may if branch is circular.

This lesson explains two distinct property scenarios under Hanafi fiqh: vertical division of a building and horizontal division of an alley. Understanding these rules helps prevent disputes over easements and respects customary rights based on urf (custom) and the principle of preventing harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage addresses two separate situations: (1) an upper apartment and lower house owned by different persons, and (2) a first alley that branches into a second alley. Recognize that the ruling for each depends on specific conditions.
2
Apply the ruling to each scenario
For scenario 1: the lower owner has permission to install structural elements (beams) and create openings for light/air, based on customary support rights. For scenario 2: if the branch alley is rectangular and not a through alley (dead-end), the first alley owners cannot open a door; if the branch is circular (ends meet), they may open a door.
The distinction hinges on whether the branch alley is private (dead-end) or common (circular).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالا خانہ ایک شخص کا اور نیچے کا مکان دوسرے شخص کا ہو نیچے والے کو شیش [؟] گاڑنے اور روشن، ان بنانے کا حکم ہے. گلی مستطیلہ ہو جس سے دوسری مستطیل گلی نکلی حالانکہ وہ آر پار نہیں تو پہلی گلی والوں کو دوسری گلی میں دروازہ کھولنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا اگر زائغه ثانیه متدیرہ ہو جس کے دونوں کنارے ملے ہوئے ہوں تو زائغہ اولی والوں کو اختیار ہے
If an upper apartment belongs to one person and the lower house to another, the lower one has permission to install [beams?] and make [lights?]. If there is a rectangular alley from which another rectangular alley emerges, and it is not a through alley, then the owners of the first alley do not have the right to open a door into the second alley. If the second branch is circular, with its two ends meeting, then the owners of the first branch have the right.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling deals with property rights and easements. When two properties are vertically divided, the lower owner has certain rights to install structural elements (like beams) and create openings for light/air. The second part concerns alley rights: if a rectangular alley branches into another rectangular alley that is a dead end (not through), the owners of the first alley cannot open a door into the second alley because that would infringe on the rights of the second alley's owners. However, if the second branch is a circular alley (cul-de-sac) that returns to itself, the owners of the first alley have the right to open doors into it. This is based on customary use and avoidance of harm.

Key Terms
بالا خانہ (bala khanah): The upper apartment or story of a building.
گلی (gali): An alley or pathway used for access.
زائغه (zaigha): A branch or side alley, probably a dead-end alley.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case can the owners of the first alley open a door into a second alley?
A) When the second alley is a through alley
B) When the second alley is rectangular and not through
C) When the second alley is circular (dead-end that returns to itself)
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants lower apartment owners customary rights for structural support and light, and strictly regulates door openings into branch alleys based on whether the branch is a dead-end or circular.

Seller's Right to Intercourse with Slave-Girl After Buyer's Denial
Ruling on seller's right with slave-girl after buyer denies sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a seller abandons a claim after the buyer's denial and identify the condition that makes intercourse permissible.

Core Idea
If the seller drops the lawsuit, the slave-girl remains his; intercourse is halal.

In transactions involving slave-girls, ownership disputes can arise. When the buyer denies the sale, the seller has a choice: pursue litigation or abandon the claim. This lesson examines the latter scenario and its legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Parties
Determine the act being ruled upon (intercourse with a slave-girl) and the parties involved (seller and buyer). Note the buyer's denial of the sale.
2
Identify the Seller's Decision
Focus on the seller's firm resolve not to pursue litigation (خصومت نہ کرنے کا پختہ ارادہ). This is the key condition.
3
Derive the Ruling
Since the seller abandons his claim, the slave-girl remains his property. Therefore, intercourse is lawful (halal) for him.
No further court action is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک نے کہا کہ تو نے مجھ سے یہ باندی خریدی ، دوسرے نے انکار کیا، بائع نے خصومت نہ کرنے کا پختہ ارادہ کیا، بائع کے لئے اس باندی سے وطی کرنا حلال ہے
One said: You bought this slave-girl from me. The other denied it. The seller firmly resolved not to pursue litigation. For the seller, having intercourse with that slave-girl is halal.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling concerns a disputed sale of a slave-girl (bought often for concubinage). The seller claims a sale occurred; the buyer denies it. If the seller decides not to take legal action and abandons his claim, the slave-girl remains his property (since the buyer denies ownership). Therefore, it is lawful (halal) for the seller to have intercourse with her, as she is still his property. The key condition is the seller's intention to drop the dispute, implying he accepts the denial.

Key Terms
بائع (ba'i'): Seller.
وطی (wat'): Sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the seller do to lawfully have intercourse with the slave-girl after the buyer denies?
A) Win a court case
B) Get the buyer's written rejection
C) Firmly resolve not to pursue litigation
D) Sell the slave-girl again

Key Takeaway
If the seller abandons his claim, the slave-girl remains his, making intercourse lawful.

The Legality of Salam Sale: Definition and Proofs
Definition and proofs for Salam sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Salam sale, identify its legal evidence from Quran and Sunnah, and explain why the Hanafi school overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Salam sale is permitted by Quran and Sunnah despite qiyas, because revealed texts override analogy.

After discussing sales where possession is not required, the Hidayah turns to Salam, a contract where the price is paid immediately but delivery is deferred. This lesson unpacks the definition, proofs, and the core Hanafi reasoning that textual evidence takes precedence over qiyas. Understanding this establishes the pattern for many exceptions in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the structural context
Note that Salam is placed before Sarf because it requires possession of only one counter-value (the price), making it simpler. This ordering reflects the author's pedagogical logic.
The sequence 'simple before compound' is a recurring method in Hanafi texts.
2
Define the contract technically
Identify the technical terms: rabb al-salam (buyer), muslam ilayh (seller), ra's al-mal (capital), muslam fih (commodity). Learn the definition: a contract with immediate payment of price and deferred delivery of a specified fungible commodity.
The etymology from 'aslama' (to deliver) highlights the requirement of handing over the price in the session.
3
Identify the primary proof from Quran
The verse of debt (al-Baqarah 2:282) is cited. Ibn Abbas interpreted it to include Salam. Note that the command to write deferred debts implies permissibility of deferred contracts, and Salam is a specific type.
The verse's general command (amr) indicates permissibility (ibaha) in the Hanafi view.
4
Identify the Sunnah proof and the role of qiyas
The Prophet (ﷺ) forbade selling what one does not possess, but explicitly permitted Salam. This is a specific exception (rukhsah). The text then states: 'qiyas rejects it, but we have left qiyas due to what we have narrated'. This is an application of istihsan based on naql (revelation).
Qiyas would treat Salam as invalid because it sells a nonexistent object. The exception is a clear case of textual preference (istihsan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السلم
ترجمہ یہ باب بیع سلم کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے پہلے ان بیوع کو بیان فرمایا ہے جن میں عوضین یا احد العوضین پر قبضہ کر نا شرط نہیں ہے۔ ان سے فراغت کے بعد اب ان بیوع کا بیان ہے جن میں عوضین یا احد العوضین پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ بیع سلم میں احد العوضین یعنی راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے اور بیع صرف میں دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے بیع سلم میں چونکہ احد العونین یعنی راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اور بیع صرف میں دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اسلئے بیع سلم بمنزلہ مفرد کے ہوئی اور بیع صرف بمنزلہ مرکب کے ہوئی اور چونکہ مفرد، مرکب پر مقدم ہوتا ہے اسلئے بیع سلم کے احکام پہلے ذکر کئے گئے اور بیچ صرف کے احکام بعد میں ذکر کئے گئے ہیں۔ علامہ کا کئی کے حوالہ سے علامہ بدرالدین عینی نے لکھا ہے کہ لفظ سلم یا تو اسلم سے لیا گیا ہے اور ہمزہ اس میں سلب کیلئے ہے۔ کیونکہ رب السلم ، رأس المال یعنی در اہم مسلم الیہ کے سپرد کر کے اُن کی سلامتی کو زائل کر کودیتا ہے، یعنی رب اسلم نے جب راس المال مسلم الیہ کو دے دیا تو وہ رب السلم کے پاس سلامت نہ رہا۔ اور یا لفظ اسلم ، تعلیم سے لیا گیا ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم میں راس المال کا مجلس کے اندر سپرد کرنا لازم اور ضروری ہے۔ لفظ مسلم اور سلف دونوں مترادف ہیں۔ اسی طرح، اسلم اور اسلف مترادف ہیں۔ مسلم لغت میں ایک ایسی بیج کا نام ہے جس میں ثمن معجل ہوتا ہے یعنی فوری ادا کیا جاتا ہے اور فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں بیع سلم کہتے ہیں موجل کو منتقل کے عوض لیتا۔ بیع سلم کا رکن ایجاب اور قبول ہے۔ مثلا ، ایک آدمی دوسرے آدمی سے کہتا ہے۔ سلمت اليك عشرة دراهم فى كر حنطة يا اسلفت الي عشرة دراهم فى كر حنطة میں نے تجھ سے ایک گر گندم میں دس درہم کے عوض عقد سلم کیا دوسرے آدمی نے کہا میں نے قبول کر لیا۔ پس صاحب دراہم ، رب اسلام کہلائے گا اور دوسرا آدمی مسلم الیہ کہلائے گا اور گندم مسلم فیہ اور دراہم راس المال کہلائیں گے۔ بیع سلم کا حکم ، رب السلم کیلئے مسلم فیہ میں مؤجل طور پر ملک کا ثابت ہونا اور مسلم الیہ کیلئے فی الحال راس المال پر ملک کا ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ بیع سلم کی شرائط جواز خود آگے چل کر مصنف ہدایہ بیان فرمائیں گے ۔ فانتظروا اني معك منتظرين بي ع اسلم کی شرعی حیثیت
السلم عقد مشروع بالكتاب وهو آية المداينة فقد قال ابن عباس اشهد ان الله تعالى احل السلف المضمون وانزل فيها اطول آية في كتابه وتلا قوله تعالى ياايها الذين أمنوا اذا تداينتم بدين الى اجل سمى فاكتبوه الأية وبالسنة وهو ما روى انه عليه السلام نهى عن بيع ما ليس عند الانسان ورخص في السلم والقياس وان كان يأباه ولكنا تركناه بما رويناه ووجه القياس انه بيع المعدوم اذ المبيع هو المسلم فيه
Chapter of Salam. Translation: This chapter is about sale of Salam. Explanation: The author of Hidayah previously mentioned those sales where possession of the price or the object is not a condition. After finishing those, now the discussion is of those sales where possession of one or both is a condition. Thus, in Salam sale, possession of one of the two, i.e., the principal (ra's al-mal), is a condition, and in Sarf sale, possession of both is a condition. Since in Salam, possession of one is a condition, and in Sarf, possession of both is a condition, therefore Salam is like a simple (mufrad) and Sarf is like a compound (murakkab). And since the simple precedes the compound, the rulings of Salam are mentioned first and those of Sarf later. Through the narration of Allama, Allama Badr al-Din al-Ayni wrote that the word 'salam' is either taken from 'aslama' where the hamza is for negation (salab), because the rabb al-salam surrenders the capital (ra's al-mal) i.e., dirhams to the muslam ilayh and thus removes their safety from himself, meaning the rabb al-salam when he gives the capital to the muslam ilayh, it is no longer safe with him. Or it is taken from 'aslama' meaning 'ta'lim' (teaching) because in Salam sale, delivering the capital in the session is necessary. The words 'muslam' and 'salaf' are synonyms. Similarly, 'aslama' and 'aslafa' are synonyms. 'Muslam' in language is the name of a sale in which the price is paid promptly. In the terminology of jurists, Salam sale means taking the deferred (mu'ajjal) in exchange for the immediate (mu'ajjal). The pillar (rukn) of Salam is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). For example, one person says to another: 'I have given Salam to you ten dirhams in exchange for one kurr of wheat' or 'I have advanced ten dirhams to you for one kurr of wheat'. The second person says: 'I accept'. Thus the owner of the dirhams is called rabb al-salam (or rabb al-Islam), the second person is called muslam ilayh, the wheat is called muslam fih, and the dirhams are called ra's al-mal. The ruling of Salam is that the rabb al-salam establishes ownership of the muslam fih in a deferred manner, and the muslam ilayh establishes ownership of the ra's al-mal immediately. The conditions of validity of Salam will be stated later by the author of Hidayah: 'So wait, I am with you, waiting'. The legal status of Bay' al-Salam: Salam is a contract established by the Book, which is the verse of al-Madayinah. Indeed, Ibn Abbas said: 'I bear witness that Allah the Exalted has permitted the guaranteed salaf (advance payment), and revealed concerning it the longest verse in His Book', and he recited the verse: 'O you who believe, when you contract a debt for a fixed term, write it down...' (Quran 2:282). And by the Sunnah: what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade selling what one does not possess, but permitted Salam. And qiyas (analogy) rejects it, but we have left qiyas due to what we have narrated. The basis of qiyas is that it is a sale of a non-existent thing, because the sold item (al-muslam fih) is the muslam fih.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter of Salam (forward sale) from the Hidayah commentary. It first explains the ordering of chapters: the author has already discussed sales where possession (qabd) does not have a condition. Now he moves to sales where possession is required. Salam requires possession of the price (ra's al-mal) in the session; Sarf (currency exchange) requires possession of both. Thus Salam is treated first as the simpler case. The etymology of 'salam' is then discussed: it may be derived from 'aslama' meaning to deliver, with the hamza implying removal of safety, or from 'aslama' meaning to teach, because the price must be handed over. 'Salam' and 'salaf' are synonyms. The technical definition: a sale with immediate payment and deferred delivery. The pillar (rukn) is offer and acceptance. An example is given. The legal status: it is established by the Quran (verse of debt) and Sunnah (prophetic permission despite the general prohibition of selling what one does not possess). Although qiyas would reject it because it involves selling a non-existent thing, the texts override qiyas. This is a clear example of istihsan (juristic preference) based on revealed texts.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid immediately in the session and the commodity is delivered later
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital or price paid by the buyer (rabb al-salam) to the seller (muslam ilayh) at the time of contract
مسلم فيه (muslam fih): The commodity to be delivered in the future, subject to Salam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason Salam sale is considered permissible despite qiyas forbidding it?
A) Because qiyas is not applicable to sales.
B) Because the Quran and Sunnah specifically permit it, so qiyas is overridden.
C) Because the commodity is always available in the future.
D) Because both parties agree to it.

Key Takeaway
Salam sale is a contract permitted by divine texts despite contradicting qiyas, exemplifying the Hanafi principle of istihsan based on revealed evidence.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Salam in Makilat and Mawzunat: Exclusion of Dirhams and Dinars
Ruling on salam in makilat/mawzunat and dispute on dirhams/dinars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of salam in makilat and mawzunat, apply the hadith proof, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute when salam is attempted in dirhams and dinars.

Core Idea
Salam is valid in measured/weighed commodities but invalid in dirhams/dinars because they are prices, not goods.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical fiqh problem: the permissibility of salam (advance sale) in different types of property. While salam is generally valid in makilat (volume-measured) and mawzunat (weight-measured) items, dirhams and dinars are excluded. The reason is that they function as prices (athman) and cannot serve as the commodity (muslam fih). Additionally, the scholars differ on whether an invalid salam contract can be salvaged as a deferred sale. This lesson will guide you through the proof, the exception, and the preferred Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The passage states that salam is permissible (sahih) in makilat and mawzunat, but invalid (batil) in dirhams and dinars.
The ruling for dirhams/dinars is batil, not merely makruh.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever among you makes a salam, let him make salam in a known measure and known weight to a known term.' This establishes the permissibility for makilat/mawzunat.
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but it overrides analogical reasoning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyuslim' indicates permissibility (ibahah). The conditions 'known measure/weight' specify the type of commodity. Dirhams/dinars are excluded because they are athman (prices) and cannot be muslam fih.
The exclusion is derived from the nature of dirhams/dinars as thaman, not from the hadith text directly.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Isa b. Aban holds that the invalid salam is absolutely void (batil), while Abu Bakr al-A'mash holds that it becomes a deferred sale (bai' bi thamin mu'ajjal) to salvage the parties' intent.
This ikhtilaf arises because of the attempt to apply the principle that contracts are interpreted according to meanings and purposes.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the view of Isa b. Aban because validation must occur in the specific place where the contract was made, and it is impossible to convert salam into a deferred sale.
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the contract is batil.

باب السلم
اس دلیل سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ بیع سلم جائز نہ ہو۔ لیکن حدیث مذکور کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا گیا ہے۔ مکیلی موزونی چیزوں میں بیع السلم جائز ہے
قال وهو جائز في المكيلات والموزونات لقوله عليه السلام من اسلم منكم فليسلم في كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم والمراد بالموزونات غير الدراهم والدنانير لانهما اثمان والمسلم فيه لابد ان يكون مثمنا فلا يصح السلم فيهما ثم قيل يكون باطلا وقيل ينعقد بيعا بثمن مؤجل تحصيلا لمقصود المتعاقدين : بحسب الامكان والعبرة في القعود للمعانى والاول اصح لان التصحيح انما يجب في محل اوجبا العقد فيه ولا يمكن ذلك
ترجمہ شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ سلم مکیلات اور موزونات میں جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جوشخص تم میں سے سلم کا عقد کرے تو اس کو معلوم پیمانہ اور معلوم وزن میں معلوم میعاد تک سلم کرنی چاہئے۔ اور موزونات سے مراد درا ہم اور دنا نیر کے علاوہ ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں شمن ہیں اور مسلم فیہ کیلئے چونکہ مبیع ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اسلئے ان دونوں میں سلم صحیح نہ ہوگی ۔ پھر کہا گیا ہے کہ مسلم باطل ہوگی اور کہا گیا کہ ادھار ثمن کے عوض بیع منعقد ہو جائے گی تا کہ عقد کرنے والوں کا مقصود حتی الامکان حاصل ہو سکے۔ اور عقود میں معانی ہی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے۔ اور قول اول صحیح ہے۔کیونکہ عقد کو صحیح بنانا اس محل میں واجب ہوتا ہے جس میں دونوں نے عقد ٹھہرایا ہے حالانکہ یہ یہاں
ممکن نہیں ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ عقد سلم ہر کیلی اور وزنی چیز میں جائز ہے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے من اسلم منكم فليسلم في كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم إلى اجل معلوم يعنى جو شخص تم میں سے عقد سلم کرے تو وہ کیل معلوم اور وزن معلوم میں میعاد معلوم تک بیع سے بھی حاصل ہو جاتے ہیں۔ پس حتی الامکان عاقدین کے مقصود کو حاصل کرنے کیلئے شمن مؤجل کے عوض بیچ کا انعقاد مان لیا گیا۔ درانحالیکہ عقود میں معانی اور مقاصد ہی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے الفاظ کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قول اول یعنی عیسی بن ابان کا قول زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد کو صیح بنانا اسی محل میں واجب ہوتا ہے جس میں عاقدین نے عقد منعقد کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ بات یہاں ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عقد منعقد کیا گیا ہے دراہم اور دنا نیر میں اور دراہم و دنا نیر کبھی بھی بیچ نہیں ہو سکتے اور در اہم و دنا نیر میچ اسلئے نہیں ہو سکتے کہ یہ دونوں پیدائشی طور پرشن ہیں اور مسلم فی بیج ہوتی ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ عاقدین نے دراہم اور دنا نیر کو مسلم فیہ بنایا ہے حالانکہ در اہم ودنا نیر مسلم فیہ نہیں ہو سکتے اسلئے یہ عقد سلم نہیں ہوگا اور چونکہ عقد سلم کو بدل کر شمن موجل کے عوض بیچ کر دینا بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے یہ بیچ بھی منعقد نہ ہوگی ۔ پس جب دونوں صورتیں ناممکن ہیں تو در اہم اور دنا نیر میں بیع سلم کرنا بالکل باطل ہو گا۔
Chapter of Salam. This proof indicates that Salam sale is not permissible. But due to the mentioned hadith, analogy is abandoned. Salam sale is permissible in measured and weighed items. He said: It is permissible in makilat (measured by volume) and mawzunat (weighed) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever among you makes a salam, let him make salam in a known measure and known weight to a known term.' And by mawzunat is meant other than dirhams and dinars because they are prices (thaman), and the muslam fih must be a commodity (muthman), so salam is not valid in them. Then it is said: [salam] is void, and it is said: it becomes a sale with deferred price to achieve the purpose of the contracting parties as much as possible, and consideration is given to meanings in contracts. The first opinion is more correct because validation is only required in the place where the contract is concluded, and that is not possible here. Translation: Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that salam is permissible in makilat and mawzunat. Because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: The person among you who makes a salam contract should make salam in a known measure and known weight for a known term. And by mawzunat is meant other than dirhams and dinars because they are both prices, and muslam fih must be a commodity, so salam is not valid in them. Then it is said: the salam is void, and it is said: it becomes a sale with deferred price so that the purpose of the contracting parties is achieved as much as possible. And in contracts, meanings are considered. The first opinion is correct because the validation is obligatory in the place where both concluded the contract, and that is not possible here. Explanation: The author al-Quduri says the salam contract is permissible in every measured and weighed item. The evidence is that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever among you makes a salam contract, then let him make salam in a known measure and known weight to a known term.' This hadith shows that the salam contract is permissible in makilat and mawzunat. The author of al-Hidayah says that in the text, by mawzunat is meant other than dirhams and dinars. Therefore, if salam is made in dirhams and dinars, despite being weighed, the salam contract is void. There are two scenarios: first, salam is made in dirhams and dinars themselves, i.e., both the capital and the muslam fih are dirhams or dinars; this is unanimously impermissible because if both are dirhams or both are dinars, there is delay (nasa') with same genus and kind; if one is dirhams and the other dinars, there is delay with unity of value. Both involve riba al-nasi'ah which is prohibited. Second, wheat is made as capital and dirhams/dinars as muslam fih; this is also impermissible because the muslam fih must be something that can be sold and becomes specified by specification, but dirhams and dinars are prices and do not become specified by specification. So making them muslam fih is invalid. Now the question: when the salam in wheat for dirhams/dinars is invalid, does it become a sale of wheat for deferred price? Isa b. Aban says it is absolutely void, neither salam nor sale. Abu Bakr al-A'mash says it becomes a sale of wheat for deferred price because the parties' purposes are achieved. The author of al-Hidayah says the first view is more correct because validation is in that place only, and it's not possible.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of salam (advance sale) in makilat and mawzunat, and the exception of dirhams and dinars. The author begins by noting that qiyas (analogy) would not permit salam, but a specific hadith overrides that. The hadith requires a known measure, weight, and term, establishing permissibility for makilat and mawzunat. The term 'mawzunat' here excludes dirhams and dinars because they function as prices (thaman), not commodities (muthman). In salam, the muslam fih must be a commodity, so salam in dirhams/dinars is invalid. The text then presents two views on what happens if such an invalid salam is attempted: (1) it is absolutely void (bati), (2) it is converted into a regular sale with deferred price (bai' bi thamin mu'ajjal) to salvage the parties' intent. The first view, attributed to Isa b. Aban and preferred by the author of al-Hidayah, is correct because the contract was concluded specifically as salam, not as a regular sale, and validation must be in the place where the contract was made. The second view (Abu Bakr al-A'mash) considers the parties' underlying purposes. The commentary then details two scenarios: (a) salam in dirhams/dinars themselves (both capital and muslam fih are dirhams/dinars) – invalid due to riba al-nasi'ah; (b) wheat as capital and dirhams/dinars as muslam fih – invalid because dirhams/dinars are not fit to be muslam fih. The preferred position is that the contract is entirely void.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later; also called bai' al-salam.
مكيلات (makilat): Items measured by volume (e.g., grains).
موزونات (mawzunat): Items measured by weight, excluding dirhams and dinars.
ثمن (thaman): Price; a medium of exchange like dirhams and dinars.
مثمن (muthman): Commodity; something sold for a price.
نساء (nasa'): Deferment; delay in exchange, often leading to riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam in dirhams and dinars invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they are not measured or weighed.
B) Because they are prices (thaman) and cannot be muslam fih, which must be a commodity (muthman).
C) Because the hadith explicitly prohibits it.
D) Because there is consensus on its prohibition.

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid only in commodities (muthman), not in prices (thaman); an invalid salam is not salvaged as a deferred sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Salam in Mazru'at and Ma'dudat: Eggs, Pomegranates, and Fulus
Extending salam to land-measured and counted items with exceptions for variable items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on salam in mazru'at and ma'dudat mutaqarib, and identify the exceptions for highly variable items (tafawut fahish) and the dispute over fulus.

Core Idea
Salam is valid in measured and non-variable counted items, but invalid in highly variable ones and in fulus according to Imam Muhammad.

Salam is a forward sale where the price is paid upfront and goods are delivered later. The Hanafi school extends it beyond weights and measures to land-measured (mazru'at) and counted items (ma'dudat), provided the units are similar in value. This lesson explores the conditions and exceptions, including the famous dispute over copper coins (fulus).

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Salam is permissible in mazru'at (items measured by length) and ma'dudat mutaqarib (counted items with non-variable units) because ignorance (jahalah) can be removed by specifying dimensions, description, and count.
The key condition is the ability to determine the subject matter precisely.
2
Examine the exception for highly variable items
Items like watermelon and pomegranate have tafawut fahish (great disparity) in unit value, making salam invalid due to gharar. Ostrich eggs are also excluded per Abu Hanifa because of variable value.
Custom ('urf) plays a role: minor differences are ignored for non-variable items.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on fulus
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow salam in fulus by count because they treat them as commodities by convention. Imam Muhammad disallows it because fulus are prices (athman).
The mufta bihi position follows Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as stated in the text ('gila').
4
Identify the proof and reasoning
The ruling is based on rational reasoning (dalil aqli): salam is valid when gharar is removed through specification. The text cites no specific hadith but relies on the principle of determinability.
The proof is zanni al-dalala but accepted in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the ruling anatomy
Conditions for valid salam include the subject being a commodity (not thaman), immediate payment, and exact specification. The contract is sahih if conditions are met, batil otherwise.
Zufar's view on measuring eggs by weight is also discussed: Abu Hanifa allows it, Zufar does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزروعی اور عددی متقارب میں بیع السلم جائز ہے
قال وكذا فى المذروعات لانه يمكن ضبطها بذكر الذرع والصفة و الصنعة ولا بد منها لترتفع الجهالة فيتحقق شرط صحة السلم وكذا فى المعدودات التى لاتتفاوت كالجوز والبيض لأن العددى المتقارب معلوم مضبوط الوصف مقدور التسليم فيجوز السلم فيه والصغير والكبير سواء باصطلاح الناس على اهدار التفاوت بخلاف البطيخ والرمان لانه يتفاوت أحاده تفاوتا فاحشاً وبتفاوت الاحاد في المالية يعرف العددى المتفاوت وعن ابي حنيفة انه لا يجوز فى بيض النعامة لانه يتفاوت احاده في المالية ثم كما يجوز السلم فيها عددا يجوز كيلا وقال زفر لا يجوز كيلا لانه عددى وليس بمكيل وعنه أنه لا يجوز عددًا ايضا للتفاوت ولنا ان المقدار مرة يعرف بالعدد وتارة بالكيل وانما صار معدودا بالاصطلاح فيصير مكيلا باصطلاحهما وكذا فى الفلوس عددا وقيل هذا عند ابي حنيفة وابى يوسف وعند محمد لايجوز لانها اثمان ولهما ان الثمنية في حقهما باصطلاحهما فيبطل باصطلاحهما ولا تعود وزنياً وقد ذكرناه من قبل
ترجمہ اور یوں ہی گزوں سے ناپنے کی چیزوں میں مسلم جائز ہے کیونکہ ان چیزوں کا ضبط میں لانا ناپ صفت اور صنعت ذکر کر کے ممکن ہے اور ان باتوں کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ جہالت دور ہو کر صحت سلم کی شرط متحقق ہو جائے اور اسی طرح گنتی کی ایسی چیزوں میں ہوں (سلم جائز ہے ) جس میں تفاوت نہیں ہوتا جیسے ، اخروٹ، انڈے۔ کیونکہ عددی متقارب کی مقدار معلوم ہے اور ان کا وصف بھی (بیان
Salam is permissible in land-measured (mazru'at) and counted items (ma'dudat) that are not highly variable. He said: Likewise in mazru'at because they can be controlled by mentioning the measure, description, and workmanship, and these are necessary to remove ignorance so that the condition for validity of salam is fulfilled. Likewise in counted items that do not vary, like walnuts and eggs, because the non-variable counted is known, description is controlled, delivery is possible, so salam is permissible. The small and the big are equal by people's custom disregarding the difference. Unlike watermelon and pomegranate because their individual units vary greatly, and by variation in value, the variable counted is known. From Abu Hanifa: it is not permissible in ostrich eggs because their units vary in value. Then, just as salam is permissible in them by count, it is permissible by measure. Zufar said: it is not permissible by measure because it is a counted item, not a measured one. From him: it is also not permissible by count due to variation. Our proof: quantity is sometimes known by count and sometimes by measure; it became counted by custom, so it becomes measured by their convention. Likewise in copper coins (fulus) by count. It is said this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad it is not permissible because they are prices (athman). For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): the quality of being a price in their context is by their convention, so it is invalidated by their convention and does not revert to being weighed. We have mentioned this before.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe, extending the permissibility of salam from makilat/mawzunat to mazru'at (items measured by length, like land or cloth) and ma'dudat (counted items) that are mutaqarib (non-variable). The reasoning for mazru'at is that ignorance can be removed by specifying dimensions, description, and workmanship. For counted items that do not vary significantly in value per unit (like walnuts, eggs), salam is valid because each unit is similar; people's custom ignores minor differences. In contrast, items like watermelon and pomegranate have high variability, so salam is invalid. A specific issue arises with ostrich eggs: Abu Hanifa rules that salam is invalid because individual eggs vary in value. The text also discusses salam in fulus (copper coins) by count: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow it because fulus are treated as commodities by convention, not as prices; however, Muhammad al-Shaybani disallows it because fulus are essentially prices (athman). The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the price nature of fulus can be negated by convention, so they become counted commodities.

Key Terms
مذروعات (mazru'at): Items measured by length/area (e.g., land, cloth) by cubits.
معدودات متقارب (ma'dudat mutaqarib): Counted items where individual units are similar in value and size.
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as money or commodity.
تفاوت فاحش (tafawut fahish): Great disparity; the condition that renders salam invalid in counted items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they are not measured by weight.
B) Because they are highly variable in value (tafawut fahish).
C) Because there is a hadith prohibiting it.
D) Because they are eaten raw.

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid in mazru'at and ma'dudat mutaqarib when properly specified, but invalid in highly variable items due to gharar; fulus are valid by count per the majority Hanafi view.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Dispute on Converting Invalid Salam into a Sale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalid salam salvaging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the views of Isa ibn Aban and Abu Bakr al-A'mash on invalid salam and apply the Hanafi tarjih mechanism to prefer the absolutely void position.

Core Idea
An invalid salam contract cannot be re-interpreted as a sale; it is absolutely void.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a salam contract fails because dirhams/dinars cannot be subject matter, can it be saved as a sale? Two later scholars differ, and the author of al-Hidayah settles the issue by preferring the view that the contract is absolutely void, as it must be validated in its original form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalid salam scenario
The scenario: a person attempts a salam contract where the subject matter (muslim fīh) is dirhams or dinars, which is invalid because they are price, not a commodity. The contract is void as a salam.
2
State the two positions
Isa ibn Aban holds the contract is absolutely void—it cannot become a valid salam nor a valid sale. Abu Bakr al-A'mash argues it becomes a valid sale with deferred price because the parties' objectives can be met.
These are later Hanafi scholars, not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Examine the reasoning for each
Isa: the contract must be validated in the form in which it was made; you cannot force a salam into a sale. Dirhams/dinars are pure prices and cannot be sold (as a commodity) in a deferred sale either. Abu Bakr: contracts are interpreted according to intent; the objectives (wheat for payment) can be achieved through a sale.
4
Understand the tarjih by al-Hidayah
The author of al-Hidayah prefers Isa ibn Aban's view, stating it is 'more correct' because the contract must be validated in its own context, which is impossible here. This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the preferred view, neither party has any obligation—the contract is void. Under the opposing view, a valid sale with deferred price would be enforceable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب ان کو مسلم فیہ بنانا درست نہیں ہے تو ان کے اندر عقد مسلم بھی درست نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن اب سوال یہ ہے کہ جب گندم کا عقد سلم در اہم اور د ائیر میں درست نہ ہوا تو کیا من مؤجل کے عوض گندم کے اندربیع منعقد ہو جائے گی یا نہیں یعنی کیا یہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ گندم کو بیع قرار دے دیا جائے اور دراہم اور دنا نیر کو ادھار ثمن قرار دے دیا جائے اور یہ کہا جائے کہ یہ ادھار شمن کے عوض گندم کی بیج ہے۔ اس بارے میں عیسی بن ابان کا قول یہ ہے کہ یہ بیج بالکل باطل ہے یعنی یہ نہ عقد سلم ہو گا اور نہ ثمن مؤجل کے عوض گندم کی بیع ہوگی۔ اور ابو بکر اعمش کا قول یہ ہوگا ہے کہ یہ ثمن مؤجل کے عوض گندم کی بیع ہے یعنی اگر اس کو بیع سلم قرار دینا ممکن نہیں ہے تو یہ کہ دیا جائے گا کہ یہ ثمن مؤجل کے عوض گندم کی بیچ ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عاقدین میں سے ایک کا مقصود گندم پر قبضہ کرنا ہے۔ اور ایک کا مقصود دراہم اور دنا نیر پر قبضہ کرنا ہے اور یہ مقاصد بیع سلم کے بغیر ثمن مؤجل کے عوض انعقاد بیع سے بھی حاصل ہو جاتے ہیں۔ پس حتی الامکان عاقدین کے مقصود کو حاصل کرنے کیلئے شمن مؤجل کے عوض بیچ کا انعقاد مان لیا گیا۔ درانحالیکہ عقود میں معانی اور مقاصد ہی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے الفاظ کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قول اول یعنی عیسی بن ابان کا قول زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد کو صیح بنانا اسی محل میں واجب ہوتا ہے جس میں عاقدین نے عقد منعقد کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ بات یہاں ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عقد منعقد کیا گیا ہے دراہم اور دنا نیر میں اور دراہم و دنا نیر کبھی بھی بیچ نہیں ہو سکتے اور در اہم و دنا نیر میچ اسلئے نہیں ہو سکتے کہ یہ دونوں پیدائشی طور پرشن ہیں اور مسلم فی بیج ہوتی ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ عاقدین نے دراہم اور دنا نیر کو مسلم فیہ بنایا ہے حالانکہ در اہم ودنا نیر مسلم فیہ نہیں ہو سکتے اسلئے یہ عقد سلم نہیں ہوگا اور چونکہ عقد سلم کو بدل کرشن موجل کے عوض بیچ کر دینا بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے یہ بیچ بھی منعقد نہ ہوگی ۔ پس جب دونوں صورتیں ناممکن ہیں تو درا ہم اور دنا نیر میں بیع سلم کرنا بالکل باطل ہو گا۔
When it is not valid to make them (dirhams and dinars) the subject matter, then the salam contract within them is also not valid. But now the question is: when the salam contract for wheat in dirhams and dinars is not valid, then will a sale be contracted for wheat in exchange for deferred price or not? That is, can it be that wheat is considered the sold commodity and the dirhams and dinars are considered the deferred price, and it is said that this is a sale of wheat for a deferred price? Regarding this, the saying of Isa ibn Aban is that this sale is absolutely void, meaning it is neither a salam contract nor a sale of wheat for a deferred price. And the saying of Abu Bakr al-A'mash is that this is a sale of wheat for a deferred price, meaning if it is not possible to consider it a salam sale, then it will be said that this is a sale of wheat for a deferred price. And the reason is that one of the contracting parties aims to take possession of wheat, and the other aims to take possession of dirhams and dinars, and these objectives are achieved by a sale with deferred price even without a salam contract. Therefore, as far as possible, to achieve the objective of the contracting parties, the contract was considered a sale with deferred price, given that in contracts, meanings and objectives are considered, not words. The author of al-Hidayah states: The first opinion, that of Isa ibn Aban, is more correct. Because it is necessary to validate the contract in the very context in which the contracting parties entered into the contract, which is not possible here. Because the contract was entered into regarding dirhams and dinars, and dirhams and dinars can never be sold commodities, and dirhams and dinars cannot be sold because they are intrinsically price and the subject matter of salam is a commodity. The conclusion is that the contracting parties made dirhams and dinars the subject matter of salam, whereas dirhams and dinars cannot be the subject matter of salam, so this contract is not a salam. And since it is not permissible to replace the salam contract and make it a sale for a deferred price, therefore this sale will also not be contracted. So when both forms are impossible, then making a salam contract in dirhams and dinars is absolutely void.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the fate of an invalid salam contract. The issue: a person attempts a salam contract where the subject matter (muslim fīh) is dirhams or dinars, which is invalid because they are not commodities. The question is whether this can be reinterpreted as a valid sale (bay') with a deferred price. Two opinions are reported: Isa ibn Aban holds that the contract is absolutely void—it cannot become a valid salam nor a valid sale. Abu Bakr al-A'mash argues that it becomes a valid sale with deferred price, because the objectives of the parties can still be met, and contracts are interpreted according to intent. The author of al-Hidayah (صاحب ہدایہ) prefers Isa ibn Aban's view, reasoning that a contract must be validated in the very form it was made; you cannot force a salam into a sale. Since dirhams/dinars are pure prices, they cannot be sold (as a commodity) in a deferred sale either. Hence the contract is entirely void.

Key Terms
مسلم فیہ (muslim fīh): The subject matter of a salam contract, which must be a commodity (not price).
شمن مؤجل (thaman mu'ajjal): Deferred price in a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute about converting an invalid salam contract into a sale, which view does the author of al-Hidayah prefer?
A) Abu Bakr al-A'mash's view that it becomes a sale with deferred price.
B) Isa ibn Aban's view that the contract is absolutely void.
C) Both views are equally valid.
D) The contract becomes valid as a salam.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an invalid salam contract cannot be transformed into a sale; it is absolutely void.

Salam in Measured and Countable Items: Conditions, Custom, and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Ruling on salam in measured and countable items with conditions and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid salam in maddroot items, apply the custom-based criterion to classify countable items as valid or invalid for salam, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in fulus.

Core Idea
Salam is valid when quantity, description, and workmanship are specified; custom determines if variation is negligible.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes the permissibility of salam in items measured by the cord (maddroot) and in countable items that are similar in value. The key is that uncertainty (jahalah) must be removed by specifying the key attributes. We also encounter important intra-Hanafi disagreements: Zufar restricts salam to count only, and Muhammad al-Shaybani prohibits salam in fulus entirely. This lesson will walk you through the conditions, the role of custom, and the reasoning behind these disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
Recognize that the passage covers two types of items: maddroot (items sold by linear measure) and adadi mutaqarib (countable items with negligible variation).
Maddroot include cloth, land, etc.; adadi mutaqarib include eggs, walnuts, etc.
2
Extract the conditions for validity
For maddroot, three things must be specified: measure (quantity), description (quality), and workmanship (craftsmanship). For countable items, quantity and description must be known, and custom must disregard minor variation.
These conditions remove uncertainty (jahalah), which invalidates the contract.
3
Apply the custom-based criterion
The passage contrasts items like eggs (valid) with watermelon (invalid) based on degree of individual variation. Determine if custom disregards the variation.
Ostrich eggs are invalid because variation affects value.
4
Analyze the dispute on measurement method
Zufar argues salam in adadi mutaqarib is only valid by count, not by weight. The Hanafi position is that it can be by weight too, because quantity can be determined by either method.
The key is that the items became countable by convention, so they can become weightable by agreement.
5
Examine the fulus dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit salam in fulus by count, while Muhammad prohibits it. The reasoning: fulus have become prices by convention, but that convention can be changed.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the relied-upon position is that of the Shaykhayn.

Salam is permissible in measured (by cord) and similar countable items. He (al-Quduri/al-Hidayah) said: Likewise, in items measured by the cord (maddroot), because it is possible to specify them by mentioning the measure (dhira'), description (sifah), and workmanship (sin'ah), and these are necessary to remove uncertainty, so the condition for validity of salam is fulfilled. Likewise, in countable items that do not vary, such as walnuts and eggs, because the similar countable is known, its description is specified, and delivery is possible, so salam in it is permissible. The small and the large are equal due to people's custom of disregarding variation. Unlike watermelon and pomegranate, because their individual units vary greatly, and by the variation of individual units in value, the countable item is known to be varied. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that salam in ostrich eggs is not permissible because their individuals vary in value. Then, just as salam in these items is permissible by count, it is permissible by weight as well. Zufar said: It is not permissible by weight because it is countable, not weightable. And from him (a narration) that it is not permissible by count either due to variation. Our proof: Quantity is sometimes known by count and sometimes by weight. It became countable by convention, so it becomes weightable by their convention. Likewise, in fulus (copper coins) by count; and it is said this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, it is not permissible because they are prices. Their (Shaykhayn) proof: The attribute of being price for them is due to their convention; thus it is nullified by their convention, and they do not revert to being weightable. We have mentioned this before. Translation: And similarly, salam is permissible in items measured by cords because it is possible to specify them by mentioning measure, description, and workmanship, and these are necessary to remove ignorance so that the condition of validity of salam is fulfilled. Similarly, in countable items that do not have variation, such as walnuts and eggs, because the quantity of similar countable items is known and their description is also specified, and delivery is possible, so salam in them is permissible. Due to people's agreement to disregard variation, their small and large are equal. Unlike watermelon and pomegranate, because their individuals have great variation, and due to variation in value, the countable item becomes known as varied. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that salam in ostrich eggs is not permissible because their individuals vary in value. Then, just as salam in similar countable items is permissible by count, similarly it is permissible by weight. Imam Zufar said that it is not permissible by weight because this item is countable, not weightable. And from Zufar there is a narration that it is not permissible by count either due to variation. Our proof: Quantity is sometimes known by count and sometimes by weight, and it has become countable by convention; thus it will become weightable by the convention of the parties. Similarly, salam in fulus is permissible by count, and it is said that this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and according to Imam Muhammad it is not permissible because fulus are prices. The proof of the two shaykhs is that fulus were prices by their convention; thus their being prices becomes void by their convention, and they do not revert to being weightable. We have mentioned this before. Explanation: Al-Quduri states: Just as salam is permissible in measurable and weightable items, similarly salam is permissible in items that are sold by measurement with cords. The proof: For a salam contract to be valid, three things must be known: quantity, description, and workmanship. These need to be known so that ignorance of the subject matter is removed and the condition for validity of salam is fulfilled. In maddroot items, these three become known: quantity by specifying length and width, description by specifying its quality (e.g., good or medium), and workmanship by specifying whether it is fine or coarse. So when these three can be known, i.e., can be specified, then salam in maddroot is permissible. The author of al-Hidayah states: Items that are sold by count and whose individual units do not vary in value—such as walnuts and eggs—salam in them is permissible because such countable items that are similar have known quantity and description is specified, and delivery is possible. Those items whose quantity is known and description specified and delivery possible, salam in them is valid. Therefore, salam in similar countable items is valid. In countable items, small and large are equal because people have agreed not to consider variation. For example, eggs of chickens have slight variation among themselves, but people by consensus do not consider that variation, so it does not happen that if an egg is slightly larger, its price is higher, and if...
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of salam in two categories: items measured by cord (ذرع) and similar countable items (عددی متقارب). The key condition for validity is the removal of uncertainty (جهالة) regarding the subject matter. For maddroot, this is achieved by specifying length, quality, and workmanship. For countable items, the items must be sufficiently similar in value that variation is disregarded by custom (like walnuts and eggs), unlike watermelon or pomegranate where variation is significant. The passage also includes a narration from Abu Hanifa that ostrich eggs are excluded because of value variation. Additionally, it addresses the method of measurement: salam in countable similar items is valid by count and also by weight, contrary to Zufar who restricts it to count. The dispute over fulus (copper coins) is also noted: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit salam in fulus by count, while Muhammad prohibits it because fulus are essentially prices. The reasoning involves the role of local convention (اصطلاح) in determining the nature of items.

Key Terms
مذروعات (maddroot): Items sold by linear measurement (by the cord/ذراع).
عددی متقارب (adadi mutaqarib): Countable items whose individual units are similar enough in value that small variations are disregarded by custom.
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins, treated as a type of money (price) or commodity depending on convention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because eggs are always sold by weight.
B) Because people customarily disregard the variation.
C) Because eggs are measured by the cord.
D) Because Imam Abu Hanifa specifically allowed it.

Key Takeaway
Salam in maddroot and adadi mutaqarib is valid when quantity, description, and workmanship are specified, and custom determines whether variation in countable items is acceptable; the intra-Hanafi dispute on fulus illustrates the role of convention in legal rulings.

Conditions for Salam: Knowledge of Quantity, Description, and Workmanship
Commentary on conditions for valid salam in measured items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three required conditions for a valid salam contract and apply them to items sold by linear measure.

Core Idea
Salam is valid only when quantity, description, and workmanship of the subject matter are fully known.

The salam contract allows the sale of goods to be delivered in the future, but it requires special care to avoid uncertainty. In this passage, Sahib al-Quduri explains that the validity of salam depends on knowing three key aspects of the subject matter. We will examine these conditions and see how they apply to items sold by length, such as cloth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The rule is that salam is permissible in makilat (measured by volume), mawzunat (weight), and mazru'at (length).
This expands the scope beyond weight and volume.
2
List the three conditions
The three conditions are: quantity (miqdar), description (sifah), and workmanship (sana'ah). These must be known to remove ignorance (jahalah).
These are the core requirements for the subject matter.
3
Understand the rationale
Ignorance about the subject matter invalidates the contract due to gharar (uncertainty). Knowing these three aspects eliminates that ignorance.
The proof is talili (teleological reasoning).
4
Apply to mazru'at
For items sold by length, quantity is known by specifying dimensions (length and width), description by quality (e.g., good or bad), and workmanship by texture (fine or coarse).
This shows how conditions are practically fulfilled.
5
Note the expansion
The proof demonstrates why salam is not limited to makilat and mawzunat; it covers any item whose subject matter can be precisely known through these three parameters.
This is an expansion of the original ruling.

اور ان تین چیزوں کا معلوم ہونا اس لئے ضروری ہے تا کہ مسلم فیہ کی جہالت دور ہو کر صحت سلم کی شرط تحقیق ہو جائے اور مذروعات میں یہ تینوں چیزیں معلوم ہو جاتی ہیں۔ اس طور پر کہ اس کا طول و عرض بیان کرنے سے مقدار معلوم ہو جائے گی۔ اور جید یا ردی ہونا بیان کرنے سے صفت معلوم ہو جائے گی۔ اور باریک یا موٹا ہونا بیان کرنے سے صنعت (کاریگری) معلوم ہو جائے گی۔ پس جب مذکورہ تینوں چیزیں معلوم ہو سکتی ہیں یعنی ان کو ضبط میں لانا ممکن ہے تو مزروعات کی بیع سلم بھی جائز ہے۔
Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri states that the salam contract is permissible in things sold by measure (makilat) and by weight (mawzunat), and similarly it is permissible in things that are sold by measuring with yards (gaz). The proof is that for the salam contract to be valid, three things must be known: 1. Quantity, 2. Description, 3. Workmanship. Knowing these three is necessary so that ignorance of the subject matter (muslam fihi) is removed and the condition for the validity of salam is fulfilled. In crops (mazru'at), these three are known: quantity is known by specifying length and width, description by specifying good or bad, and workmanship by specifying fine or coarse. Since these three can be known, i.e., it is possible to specify them, salam in crops is permissible.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for a valid salam contract. The author, Sahib al-Quduri, states that salam is not limited to items sold by weight or volume; it is also valid for items sold by linear measure (like cloth). The key requirement is that the subject matter (muslam fihi) must be known in three aspects: quantity (miqdar), description (sifah), and workmanship (sana'ah). This ensures that the parties are not ignorant of what is being sold, which would otherwise invalidate the contract. For crops, quantity is determined by specifying dimensions, description by quality (good or bad), and workmanship by texture (fine or coarse). Since these can be specified, salam in crops is valid.

Key Terms
مکیلات (makilat): Things sold by measure (volume).
موزونات (mawzunat): Things sold by weight.
مذروعات (mazru'at): Things sold by length (like cloth).
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The subject matter in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Salam in Counted Items: Homogeneous vs Heterogeneous
Ruling on salam in counted items based on price uniformity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing homogeneous from heterogeneous counted items for salam contracts.

Core Idea
Salam in counted items is valid only when items are uniform in price by custom.

This lesson examines a key ruling from al-Hidayah on salam (advance purchase) in items sold by count. The central distinction is whether the items are homogeneous (mutaqarib) or heterogeneous (mutafawit) in price. Homogeneous items like chicken eggs are considered equal despite minor size variations, making salam valid. Heterogeneous items like melons vary significantly, causing uncertainty and invalidating salam. We also explore an intra-Hanafi narration on ostrich eggs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is salam (advance payment for future delivery). The ruling depends on whether the counted items are homogeneous or heterogeneous in price.
Salam is a sale of specified future goods.
2
Locate the criterion
The criterion is price uniformity based on custom ('urf). If people treat items as equal in price despite minor differences, they are mutaqarib. If significant price differences are recognized, they are mutafawit.
Custom is a source of law in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the criterion to examples
Chicken eggs are mutaqarib because minor size differences do not affect price. Melons are mutafawit because one melon may cost double another.
Apply to the examples given in the text.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration that ostrich eggs are mutafawit, making salam invalid. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) treats them as mutaqarib.
The difference arises from varying customs regarding ostrich eggs.
5
Derive the practical rule
For salam in counted items, always assess whether the items are considered uniform in price by local custom. If yes, salam is valid; if no, it is invalid.
Custom can vary by time and place.

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جن چیزوں کو گن کر فروخت کیا جاتا ہے اور ان کے افراد میں مالیت کے اعتبار سے تفاوت نہیں ہوتا جیسے اخروٹ اور انڈے ان کی بیع سلم بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ ایسی عددی چیزیں جو باہم قریب قریب ہوتی ہیں ان کی مقدار بھی معلوم ہے۔ اور بیان سے ان کا وصف بھی منضبط ہو جاتا ہے اور ان کو سپرد کرنا بھی ممکن ہے اور جن چیزوں کی مقدار معلوم ہو اور ان کا وصف منضبط ہو جاتا ہو اور ان کا سپرد کرنا ناممکن ہو ان کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے عددی متقاربہ کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ عددی چیزوں میں چھوٹا، بڑا برابر ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ان کے درمیان تفاوت کا اعتبار نہ کرنے پر لوگوں نے اتفاق کر لیا ہے۔ مثلاً : مرغی کے انڈوں میں اگر چہ خفیف سا تفاوت ہوتا ہے لیکن لوگ بالاتفاق اس تفاوت کا اعتبار نہیں کرتے چنانچہ ایسا نہیں ہوتا کہ مرغی کا انڈا اگر کچھ بڑا ہو تو اس کی قیمت زیادہ ہو اور اگر کچھ چھوٹا ہو تو اس کی قیمت کم ہو بلکہ قیمت کے اعتبار سے سب برابر ہوتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خربوزے اور انار کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح کدو، لوکی، جانوروں کے سر اور پاؤں کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قیمت کے اعتبار سے ان کے افراد میں بہت بڑا تفاوت ہوتا ہے اور لوگ ان کے درمیان تفاوت کا اعتبار بھی کرتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ ایک خربوزہ ایک روپیہ کا ہوتا ہے اور دوسرا دو روپیہ کا ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ایک انار کم قیمت پر ملتا ہے اور دوسرا اس سے زیادہ قیمت پر ملتا ہے اور قیمت کے اعتبار سے جن چیزوں کے افراد میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے خربوزے اور انار وغیرہ اشیاء کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اب عددی متقارب اور عددی متفاوت کے درمیان ضابطہ یہ ہوا کہ اگر عددی چیز کے افراد میں قیمت کے اعتبار سے تفاوت ہوا تو وہ چیز عددی متفاوت کہلائے گی اور اگر تفاوت نہ ہو تو وہ عددی متقارب کہلائے گی۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ شتر مرغ کے انڈوں کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شتر مرغ کے انڈے مالیت کے اعتبار سے متفاوت ہوتے ہیں اور سابق میں گزر چکا ہے کہ عددی متفاوت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے شتر مرغ کے انڈوں کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Sahib al-Hidayah states: Salam is permissible for things that are sold by count and whose individuals do not differ in value, such as walnuts and eggs, because such counted items that are close to one another have their quantity known, and their description can be specified, and it is possible to deliver them. If the quantity is known, description is specified, and delivery is possible, salam is valid. Therefore salam in homogeneous counted items is valid. In counted items, a small and a large are considered equal because people have agreed not to consider the difference. For example, in chicken eggs, although there is a slight difference, people do not consider that difference; a slightly bigger egg is not priced higher, and a slightly smaller one is not priced lower; all are equal in price. Sahib al-Hidayah states that salam is not permissible for melons and pomegranates, and similarly for pumpkins, gourds, animal heads and feet, because among their individuals there is a great difference in value, and people do consider that difference. Thus we see one melon for one rupee and another for two rupees, similarly pomegranates vary in price. Therefore salam is not valid for such items. The rule is: if the individuals of a counted item differ in value, it is called 'mutafawit' (heterogeneous); if they do not differ, it is 'mutaqarib' (homogeneous). There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that salam in ostrich eggs is not valid because they differ in value, as previously established that salam in heterogeneous counted items is not valid.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and reasoning for salam in counted items. The key distinction is whether the items are homogeneous (mutaqarib) or heterogeneous (mutafawit) in price. Homogeneous items like chicken eggs are considered equal despite minor size differences, based on custom ('urf). Heterogeneous items like melons vary significantly in price, so salam is invalid due to uncertainty. Ostrich eggs fall into the latter category according to one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
عددی متقارب (adadi mutaqarib): Counted items whose individuals are close in value, considered homogeneous.
عددی متفاوت (adadi mutafawit): Counted items whose individuals differ significantly in value, considered heterogeneous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam in melons invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) They are not counted.
B) Their individuals vary greatly in price.
C) They cannot be delivered.
D) They spoil quickly.

Key Takeaway
Salam in counted items is valid only when the items are homogeneous in price based on custom; heterogeneity invalidates the contract due to uncertainty.
