Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Selling Homogeneous Counted Items by Measure and Fulus
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam by measure for counted items and fulus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school allows salam by measure for homogeneous counted items and differentiate the positions of Imam Zufar and Imam Muhammad on fulus.

Core Idea
Homogeneous counted items can be sold by measure if parties agree; classification is based on custom, not revelation.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether homogeneous counted items (like eggs) can be sold by measure in a salam contract. It also touches on a separate dispute about fulus (copper coins). Understanding this shows how Hanafi fiqh uses custom ('urf) and mutual agreement to determine contractual methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and disputed ruling
Recognize that the issue is the permissibility of salam (forward sale) for homogeneous counted items (ma'dudat mutaqariba) by measure (kayl) rather than by count.
2
State Imam Zufar's position
Imam Zufar holds that salam by measure is invalid because these items are originally counted, not measured. In one narration, he also invalidates salam by count due to slight individual differences.
He provides two narrations: one prohibiting measure only, another prohibiting both.
3
Explain the Hanafi proof
Quantity can be determined by either count or measure. The classification as 'counted' is not divinely ordained but based on people's agreement ('urf). Therefore, parties can agree to treat them as measured.
This is a qiyas khafi analogy: just as 'urf makes an item counted, agreement makes it measured.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the original classification is flexible. Since 'urf is changeable, parties can stipulate measure, making the contract valid by their mutual consent.
5
Note the fulus dispute
The passage also records that Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permit salam in fulus by count, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it, considering fulus as thaman subject to riba.
The relied-upon position follows Shaykhayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ معدودات متقاربہ کی بیع سلم جس طرح شمار کر کے جائز ہے اسی طرح کیل کر کے بھی جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایک روپیہ کے ایک فقیر انڈوں کی بیع سلم کی گئی تو جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ معدودات متقاربہ میں شمار کر کے بیع سلم کرنا تو جائز ہے لیکن کیل کر کے جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ معدودات متقاربہ کے قبیلہ سے جو چیزیں ہیں وہ سب عددی ہیں کیلی نہیں ہیں۔ اور جو چیزیں کیلی نہ ہوں ان کی بیع سلم، کیل کے ذریعہ کسی طرح درست ہو سکتی ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ معدودات متقاربہ کی بیع سلم، کیل کر کے ناجائز ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر کی ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ معدودات متقاربہ کی بیع سلم نہ کیل جائز ہے اور نہ عدداً جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ معدودات متقاربہ کے افراد کے درمیان تفاوت ہوتا ہے اگر تفاوت خفیف ہے اور وہ عددی چیز جس کے افراد میں تفاوت ہو اس کی بیع سلم چونکہ عدداً (شمار کر کے) بھی جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے معدودات متقاربہ کی بیع سلم عدداً بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقدار کبھی تو شمار کرنے سے پہچانی جاتی ہے اور کبھی کیل کے ذریعہ معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ پس معدودات متقاربہ کا شمار اور کیل دونوں سے ضبط کرنا ممکن ہے اور جب دونوں سے ضبط کرنا ممکن ہے تو دونوں کے ساتھ بیع سلم کرنا جائز ہے یعنی معدودات متقاربہ کی بیع عدداً بھی جائز ہے اور کیلاً بھی جائز ہے۔ اور رہا ان کا عددی ہونا تو یہ حکم نص نہیں ہے بلکہ لوگوں کے اتفاق کرنے سے عددی ہوگئی ہیں۔ تو گویا مدار لوگوں کے اتفاق پر ہوا پس جس طرح لوگوں کے اتفاق سے ایک چیز عددی ہوگئی ہے اسی طرح عاقدین کے اتفاق سے وہ چیز کیلی ہو جائے گی اور جب عددی چیز عاقدین کے اتفاق سے کیلی ہو گئی تو اس کی بیع سلم جس طرح عدداً جائز ہے اسی طرح کیلاً بھی جائز ہوگی۔ وكذا في الفلوس ... الخ سے صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ فلوس کی بیع سلم بھی عدداً جائز ہے۔ یہ حکم جامع صغیر میں بغیر اختلاف کے مذکور ہے۔ لیکن صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ بعض مشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ یہ حکم شیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور امام محمدؐ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔
Sahib al-Hidayah states that salam in homogeneous counted items is permissible both by count and by measure. For example, if salam is made for one rupee's worth of eggs, it is valid. Imam Zufar said that salam in homogeneous counted items by count is valid, but by measure it is not valid because counted items are of the category of counted, not measured. Things that are not measured cannot be sold by measure. Thus it is established that salam by measure is not valid. Another narration from Imam Zufar states that salam in homogeneous counted items is valid neither by measure nor by count, because there is a slight difference among individuals, and any counted item with difference is not valid even by count. Our proof is that quantity is sometimes known by count and sometimes by measure. So it is possible to specify homogeneous counted items by both count and measure. Their being counted is not a divine ruling but based on people's agreement. Just as people agreed to treat them as counted, the contracting parties can agree to treat them as measured. Therefore salam by measure is also valid. Similarly for fulus (copper coins): Sahib al-Hidayah states that salam in fulus is valid by count. This ruling is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir without dispute. However, some scholars say this is the view of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), while Imam Muhammad considers it invalid.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that homogeneous counted items can be sold by measure if the parties agree, because the determining factor is the ability to specify the quantity, not the customary method. The Hanafi proof is that quantity can be determined by either count or measure, so the contract can specify either. Imam Zufar's view that measure is invalid is based on the original nature of the items as counted. The issue of fulus (copper coins) involves a dispute between Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad. The Shaykhayn allow salam in fulus by count, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it because fulus are considered a medium of exchange (thaman) and thus subject to riba rules.

Key Terms
معدودات متقاربہ (ma'dudat mutaqariba): Homogeneous counted items close in value.
کیل (kayl): Measurement by volume.
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Shaykhayn), is salam in fulus (copper coins) valid?
A) Yes, by count.
B) No, never.
C) Only by weight.
D) Only if specified as thaman.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits salam by measure for homogeneous counted items if the parties agree, because the method of specification is based on custom and mutual consent.

Salam in Price-Variant Countable Items and Ma'dud Categories
Definition of ma'dud categories with a ruling on salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam for ma'dud mutafawit items and distinguish between ma'dud mutaqarib and ma'dud mutafawit based on price uniformity.

Core Idea
Salam is impermissible for countable items with significant price variation among individuals.

This lesson clarifies when a forward sale (salam) is valid for countable items. The Hanafi school draws a crucial distinction between items whose individuals have similar prices (ma'dud mutaqarib) and those with wide price variation (ma'dud mutafawit). The latter, such as watermelons, are not valid for salam due to the risk of dispute (gharar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses the permissibility of salam in items like watermelon and pomegranate. The ruling is that salam in such items is not permissible (la yajuz).
The ruling is explicit: 'salam sale of watermelon and pomegranate is not permissible'.
2
Understand the illa (legal cause)
Analyze why these items are prohibited. The author states the cause: 'great disparity in price among individuals, which people consider.' This disparity leads to uncertainty (gharar) and potential disputes.
The illa is the significant price variation among individuals of the same type.
3
Distinguish between ma'dud mutaqarib and ma'dud mutafawit
The passage defines two categories: ma'dud mutaqarib (countable items with uniform price) and ma'dud mutafawit (countable items with price variation). Memorize this dichotomy as it determines salam validity.
Example: eggs of hen are mutaqarib; watermelons are mutafawit.
4
Apply the rule to other examples
The passage lists similar items: gourd, bottle gourd, animal heads and feet. Use the illa to test other items. If a countable item has individuals with significant price differences, salam is invalid.
This step reinforces the principle through analogical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خربوزے اور انار کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح کرو، لوکی ، جانوروں کے سر اور پاؤں کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قیمت کے اعتبار سے ان کے افراد میں بہت بڑا تفاوت ہوتا ہے اور لوگ ان کے درمیان تفاوت کا اعتبار بھی کرتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ ایک خربوزہ ایک روپیہ کا ہوتا ہے اور دوسرا دو روپیہ کا ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ایک انار کم قیمت پر ملتا ہے اور دوسرا اس سے زیادہ قیمت پر ملتا ہے اور قیمت کے اعتبار سے جن چیزوں کے افراد میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے خربوزے اور انار وغیرہ اشیاء کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اب عددی متقارب اور عددی متفاوت کے درمیان ضابطہ یہ ہوا کہ اگر عددی چیز کے افراد میں قیمت کے اعتبار سے تفاوت ہوا تو وہ چیز عددی متفاوت کہلائے گی اور اگر تفاوت نہ ہو تو وہ عددی متقارب کہلائے گی۔
The author of Hidayah says: Salam sale of watermelon and pomegranate is not permissible, similarly gourd, bottle gourd, animal heads and feet are not permissible. Because there is a great disparity in their individuals in terms of price, and people consider that disparity. For example, we see one watermelon for one rupee and another for two rupees. Similarly one pomegranate is obtained at a low price and another at a higher price. And things whose individuals have disparity in price, their salam sale is not permissible. Therefore salam sale of watermelon, pomegranate, etc. will not be permissible. Now the rule between ma'dud mutaqarib and ma'dud mutafawit is that if in the individuals of a countable thing there is price disparity, it is called ma'dud mutafawit, and if there is no disparity, it is called ma'dud mutaqarib.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding salam in items like watermelon, pomegranate, gourd, lotus, animal heads and feet. The reasoning is that these items have individuals that vary greatly in market price, leading to potential disputes. For example, one watermelon may cost one rupee while another costs two, and people take this price difference into account. Since the purpose of salam is to have a known, standardized commodity, such price variation invalidates the contract. The passage then introduces the key distinction between ma'dud mutaqarib (countable items with similar individual prices) and ma'dud mutafawit (countable items with varying individual prices). The former is valid for salam, the latter is not. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi rulings on salam.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for a specific commodity to be delivered later.
عددي متقارب (ma'dud mutaqarib): Countable items whose individuals have negligible or no price disparity, e.g., eggs of hen.
عددي متفاوت (ma'dud mutafawit): Countable items whose individuals have significant price disparity, e.g., watermelons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is salam in watermelons not permissible?
A) Because watermelons are not a countable item.
B) Because watermelons have seasonal availability.
C) Because individuals vary greatly in price, leading to potential dispute.
D) Because watermelons are perishable.

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid only for countable items with uniform or negligible price variation (ma'dud mutaqarib); items with significant price disparity (ma'dud mutafawit) invalidate the contract.

Salam in Ostrich Eggs: Prohibition due to Ma'dud Mutafawit
Ruling on salam in ostrich eggs with analogical reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in ostrich eggs and explain the reasoning based on the category of ma'dud mutafawit.

Core Idea
Salam in ostrich eggs is impermissible because they are ma'dud mutafawit.

In this passage, we learn a specific ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding salam (forward sale) of ostrich eggs. While salam is generally allowed for standardized goods, it is prohibited for items that vary significantly in value. Ostrich eggs fall into this category, and the ruling illustrates how general principles are applied to specific cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is salam (salam contract) on ostrich eggs. The ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa is that it is not permissible (jā'iz nā' hai).
Think of the ruling as 'not permissible' which in Hanafi terminology can mean makruh tahrimi or haram; the toolbox categorizes it as makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the reason (illa)
The text states the reason: ostrich eggs are variable in value (ma'dud mutafawit). They differ in size, quality, and fertility, causing price uncertainty.
This reason is a sub-category of gharar (uncertainty) which invalidates salam.
3
Connect to the general principle
Earlier lessons established that salam in ma'dud mutafawit (countable items with price variance) is not permissible. Ostrich eggs are an instance of this category, so the general rule applies via qiyas.
The analogy is explicit: 'as has passed previously that salam of ma'dud mutafawit is not permissible.'
4
Consider the authority weight
This is a riwaya (narration) from Abu Hanifa, classified as nawadir (rare transmissions). Despite being rare, it is accepted in the Hanafi school.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) follows this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ شتر مرغ کے انڈوں کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شتر مرغ کے انڈے مالیت کے اعتبار سے متفاوت ہوتے ہیں اور سابق میں گزر چکا ہے کہ عددی متفاوت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے شتر مرغ کے انڈوں کی بیع مسلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔

And the reason for impermissibility is that ostrich eggs are variable in terms of value, and it has passed previously that salam of ma'dud mutafawit is not permissible. Therefore, salam sale of ostrich eggs will not be permissible.

Commentary
This passage presents a specific ruling transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding salam in ostrich eggs. The reasoning is analogical: ostrich eggs fall under the category of ma'dud mutafawit (countable items with price variance) due to their differing sizes and qualities, affecting their market value. Since the general rule prohibits salam in such items, this specific application follows. The ruling is consistent with the principles established in the previous lesson.

Key Terms
شتر مرغ کے انڈے (shatur-murgh ke anday): Ostrich eggs; considered a countable item with price variance (ma'dud mutafawit).

Salam in Countable Items: Can Measurement Replace Counting?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam by measurement vs counting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on salam in ma'dud mutaqarib by measurement, identify the opposing view of Imam Zufar, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Counting is convention, not a fixed rule – parties can agree to measurement.

Salam (advance sale) of uniformly valued countable items like eggs is normally done by specifying a number. But what if the parties agree to deliver by measurement? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf) allow it based on custom and convenience, while Imam Zufar insists on counting only. We'll unpack the reasoning and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that salam in ma'dud mutaqarib is valid by counting or measurement.
This is the view supported in Al-Hidayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar holds that only counting is valid; measurement is not permissible.
He argues that countable items are inherently not measurable.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Imam Zufar's dalil: ma'dud items are from the category of counted things, so they are not measurable; salam by measurement is invalid.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority counters that countability is based on 'urf (custom), not a revealed text. Therefore, parties can agree to treat it as measurable. Also, quantity can be known by both methods.
This is an istihsan over qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If parties agree to deliver measured items, the contract is valid per majority but invalid per Imam Zufar.
A judge following Imam Zufar would nullify such a contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ معدودات متقاربہ کی بیع سلم جس طرح شمار کر کے جائز ہے اسی طرح کیل کر کے بھی جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایک روپیہ کے ایک فقیر انڈوں کی بیع سلم کی گئی تو جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ معدودات متقاربہ میں شمار کر کے بیع سلم کرنا تو جائز ہے لیکن کیل کر کے جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ معدودات منقار بہ کے قبیلہ سے جو چیزیں ہیں وہ سب عددی میں کیلی نہیں ہیں۔ اور جو چیزیں کیلی نہ ہوں ان کی بیع سلم ، کیل کے ذریعہ کسی طرح درست ہو سکتی ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقدار کبھی تو شمار کرنے سے پہچانی جاتی ہے اور کبھی کیل کے ذریعہ معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ پس معدودات منقار بہ کا شمار اور کیل دونوں سے ضبط کرنا ممکن ہے اور جب دونوں سے ضبط کرنا ممکن ہے تو دونوں کے ساتھ بیچ مسلم کرنا جائز ہے یعنی معدودات متقاربہ کی بیع عدداً بھی جائز ہے اور کیلا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور رہا ان کا عددی ہونا تو یہ حکم نص نہیں ہے بلکہ لوگوں کے اتفاق کرنے سے عددی ہوگئی ہیں۔ تو گویا مدارلوگوں کے اتفاق پر ہوا پس جس طرح لوگوں کے اتفاق سے ایک چیز عددی ہوگئی ہے اسی طرح عاقدین کے اتفاق سے وہ چیز کیلی ہو جائے گی اور جب عددی چیز عاقدین کے اتفاق سے کیلی ہو گئی تو اس کی بیع سلم جس طرح عدداً جائز ہے اسی طرح کیلا بھی جائز ہوگی۔
The author of Hidayah says: Salam sale of ma'dud mutaqarib is permissible by counting as well as by measurement. For example, if a salam is made for a rupee's worth of eggs, it is permissible. Imam Zufar said: Salam in ma'dud mutaqarib is permissible by counting, but not by measurement. Because items that are from the category of counted things are all countable, not measurable. And things that are not measurable, their salam by measurement cannot be valid. Our proof is that quantity is sometimes known by counting, sometimes by measurement. So it is possible to control counted items by both counting and measurement. And when control by both is possible, then selling by both is permissible, i.e., salam in ma'dud mutaqarib is permissible by number and by measurement. And as for their being countable, that is not a textual ruling, but they became countable by people's convention. So the criterion is people's convention. Just as a thing became countable by people's agreement, similarly by the agreement of the contracting parties it can become measurable. And when a countable thing becomes measurable by agreement of the parties, then its salam is permissible both by number and by measurement.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the author of Al-Hidayah (representing the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Zufar. The issue is whether salam contracts in ma'dud mutaqarib (countable items with uniform price) can be executed by measurement (kayl) in addition to counting. Imam Zufar restricts it to counting only, arguing that such items are inherently countable and not measurable. The Hanafi counter-argument is based on the principle that quantity can be known through either method, and people's convention ('urf) determines the mode. Since the parties can agree to treat a countable item as measurable, salam by measurement becomes valid. This ruling is supported by istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas because it facilitates trade.

Key Terms
کیل (kayl): Measurement by volume or weight; a method of determining quantity in sales.
عد (add): Counting; determining quantity by number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on salam in ma'dud mutaqarib by measurement?
A) Not permissible at all.
B) Permissible only if the item is also sold by weight.
C) Permissible because parties can agree to treat it as measurable.
D) Permissible only for eggs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority upholds salam by measurement for countable items when parties agree, based on custom and istihsan.

Salam in Fulūs (Copper Coins) — Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on salam in fulus with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding salam in fulus and state the mufta bihi ruling with its proof.

Core Idea
Fulus can become goods by party agreement, making salam valid — thamaniyyah is not inherent but conventional.

The salam contract requires the subject matter to be a commodity (sila'), not currency. Fulus (copper coins) are normally used as currency, but the Hanafi school allows parties to treat them as goods by mutual agreement. This passage from al-Hidayah explores the dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) over whether salam in fulus is permissible. Understanding the reasoning behind each position strengthens your grasp of the role of party autonomy in determining the legal nature of an item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
Note that the author of al-Hidayah states the ruling (salam in fulus is permissible by number) but then attributes it to the two shaykhs, implying Imam Muhammad differs. Identify the exact point of contention: Is fulus always thaman (currency) and therefore not a valid subject for salam?
The passage says 'this ruling is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir without difference,' indicating it is mufta bihi in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad argues that fulus are thaman. Since salam in thaman is invalid (because it resembles a loan with profit), salam in fulus must be invalid. Understand why thaman is problematic in salam: the price in salam must be paid immediately, but the subject matter must be a measurable commodity.
This is a qiyas jali: fulus → thaman → salam invalid.
3
Examine the majority's rebuttal
The two shaykhs respond that thamaniyyah is not an inherent attribute; it is established by the parties' agreement. Since no outsider has authority over the parties, the same parties can nullify that attribute by mutual consent. Once thamaniyyah is annulled, fulus become goods (sila'), and salam in goods is permissible.
This is istihsan based on the principle that what is established by custom (urf) can be removed by the same custom.
4
Understand the objection and answer
A hypothetical objection: If fulus lose thamaniyyah, they should revert to being weighed items (as they were before being used as currency). But the ruling says salam is valid by number. The answer: the parties only annulled the attribute of thamaniyyah, not the attribute of countability. Countability (being ma'dud) is independent and can survive even after thamaniyyah is removed.
The key distinction: Countability (عددی) is not contingent on thamaniyyah; it can be a separate characteristic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا في الفلوس ... الخ سے صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ فلوس کی بیع سلم بھی عددا جائز ہے۔ یہ حکم جامع صغیر میں بغیر اختلاف کے مذکور ہے۔ لیکن صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ بعض مشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ واز کا یہ حکم شیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور امام محمدؐ کے نزدیک فلوس کی بیع سلم نا جائز ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فلوس شمن ہوتے ہیں اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ ثمن کی بیچ مسلم نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے فلوس کی بیچ سلم نا جائز ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فلوس کا شمن ہونا عاقدین کے حق میں ان دونوں کے اتفاق سے ثابت تھا اسلئے کہ دوسرے آدمی کو ان پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے پس جب فلوس کا شمن ہونا ان دونوں کے حق میں ان کے اتفاق سے تھا تو انہیں کے اتفاق سے ثمن ہونا باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور جب فلوس کاشمن ہونا باطل ہو گیا تو فلوس ان کے حق میں سامان ہو گئے اور سامان کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے لہذا فلوس کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ ولا تعود وزنياً سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ فلوس شمن ہونے سے پہلے چونکہ پیتل اور دھات کے ٹکڑے تھے اس لئے موزونات کے قبیلہ سے تھے لیکن جب ان کے ثمن ہونے پر اتفاق کر لیا تو یہ عددی ہو گئے تھے۔ پس جب عاقدین کے ان کی شمعیت کے ابطال پر اتفاق کرنے سے ان کا شمن ہونا باطل ہو گیا تو ان کا عددی ہونا بھی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ فلوس ثمنیت ہی کی وجہ سے عددی ہوئے تھے۔ مگر جب فلوس شمن ہی نہ رہے تو عددی بھی نہ رہیں گے بلکہ حالت سابقہ پر وزنی ہو جائیں گے۔ اور جب فلوس عددی نہ رہے بلکہ وزنی ہو گئے تو ان کی بیع سلم شمار کر کے جائز نہ ہونی چاہئے تھی بلکہ وزن سے جائز ہونی چاہئے تھی حالانکہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ فلوس کی بیع سلم عدد جائز ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عاقدین نے فلوس کے شمن ہونے کا اعتبار کرنے سے اعراض کیا ہے۔ ان کے عددی ہونے کا اعتبار کرنے سے اعراض نہیں کیا ہے۔ یعنی عاقدین نے فلوس کے شمن ہونے کے ابطال پر اتفاق کیا ہے۔ ان کے عددی ہونے کے ابطال پر اتفاق نہیں کیا ہے اور فلوس کی شمنیت کے ابطال سے ان کے عددی ہونے کا ابطال لازم نہیں آتا اور جب فلوس کی شمعیت کے ابطال سے عددی ہونے کا ابطال لازم نہیں آیا تو فلوس با وجود دشمن نہ ہونے کے عددی ہوں گے وزنی نہ ہوں گے ۔ اور جب فلوس عددی رہے عود کر کے وزنی نہ ہوئے تو فلوس کی بیع سلم بھی عدد آ جائز ہوگی۔
And likewise regarding fulus... the author of Hidayah said that salam of fulus is permissible by number. This ruling is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir without difference. But some mashayikh said that this ruling is according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to Imam Muhammad, salam of fulus is not permissible. Imam Muhammad's proof is that fulus are thaman (price, currency), and it has passed that salam of thaman is not permissible. Therefore salam of fulus is not permissible. Our proof is that the thamaniyyah of fulus was established for the parties by their mutual agreement, because no other person has authority over them. So when their thamaniyyah was by their agreement, their agreement can also nullify it. And when thamaniyyah becomes null, fulus become goods (sila') for them, and salam of goods is permissible. Therefore salam of fulus is permissible. The phrase 'wa la ta'ud wazaniyya' answers a question. The question: Before fulus were thaman, they were pieces of copper and metal, so they were from the category of weighed items. But when they agreed to treat them as thaman, they became countable. So when the parties agree to annul their thamaniyyah, their countability should also become null, because fulus became countable only due to thamaniyyah. But if they are no longer thaman, they should return to their original state of being weighed. Then salam by number should not be permissible, only by weight. Yet you claim salam by number is permissible. Answer: The parties have abandoned the consideration of thamaniyyah but not the consideration of countability. They agreed to annul thamaniyyah, not countability. And annulment of thamaniyyah does not necessarily entail annulment of countability. So fulus remain countable, not weighed. Therefore salam by number remains permissible.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage deals with the permissibility of salam in fulus (copper coins used as currency). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) consider salam in fulus permissible by counting, while Imam Muhammad considers it invalid. Imam Muhammad's reasoning is that fulus function as thaman (price/currency), and salam in thaman is not allowed because it resembles a loan (qard) with profit. The majority's response is that thamaniyyah is a contingent attribute based on the parties' agreement; since the parties can agree to treat fulus as goods (sila'), they can also annul the thamaniyyah, making fulus a commodity. The crucial point is that countability (being ma'dud) does not depend solely on thamaniyyah; fulus retain their countability even after annulling thamaniyyah. Thus salam by number remains valid. This ruling is supported by analogy and istihsan.

Key Terms
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as currency, considered here as potentially both thaman and commodity.
ثمن (thaman): Price, currency; medium of exchange.
شمنیت / ثمنیت (thamaniyyah): The attribute of being a price/currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs, why does the annulment of thamaniyyah not lead to the annulment of countability?
A) Because fulus are naturally countable and cannot be weighed.
B) Because the parties agreed only to annul thamaniyyah, not countability.
C) Because countability is a direct consequence of thamaniyyah.
D) Because Imam Muhammad's objection was about weight, not number.

Key Takeaway
Salam in fulus is permissible by number according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, based on the parties' ability to annul thamaniyyah by agreement, with countability remaining independent.

Salam in Animals — Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on salam in animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in animals, cite the two proofs (hadith and rational), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument by identifying the specific Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is impermissible in the Hanafi school—even after description, hidden variation causes dispute, and the Prophet explicitly forbade it.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of salam (forward sale) in animals. The Hanafi school declares it impermissible, while Imam al-Shafi'i permits it with sufficient description. We will analyze both positions, their proofs, and the critical Hanafi response that resolves the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and the Shafi'i opposing view
Identify the two positions: Hanafi says salam in animals is not permissible; Shafi'i says it is permissible with detailed description.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Understand the Shafi'i analogy: animals become known by description, and remaining variation is slight, like clothes.
3
Examine the Hanafi rational proof
Analyze the Hanafi counter-anology: hidden internal qualities cause significant price variation, leading to dispute (gharar), unlike manufactured clothes.
4
Examine the Hanafi textual proof
Consider the hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly prohibited salam in animals, which is a primary textual evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi deems such salam contracts invalid; Shafi'i allows them if properly described. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز السلم في الحيوان وقال الشافعى يجوز لانه يصير معلوما ببيان الجنس والسن والنوع والصفة والتفاوت بعد ذلك يسير فاشبه الثياب ولنا ان بعد ذكر ما ذكر يبقى فيه تفاوت فاحش في المالية باعتبار المعانى الباطنة فيفضى الى المنازعة بخلاف الثياب لانه مصنوع للعباد فقلما يتفاوت الثوبان اذا نسجا على منوال واحد وقد صح ان النبي عليه السلام نهى عن السلم فى الحيوان ويدخل فيه جميع اجناسه حتى العصافير
Salam in animals is not permissible. And al-Shafi'i said it is permissible, because it becomes known by specifying the type, age, kind, and description, and the variation after that is slight, so it resembles clothes. And our argument is that after mentioning all that, there remains a substantial disparity in value due to internal qualities, leading to dispute, unlike clothes because they are manufactured by people and two cloths woven on the same loom rarely differ. And it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited salam in animals, and this includes all their types, even sparrows.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute on salam in animals. Imam al-Shafi'i permits it if the animal is described thoroughly (type, age, gender, qualities), arguing that the remaining variation is negligible, just like in garments. The Hanafi school opposes this, citing two proofs: (1) Rational argument (qiyas): Even with description, animals have hidden internal differences (e.g., temperament, health, strength) that cause significant price variation, leading to disputes (gharar). This is unlike manufactured cloth, where identical looms produce nearly identical products. (2) Textual proof (hadith): The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly forbade salam in animals, and this prohibition extends to all species, including small birds like sparrows. Thus, according to the Hanafi school, any salam contract involving an animal as the subject matter is invalid.

Key Terms
حيوان (hayawan): Any living animal, including birds and livestock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a Hanafi proof against salam in animals?
A) Hadith prohibition from the Prophet.
B) Rational argument about hidden price variation.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Analogy to clothes (but reversed).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits salam in animals due to explicit hadith and risk of gharar from hidden variation, overriding the Shafi'i analogy to clothes.

Salam in Fulus: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in copper coins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on salam in fulus and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Fulus are thaman by agreement, not by nature; annulling their thaman status makes them goods, permitting salam.

In Hanafi fiqh, salam (forward sale) is generally not permitted in thaman (price) but is permitted in goods (sama'n). Copper coins (fulus) typically function as thaman, but the school sees their thaman status as based on mutual agreement, not inherent nature. This creates a dispute within the Hanafi school: can the parties annul that status and treat fulus as goods for salam? This lesson unpacks the arguments of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the reasoning behind the reliance on Abu Hanifa's view, and the key nuance of countability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
State that Imam Muhammad considers salam in fulus invalid because fulus are inherently thaman. Abu Hanifa holds it valid because thaman status is based on agreement and can be annulled.
Abu Hanifa's position is the mufta bihi.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad argues: fulus are thaman; salam in thaman is invalid; therefore salam in fulus is invalid.
This relies on the premise that thaman status is inseparable from fulus.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa responds: thaman status is established by the parties' mutual agreement; therefore, they can annul it by mutual agreement, transforming fulus into goods for the purpose of salam.
The key is the contractual power of the parties (wilaya) over their own transaction.
4
Examine the objection about revert to weighable
An objection arises: if thaman status is annulled, fulus should revert to their original weighable nature, making salam by weight necessary. But Abu Hanifa allows salam by count.
This targets the apparent inconsistency.
5
Understand the resolution: countability remains
The response: annulling thaman status does not automatically annul countability (adadi) because countability was also established by convention and the parties did not agree to annul it. Thus, fulus remain countable and salam by count is valid.
This distinction is crucial and is explained with reference to the chapter of Riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نزدیک فلوس کی بیع سلم نا جائز ہے۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فلوس شمن ہوتے ہیں اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ ثمن کی بیچ مسلم نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے فلوس کی بیچ سلم نا جائز ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فلوس کا شمن ہونا عاقدین کے حق میں ان دونوں کے اتفاق سے ثابت تھا اسلئے کہ دوسرے آدمی کو ان پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے پس جب فلوس کا شمن ہونا ان دونوں کے حق میں ان کے اتفاق سے تھا تو انہیں کے اتفاق سے ثمن ہونا باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور جب فلوس کاشمن ہونا باطل ہو گیا تو فلوس ان کے حق میں سامان ہو گئے اور سامان کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے لہذا فلوس کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔
ولا تعود وزنياً سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ فلوس شمن ہونے سے پہلے چونکہ پیتل اور دھات کے ٹکڑے تھے اس لئے موزونات کے قبیلہ سے تھے لیکن جب ان کے ثمن ہونے پر اتفاق کر لیا تو یہ عددی ہو گئے تھے۔ پس جب عاقدین کے ان کی شمعیت کے ابطال پر اتفاق کرنے سے ان کا شمن ہونا باطل ہو گیا تو ان کا عددی ہونا بھی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ فلوس ثمنیت ہی کی وجہ سے عددی ہوئے تھے۔ مگر جب فلوس شمن ہی نہ رہے تو عددی بھی نہ رہیں گے بلکہ حالت سابقہ پر وزنی ہو جائیں گے۔ اور جب فلوس عددی نہ رہے بلکہ وزنی ہو گئے تو ان کی بیع سلم شمار کر کے جائز نہ ہونی چاہئے تھی بلکہ وزن سے جائز ہونی چاہئے تھی حالانکہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ فلوس کی بیع سلم عدد جائز ہے۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عاقدین نے فلوس کے شمن ہونے کا اعتبار کرنے سے اعراض کیا ہے۔ ان کے عددی ہونے کا اعتبار کرنے سے اعراض نہیں کیا ہے۔ یعنی عاقدین نے فلوس کے شمن ہونے کے ابطال پر اتفاق کیا ہے۔ ان کے عددی ہونے کے ابطال پر اتفاق نہیں کیا ہے اور فلوس کی شمنیت کے ابطال سے ان کے عددی ہونے کا ابطال لازم نہیں آتا اور جب فلوس کی شمعیت کے ابطال سے عددی ہونے کا ابطال لازم نہیں آیا تو فلوس با وجود دشمن نہ ہونے کے عددی ہوں گے وزنی نہ ہوں گے ۔ اور جب فلوس عددی رہے عود کر کے وزنی نہ ہوئے تو فلوس کی بیع سلم بھی عدد آ جائز ہوگی۔ اس کی تفصیل باب الربوا میں بیع الفلس با فلسین کے مسئلہ کے تحت گذر چکی ہے۔
According to us, salam in fulus (copper coins) is not permissible. Imam Muhammad's proof is that fulus are thaman (price) and it has already passed that salam in thaman is not permissible. Therefore salam in fulus is not permissible. Our proof is that the status of fulus as thaman was established between the two contracting parties by their mutual agreement, because no other person has authority over them. So when their status as thaman was established by their agreement, then by their agreement it can be invalidated. And when the thaman status of fulus is invalidated, they become goods in their context, and salam in goods is permissible. Hence salam in fulus is permissible.
“And they do not revert to being weighable” is the answer to a question.
The question is: Before being thaman, fulus were pieces of brass and metal, so they belonged to the category of weighables. But when they agreed on them being thaman, they became countable. So when the contracting parties agreed on annulling their thaman status, their being countable would also become invalid, because fulus became countable only because of thaman status. But when fulus are no longer thaman, they will not remain countable; rather they will revert to their original state of being weighable. And when fulus are no longer countable but become weighable, then salam in them should not be permissible by count but by weight, whereas you (Abu Hanifa) have stated that salam in fulus is permissible by count.
The answer to this is that the contracting parties have abandoned the consideration of fulus being thaman; they have not abandoned the consideration of their being countable. That is, the parties agreed on annulling their thaman status, but they did not agree on annulling their countability. And the invalidation of thaman status does not necessitate the invalidation of their countability. When the invalidation of thaman status does not necessitate the invalidation of countability, then fulus, despite not being thaman, remain countable, not weighable. And since fulus remain countable and do not revert to being weighable, salam in fulus is permissible by count. The detail of this has passed in the chapter of Riba under the issue of selling one coin for two coins.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of salam (forward sale) in fulus (copper coins). Imam Muhammad holds that salam in fulus is invalid because fulus function as thaman (price), and salam in thaman is not permitted. The relied-upon Hanafi position (attributed to Abu Hanifa and the majority) argues that the thaman status of fulus is established only by mutual agreement of the parties; therefore, they can also agree to annul that status. Once annulled, fulus become goods (sama'n), and salam in goods is valid. A subsequent objection questions why fulus do not revert to being weighable (since they were originally weighable) and thus require salam by weight rather than count. The response clarifies that the annulment of thaman status does not annul the countability (adadi) that was also established by agreement. Thus, fulus remain countable for salam purposes. This ruling is part of the Hanafi school's distinctive treatment of fulus as having a dual nature—countable by convention and weighable by origin—and illustrates the use of rational reasoning (istihsan) in resolving apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as currency, specifically considered as thaman (price) by convention.
ثمن (thaman): The price or monetary medium in a sale; salam in thaman is generally invalid because it leads to riba.
عددی (adadi): Countable items, i.e., items sold by number rather than weight or measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, why is salam in fulus (copper coins) permissible even though they are typically considered thaman?
A) Because fulus are not real thaman but only goods.
B) Because the contracting parties can agree to annul the thaman status, turning fulus into goods, and salam in goods is permissible.
C) Because Imam Muhammad ruled it permissible.
D) Because fulus are weighable by nature and salam is allowed in weighable items.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of salam in fulus hinges on the parties' ability to annul the thaman status, turning fulus into goods, while countability remains unchanged.

Salam in Animals: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on salam in animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school invalidates salam in animals even when attributes are specified, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Prophetic prohibition and hidden value variation make salam in animals invalid despite specification.

The validity of salam (advance payment sale) in animals is a classic point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While both agree that salam is permissible in general, they diverge on whether animals can be specified sufficiently to avoid uncertainty. This lesson examines the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Salam in animals is invalid even with specification of type, age, species, and description.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad permit salam in animals if attributes are specified.
The text mentions Al-Shafi'i specifically.
3
Analyze the opponent's proof
They argue specification makes the animal known like garments; variation is slight; and the Prophet practiced salam with 'Amr ibn al-'As.
The garment analogy is key.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
Hidden variations in animals (temperament, health, abilities) cause significant value differences leading to disputes, unlike manufactured goods; and the explicit hadith prohibits salam in animals.
The hadith is general, including all animals.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically: Hanafis consider the contract invalid and requiring rescission; Shafi'is enforce it.
Be aware of which ruling applies in your context.

تشریح جانوروں کے اندر بیع سلم کی دوصورتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ مطلق جانور کی بیع سلم کی گئی ہو یعنی نہ اس کی جنس بیان کی ہو، نہ عمر بیان کی ہو، نہ صفت بیان کی ہو، اور نہ اس کی نوع بیان کی ہو۔ دوسرے یہ کہ مذکورہ چیزیں بیان کر کے جانور کی بیع سلم کی گئی ہو ۔ پہلی صورت میں بالا تفاق بیع سلم نا جائز ہے اور دوسری صورت میں ہمارے نزدیک نا جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اس کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب جانور کی جنس بیان کر دی گئی ہمثلاً کہا گیا کہ وہ اونٹ ہو یا بھینس ہو۔ اور عمر بیان کر دی گئی مثلاً کہا گیا کہ وہ بنت مخاض نہو یا بنت لبون ہو یا کہا گیا کہ جذعہ ہو یا شنی ہو یا ہمارے زمانہ میں کہا گیا کہ وہ ایک دانت ہو یا دو دانت ہو، اور نوع بیان گئی مثلاً کہا گیا کہ وہ بختی ہو یا عربی ہو اور صفت بیان کر دی گئی مثلاً کہا گیا کہ وہ خوب فربہ ، موٹا تازہ ہو یا دبلا پتلا لاغر ہو تو مسلم فیہ کی مالیت منضبط اور معلوم ہو جائے گی ۔ اور ہر وہ چیز جو اوصاف کے بیان سے معلوم اور منضبط ہو جاتی ہو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے جنس ہن، نوع اور صفت کے بیان کر دینے کے بعد جانور کی بیع سلم بھی جائز ہو جائے گی۔ اور رہا یہ سوال کہ جانور کی جنس ہن، نوع اور صفت بیان کرنے کے باوجود تفاوت باقی رہتا ہے۔ لہذا جانور کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہونی چاہئے تھی۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ چار چیزیں بیان کرنے کے بعد جو تفاوت باقی رہ جاتا ہے وہ بہت خفیف اور کم ہوتا ہے۔ پس یہ کپڑوں کے مشابہ ہو گیا یعنی جس طرح کپڑے کی جنس، نوع ، صفت اور موٹا پتلا بیان کرنے سے کپڑا یعنی مسلم فیہ معلوم ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کی بیع سلم بالاتفاق جائز ہے باوجود یکہ تھوڑا سا تفاوت باقی رہ جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح جانور کی بیع سلم بھی جائز ہوگی۔

Salam in animals is not permissible. Al-Shafi'i said it is permissible, because it becomes known by specifying the type, age, species, and description, and after that the variation is slight, so it resembles garments. Our [Hanafi] proof is that after mentioning what has been mentioned, there remains a gross variation in value due to inner qualities, leading to dispute, unlike garments because they are manufactured by people; rarely do two garments differ when woven on the same loom. And it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited salam in animals, and all types of animals are included, even sparrows.
[Urdu: Translation and commentary follows clarifying the two scenarios: absolute salam in animals without specification (invalid by consensus) and specified salam (invalid according to us, valid according to al-Shafi'i). Al-Shafi'i's detailed proof includes the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As regarding purchasing one camel for two on credit, which is a salam contract. The Hanafi response emphasizes the gross remaining variation due to hidden traits like speed, obedience, intelligence, beauty, etc.]
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute on salam in animals. The Hanafi position, supported by a hadith prohibition and reasoning about hidden variations, holds that salam in animals is invalid even if attributes are specified. Al-Shafi'i argues that specification makes the animal sufficiently known, similar to garments, and cites the Prophet's practice with 'Amr ibn al-'As. The commentary explains two scenarios: absolute salam (invalid by consensus) and specified salam (invalid for Hanafis, valid for Shafi'is). The Hanafi proof stresses that despite specification, animals have significant internal differences (temperament, health, abilities) that lead to disputes, unlike standardized manufactured goods. The hadith prohibition is general, including all animals from camels to sparrows.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for a specifically described good to be delivered at a future date.
حيوان (hayawan): Animals of all types, including cattle, birds, etc.
تفاوت (tafawut): Variation in value or quality among items of the same apparent description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Why do Hanafis consider salam in animals invalid even when attributes like type, age, species, and description are specified?
A) Because animals are not goods and cannot be subject to salam.
B) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited salam in animals, and due to hidden variations in value causing disputes.
C) Because animals must be delivered immediately in salam.
D) Because salam is only allowed for crops and textiles.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school invalidates salam in animals due to the prophetic prohibition and the presence of significant hidden variations that lead to disputes, unlike standardized goods.

Salam in Animals: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute over salam in animals: Hanafi vs Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi prohibition of salam in animals, evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hidden differences in animals make salam invalid – describing the exterior does not remove gharar.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a legitimate contract for fungible goods like grain or cloth. But when the subject matter is an animal, the Hanafi school rules it invalid even with full description, while the Shafi'i school permits it. This lesson explores the reasoning behind each position and the key point of contention: whether describing an animal's species, age, type, and attributes eliminates the uncertainty (gharar) that salam is designed to avoid.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: salam in animals is fasid (voidable) even when fully described. Note that the Hanafis base this on a hadith prohibiting salam in animals and the principle of mufḍī ilā al-munāza‘ah (leading to dispute).
The Hanafi ruling applies to all animals, including small ones like sparrows.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik and Ahmad) hold that salam in animals is permissible if the animal is fully described by species, age, type, and attribute.
They consider any remaining difference insignificant, analogous to cloth.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: qiyas to cloth where description removes uncertainty, and the hadith of the Prophet ordering salam in camels for the army of 'Amr ibn al-'As.
The qiyas argues that just as cloth becomes known through description, so do animals.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: (1) Qiyas is invalid because animals are divinely created with hidden variations (speed, temperament, beauty) that affect value, while cloth is man-made and uniform. (2) The hadith of camels is abrogated by the riba verse. (3) The Hanafis have their own hadith prohibiting salam in animals, which covers all types.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis do not permit salam in animals except in rare cases, while Shafi'is allow it widely. This affects financing and trade of livestock.
A Hanafi mufti will reject such contracts, while a Shafi'i will accept them.

کبوتر اور چڑیا جیسے جانورں کی بیع سلم بھی اس نص کی وجہ سے جائز نہ ہوگی اگر چہ ان کے افراد میں زیادہ تفاوت نہیں ہوتا۔
It becomes known and after that the difference is insignificant, so it became similar to cloth. And our proof is that after mentioning the aforementioned matters, since in an animal there remains a great difference in value with regard to internal matters, therefore it will lead to dispute, unlike cloth because cloth is made by servants (humans). So when two cloths are woven on one loom, there is very little difference between them. And this is correct that the Prophet (PBUH) prohibited salam (advance sale) of animals, and the word 'animal' includes all its types, even sparrows. Explanation: There are two scenarios for salam in animals. One is that salam is made absolutely, i.e., neither its species, nor age, nor attribute, nor type is specified. The second is that salam is made after specifying the mentioned things. In the first scenario, salam is unanimously impermissible, and in the second scenario, it is impermissible according to us (Hanafis). According to Imam Shafi'i, it is permissible; Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that when the species of the animal is specified (e.g., camel or buffalo), and the age is specified (e.g., bint makhad, bint labun, jadha'a, thani, or in our time: one-tooth or two-tooth), and the type is specified (e.g., Bakhti or Arabi), and the attribute is specified (e.g., very fat, plump and fresh, or lean and thin), then the value of the muslam fihi becomes defined and known. And whatever becomes defined and known through the description of attributes, salam in it is permissible. Therefore, after specifying species, type, and attribute, salam in animals also becomes permissible. As for the objection that despite specifying species, type, and attribute, a difference remains, so salam in animals should not be permissible, the answer is that after mentioning these four things, the remaining difference is very insignificant. So it became similar to cloth, meaning just as by specifying the cloth's type, kind, attribute, and thickness, the cloth (muslam fihi) becomes known, and salam in it is unanimously permissible despite a slight remaining difference, similarly salam in animals becomes permissible. In support of the permissibility of salam in animals, Imam Shafi'i also argues that the Prophet (PBUH) commanded during the preparation of the army of 'Amr ibn al-'As to buy one camel in exchange for two camels with a fixed term, i.e., take one camel immediately and give two camels after a period. So the one camel taken immediately is the capital (ra's al-mal), and the two camels to be delivered after a period are muslam fihi, and this contract is called salam. From this, it is known that the Prophet (PBUH) commanded salam in animals. And who can doubt the permissibility of something commanded by the Messenger of Allah? So it is established that salam in animals is permissible. Our proof is that even after specifying the four attributes (species, age, type, and attribute), there remains a great difference in animals in terms of value and price, and this difference is due to internal matters. For example, a horse being fast and obedient, a slave being intelligent and efficient, a slave woman being beautiful—such matters increase people's desire and raise the price, and their absence reduces the price. This is why sometimes two horses are equal in species, age, type, and attribute, but due to internal matters, one has a very high price and the other a low price. So due to these internal matters, a dispute will arise at the time of delivery of the muslam fihi, and any contract in which there is a possibility of dispute is a fasid (voidable) contract. Therefore, we say that salam in animals is impermissible and fasid. And Imam Shafi'i's analogizing animals to cloth is not correct because cloths are made by humans, and when humans weave two pieces on one thread and one loom in the same style, there is very little difference in value between them. But humans have no role in the creation of animals; rather, Allah, the Glorious and Exalted, creates two animals of the same species by His power, and there is a great difference in value between them. So with this difference, how can analogizing animals to cloth be correct? And the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As about buying one camel for two camels was a command before the revelation of the verse of riba; this command was abrogated by the verse of riba. Since an abrogated hadith cannot be used as evidence, using this hadith as evidence is not correct. As for the hadith, our transmitted proof is that the Prophet (PBUH) prohibited salam in animals, and the word 'animal' includes all its types, even pigeons and sparrows, meaning salam in animals like pigeons and sparrows is also not permissible due to this text, even if there is not much difference among their individuals.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of salam (advance payment sale) in animals. The text begins by presenting the Hanafi position: salam in animals is impermissible even when the animal is described by species, age, type, and attribute. It contrasts this with the Shafi'i view (also held by Maliki and Hanbali schools) that such description removes uncertainty, making salam permissible. The commentary then explains the two scenarios: absolute salam (impermissible by consensus) and described salam (disputed). The Shafi'i argument is presented in detail: description (jins, sinn, naw', sifah) makes the subject matter known, analogous to cloth; any remaining difference is insignificant. The Shafi'i also cite the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As where the Prophet ordered salam in camels. The Hanafi response follows: first, the analogy to cloth is flawed because animals are divinely created with significant internal variations (such as temperament, skill, beauty) that affect value, while cloth is man-made and uniform. Second, the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As is abrogated by the riba verse. Finally, the Hanafis rely on their own hadith where the Prophet explicitly prohibited salam in animals, and this prohibition covers all kinds, even small ones like sparrows. The commentary emphasizes that the Hanafi ruling is based on the principle that salam is meant to avoid dispute, and hidden differences in animals inevitably lead to conflict at delivery.

Key Terms
بیع سلم (bay' al-salam): A sale where payment is made in advance for a specified commodity to be delivered at a future date.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The commodity being sold in a salam contract, which is to be delivered later.
تفاوت (tafāwut): Difference or variation in value or quality.
مفضی الی المنازعہ (mufḍī ilā al-munāza‘ah): Leading to dispute or contention, a criterion for invalidity in contracts.
منسوخ (mansūkh): Abrogated; a ruling from the Quran or Sunnah that has been superseded by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi school's ruling on salam in animals after specifying species, age, type, and attribute?
A) Sahih (valid)
B) Batil (void)
C) Fasid (voidable)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits salam in animals due to hidden differences in value that cause gharar, even if the animal is fully described; the Shafi'i school permits it based on analogy to cloth and a hadith they consider valid.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Salam in Animal Limbs, Hides, and Non-Standardizable Countables
Ruling on salam in animal parts and other countables with inherent variation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in animal limbs, hides, firewood bundles, and grass sheaves, and identify the condition under which such contracts become permissible.

Core Idea
Salam in countables with inherent variation (adadi mutafawit) is invalid unless measurement is specified and uniformity assured.

The Hanafi school strictly regulates salam (forward sale) to prevent uncertainty (gharar). This passage from al-Hidayah extends the general principle to specific items: animal heads and trotters, hides, firewood bundles, and grass sheaves. These are considered 'adadi mutafawit'—countable but varying significantly in size and value. The ruling is impermissible by default, but an exception exists when the variation is eliminated by specifying a measurable attribute such as the length of the bundle. Understanding this ruling helps you grasp how Hanafi jurists balance contractual freedom with the need to avoid disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and the general ruling
List the items mentioned: animal limbs (heads and trotters), hides (by count), firewood (by bundles), fresh grass (by sheaves). The general ruling: salam is not permissible (la yajuz) in all these cases.
The ruling is stated in the first part of the passage.
2
Understand the 'illa (reason) for prohibition
The text gives the reason: 'due to difference' (li al-tafawut). These items are described as 'adadi mutafawit' (numerically varying) with no standard measure. This variation leads to potential dispute at delivery, which is the core of gharar.
The 'illa is inherent variation that cannot be standardized by mere count.
3
Recognize the exception
The passage states that salam becomes permissible 'if that is known by specifying the length of what the bundle is tied with, that it is a handspan or a cubit; then it becomes permissible if it is in a manner that does not differ.' The exception applies only when a measurable attribute is specified and the items are uniform.
Specifying the tie length (shibr or dhira') removes ambiguity for bundles and sheaves.
4
Note the condition of uniformity
The exception requires that the items 'do not differ'—i.e., all delivered bundles must match the specified measurement exactly. If variation persists, the contract remains invalid.
Uniformity is a condition for validity, not just the specification.
5
Apply to new similar cases
The same principle applies to any countable item with significant individual variation: e.g., salam in watermelons by piece is invalid, but if specified by weight or size, it may be permissible. Identify the attribute that eliminates variation.
The key is to find a measurable attribute that ensures uniformity.

قال ولا فى اطرافه كالرؤس والاكارع للتفاوت فيها اذهو عددى متفاوت لامقدر لها قال ولا فى الجلود عددا ولا في الحطب حزماً ولا فى الرطبة جُرزاً للتفاوت الا اذا عرف ذلك بان يبين له طول ما يشد به الحزمة انه شير او ذراع فحينئذ يجوز اذا كان على وجه لا يتفاوت ترجمہ اور جانور کے اطراف سر اور پاؤں کے مانند میں بھی (بیع سلم ) جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان چیزوں میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے اسلئے کہ یہ چیز میں عددی متفاوت ہیں ۔ ان کے واسطے کوئی اندازہ نہیں ہے۔ اور کھالوں کی بیع سلم عددا اور لکڑیوں کی بیع سلم گھڑی سے اور گھاس کی بیع سلم پولی سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے افراد میں ) تفاوت ہوتا ہے مگر جبکہ معلوم ہو بایں طور کہ اس چیز کا طول کہ ایک بالشت ہے یا ایک ہاتھ ہے بیان کر دے جس سے گھا باندھا جائے گا تو اس وقت بیع سلم جائز ہوگی جبکہ ایسے طور پر ہو کہ اس میں تفاوت نہ ہوتا ہو۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ جانوروں کے سروں اور پاؤں کی بیچ مسلم جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ جانوروں کے سروں اور پاؤں میں چھوٹا اور بڑا ہونے کی وجہ سے مالیت میں بہت بڑا تفاوت ہوتا ہے تو گویا یہ عددی متفاوت ہوئے ان کے واسطے کوئی اندازہ نہیں لگایا جا سکتا ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ عددی متفاوت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے جانوروں کے سر اور پاؤں کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جانوروں کی کھالوں میں بھی عدد بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ کھا لیں عددی ہیں۔ اور ان میں بعض کھالیں چھوٹی اور بعض بڑی ہوتی ہیں۔ اسی طرح بعض کا چوڑان کم اور بعض کا زیادہ ہوتا ہے بہر حال اس تفاوت کی وجہ سے ان کی مالیت میں بہت بڑا تفاوت ہوتا ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ عددی متفاوت کی بیع سلم مفضی الی المنازعہ ہونے کی وجہ سے چونکہ نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔
He said: 'And not in its limbs, like heads and trotters, due to difference in them; for they are numerically varying, not measurable. He said: 'And not in hides by count, nor in firewood by bundles, nor in fresh grass by sheaves, due to difference, unless that is known by specifying the length of what the bundle is tied with, that it is a handspan or a cubit; then it becomes permissible if it is in a manner that does not differ.' Translation: And salam in the limbs of an animal, like heads and feet, is also not permissible because there is difference in these things, so they are numerically varying; there is no estimate for them. And salam in hides by count, and in firewood by bundle, and in grass by sheaf is not permissible because there is difference among their individuals, except when it is known such that he specifies the length of what the bundle is tied with, that it is a handspan or a cubit; then salam becomes permissible if it is in a manner that does not differ. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that salam in animal heads and feet is not permissible because in animal heads and feet, due to being small or large, there is a great difference in value; so they are numerically varying, no estimate can be made for them, and it has passed earlier that salam in numerically varying items is not permissible. Therefore, salam in animal heads and feet will not be permissible. Sahib al-Quduri says that in animal hides as well, by count, salam is not permissible because hides are numerical; some hides are small and some large, similarly some have less width and some more; in any case, due to this difference, there is a great difference in their value, and it has passed earlier that salam in numerically varying items, because it leads to dispute, is not permissible.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents a straightforward ruling from al-Hidayah (via Quduri) regarding salam in specific items: animal limbs (heads and feet), hides (by count), firewood (by bundles), and fresh grass (by sheaves). The general principle is that salam is not permissible in these because they are 'adadi mutafawit' (countable but varying significantly in size and value), which leads to uncertainty and potential dispute. However, an exception is made if the items are precisely measured: for example, if the length of the bundle (for firewood or grass) is specified in handspans or cubits, and the items are produced uniformly without variation, then salam becomes permissible. The commentary from Sahib al-Quduri emphasizes that heads and feet of animals vary greatly in size, so they cannot be standardized; similarly, hides vary in area. The key criterion is that the subject matter of salam must be known in a way that prevents conflict at delivery. This ruling is consistent with the earlier discussion on salam in animals: the prohibition stems from the principle of avoiding gharar (uncertainty).

Key Terms
اطراف (atrāf): Limbs of an animal, specifically heads and trotters/feet in this context.
عددی متفاوت (‘adadi mutafāwit): Countable items where individual units vary significantly in size or value.
حزمة (huzmah): A bundle of firewood or grass, tied together.
جرزة (jurzah): A sheaf or bundle of fresh grass.
شبر / ذراع (shibr / dhirā‘): Handspan and cubit, units of length used to specify the size of bundles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does salam in firewood by bundles become permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the type of wood is specified
B) When the length of the bundle is specified in handspans or cubits
C) When the wood is dry
D) When the buyer inspects the wood before the contract

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi salam, countables with inherent variation (adadi mutafawit) are impermissible unless the variation is eliminated by specifying a measurable attribute such as length or weight and ensuring uniformity.

Salam in Animals: Why Variation Invalidates the Contract
Explains why salam in animals is invalid and refutes Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in animals and explain why the analogy to cloth is rejected.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is invalid because hidden variation leads to dispute, and analogy to cloth fails due to lack of human control over animal traits.

In this passage, the Hanafi school explains why salam (advance payment sale) in animals is not valid. While Imam Shafi'i analogizes animals to cloth, the Hanafis reject this analogy, pointing to the inherent unpredictability of animal traits. We will examine the Hanafi reasoning and the response to the Shafi'i objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The passage states that salam in animals is invalid (fasid) because hidden qualities cause price variation, leading to disputes. Any contract prone to dispute is invalid. Also, the Prophet explicitly forbade salam in animals.
The prohibition (nahy) indicates fasād per Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam Shafi'i allows salam in animals by analogizing (qiyas) to cloth, which is permissible in salam. He also cites the hadith of Amr ibn al-As who exchanged a camel for two camels before the riba verses.
Shafi'i considers the hadith as evidence that salam in animals is allowed.
3
Analyze the Hanafi refutation of the analogy
The Hanafi response: Cloth is manufactured by humans under controlled conditions, so variation is minimal. Animals are created by Allah with inherent variation, making them unsuitable for precise specification. The illa (effective cause) of human control is absent, so qiyas fails.
This refutation highlights the importance of illa in analogical reasoning.
4
Note the use of abrogation regarding the hadith
The Hanafis argue that the hadith of Amr ibn al-As is abrogated by the verses on riba (e.g., Quran 2:275). An abrogated hadith cannot be used as evidence.
Thus, the Shafi'i proof from that hadith is rejected.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that salam in animals is invalid for all species, including birds, even if variation is small, due to the general prohibition.
The rule is general: salam is only valid for goods that can be precisely described (like manufactured items).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ جلد- منم ہوتے ہیں مگر امور باطنہ کی وجہ سے ایک کی قیمت بہت زیادہ اور دوسرے کی کم ہوتی ہے۔ پس ان امور باطنہ کی وجہ سے مسلم فیہ کی سپردگی کے وقت جھگڑا پیدا ہوگا اور جس عقد میں جھگڑا پیدا ہونے کا امکان ہو وہ عقد فاسد ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے ہم نے کہا کہ جانور کی بیع سلم نا جائز اور فاسد ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کا جانوروں کو کپڑوں پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کپڑے بندوں کے تیار کردہ ہیں اور بندے جب دو تھان ایک سوت اور ایک آلہ سے ایک ہی طرز پر بنتے ہیں تو مالیت کے اعتبار سے ان میں بہت کم تفاوت ہوتا ہے اور جانور پیدا کرنے میں بندوں کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے بلکہ حق سبحانہ و تعالیٰ اپنی قدرت سے ایک ہی جنس کے دو جانور پیدا کرتا ہے اور ان دونوں میں مالیت کے اعتبار سے بہت بڑا تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے جانور کو کپڑوں پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہو گا اور حدیث عمرو بن العاص میں ایک اونٹ کو دو اونٹوں کے عوض خرید نا آیت ربوا نازل ہونے سے پہلے کا حکم ہے آیت ربوا سے یہ حکم منسوخ ہو گیا ہے اور حدیث منسوخ چونکہ قابل استدلال نہیں ہوتی اسلئے اس حدیث سے استدلال کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ حدیث چونکہ سے نہ ہماری طرف سے نقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حیوان کی بیع سلم سے منع فرمایا ہے اور لفظ حیوان میں اس کے تمام اجناس داخل ہو جائیں گے ۔ حتیٰ کہ کبوتر اور گوریئے بھی داخل ہو جائیں گے یعنی کبوتر اور چڑیا جیسے جانورں کی بیع سلم بھی اس نص کی وجہ سے جائز نہ ہوگی اگر چہ ان کے افراد میں زیادہ تفاوت نہیں ہوتا۔
There are hidden matters due to which the price of one is very high and the other low. So due to these hidden matters, at the time of delivery of the subject matter, a dispute will arise, and any contract in which there is possibility of dispute is a invalid contract. Therefore we said that salam sale of animals is impermissible and invalid. And Imam Shafi'i's analogy of animals to cloth is not correct. Because cloth is made by servants, and when servants weave two pieces from the same thread and same tool in the same style, there is very little difference in value. But in the creation of animals, servants have no role; rather Allah the Exalted by His power creates two animals of the same species, and there is a great difference in their value. So given this difference, how can analogizing animals to cloth be correct? And the hadith of Amr ibn al-As about buying one camel for two camels is a ruling from before the revelation of the verses on riba; that ruling was abrogated by the riba verses. Since an abrogated hadith is not admissible as evidence, using this hadith as evidence is not correct. The hadith from us is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade salam sale of animals, and the word 'animal' includes all its species, even pigeons and sparrows. That is, salam sale of birds like pigeons and sparrows is also not permissible due to this text, even though there is not much variation among their individuals.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that salam in animals is invalid. The reasoning is that animals have hidden qualities that cause significant price variation, leading to disputes at delivery. Any contract prone to dispute is invalid (fasid). The commentary refutes Imam Shafi'i's analogy (qiyas) to cloth, arguing that cloth is manufactured by humans and thus uniform, while animals are created by Allah with inherent variation. Additionally, the hadith of Amr ibn al-As allowing camel exchange is abrogated by the riba verses. The primary Hanafi proof is the Prophet's prohibition of salam in animals, which covers all animal species including birds.

Key Terms
مسلم فیہ (muslim fihi): The subject matter of a salam contract that is to be delivered in the future.
تفاوت (tafawut): Variation in quality or value that leads to uncertainty and potential dispute.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning applied by Shafi'i to extend ruling from cloth to animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider salam in animals invalid?
A) Because animals cannot be delivered in the future.
B) Because hidden variations in animals cause disputes at delivery.
C) Because the Prophet forbade selling animals altogether.
D) Because animals are not measurable by weight or volume.

Key Takeaway
Salam in animals is invalid in the Hanafi school because of excessive hidden variation, and the Shafi'i analogy to cloth is rejected due to the difference in cause (human control vs. divine creation).

Salam in Numerically Varying Items: Animal Parts, Hides, Bundles, and Fodder
States rulings on salam in various items and conditions for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in numerically varying items and identify the condition that makes salam valid in such items.

Core Idea
Salam in items with significant variation and no standard measure is invalid unless the variation is removed by specification.

In the previous lesson, we learned that salam requires a fully specified subject matter. This lesson extends that principle to items like animal heads, hides, firewood bundles, and fodder bunches—items that are counted but vary greatly in size and value. The passage from al-Hidayah explains why these are invalid and the narrow exception that allows salam when the variation is eliminated through specification of a standard measure, such as the length of the tying rope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and their default ruling
List the four categories of items that are ruled invalid for salam: animal extremities (heads, feet), hides (by number), firewood (by bundle), and fodder (by bunch). The default ruling is that salam in these is invalid (fasid).
The invalidity is not due to the item being non-existent but due to excessive variation.
2
Understand the cause (illah) of invalidity
The cause is 'tafawut' (variation) combined with 'adadi mutafawit' (numerically varying with no standard measure). Such items lead to dispute (mufdi ila al-munaza'ah) at delivery because the precise quantity/value cannot be determined upfront.
This is a core Hanafi principle: contracts that inevitably lead to dispute are invalid.
3
Recognize the exception
The text states that if the variation is removed by specifying the length of the rope used to tie bundles (e.g., one span or one cubit), then salam becomes valid, provided the bundles are uniform. This shows that specification of a standard measure can cure the uncertainty.
The exception applies only if the specification eliminates all significant variation.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute on hides
Imam Malik allows salam in hides by weight because hides are deliverable and knowable by weight. The Hanafi school rejects this because hides are not customarily weighed; they are sold by number, and as numerically varying items, salam is invalid even if weight is specified.
The Hanafi reliance on custom (urf) is decisive here.
