Salam in Salted Fish: Conditions and Ruling
Ruling with proof on conditions for salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid salam in salted fish and apply them to distinguish valid from invalid contracts.

Core Idea
Salam in salted fish requires known weight and type; count is invalid due to value disparity.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a special contract that requires the subject matter to be precisely defined to avoid uncertainty. This passage from Al-Hidayah examines its application to salted fish. You will learn why specifying weight and type makes the contract valid, while specifying by count makes it invalid because individual fish differ in value. Understanding this ruling will help you grasp the broader Hanafi condition that salam goods must be known in quantity, description, and deliverable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal status of salam in salted fish when done by known weight and known type? The text states it is permissible (ja'iz). When done by count? It is not permissible (la yajuz).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
What three reasons are given for permissibility? The fish is known in quantity (by weight), well-defined in description (by type), and deliverable (since it is always available). These remove uncertainty.
The proof is a talil (reasoning), not a direct textual source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each condition contribute to validity? Weight removes ambiguity about how much; type removes ambiguity about what kind; continuous availability ensures the seller can deliver. Together they eliminate gharar (excessive uncertainty).
4
Analyze the prohibition by count
Why is count invalid? Because fish individuals are disparate (mutafawit) in size and value, so specifying a number (e.g., 100 fish) does not define the quantity adequately—leading to jahl (ignorance) and potential dispute.
This is a crucial distinction: count is valid only when items are uniform (like currency or eggs).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that salam in salted fish is permissible with known weight and type, and impermissible by count. This is the standard view in the Hanafi school.
This ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is consistent across the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز السلم في السمك المالح وزنا معلوما وضربا معلوما لانه معلوم القدر مضبوط الوصف مقدور التسليم اذ هو غير منقطع ولا يجوز السلم فيه عددا للتفاوت
ترجمہ اور نمک آلودہ مچھلی میں وزن معلوم اور قسم معلوم کے ساتھ بیع سلم جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی مقدار معلوم ہے ، صفت منضبط ہے اس کا سپر د کر نا قدرت میں ہے اسلئے کہ یہ منقطع نہیں ہوتی ہے اور اس نمک آلودہ مچھلی میں گنتی کے ساتھ بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے افراد متفاوت ہوتے ہیں۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مچھلی اگر نمک آلودہ ہو تو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہے بشرطیکہ اس کا وزن معلوم ہو اور اس کی نوع بیان کر دی گئی ہو۔ کیونکہ وزن بیان کرنے سے اس کی مقدار معلوم ہوگئی ہے اور نوع بیان کرنے سے اس کا وصف منضبط اور معلوم ہو گیا ہے۔ اور نمک آلودہ مچھلی چونکہ ہر زمانے میں دستیاب ہو جاتی ہے کبھی بازار سے منقطع نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے مسلم الیہ کو اس کے سپرد کرنے پر قدرت بھی حاصل ہے اور جس چیز کی مقدار معلوم ہو اور اس کا وصف منضبط ہو اور اس کے سپرد کرنے پر قدرت ہو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے نمک آلودہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم ، وزن معلوم اور قسم معلوم کے ساتھ جائز ہے لیکن اگر نمک آلودہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم گنتی سے کی گئی مثلا مسلم فیہ ایک سو مچھلی قرار دی گئی تو اس صورت میں بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اسلئے کہ مچھلی کے افراد میں مالیت کے اعتبار سے بہت بڑا تفاوت ہوتا ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ جن چیزوں کے افراد متفاوت ہوتے ہیں ان کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہوتی ۔ اسلئے گنتی سے نمک آلودہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔
He said: Salam in salted fish with known weight and known type is permissible, because it is known in quantity, well-defined in description, possible to deliver, as it is not intermittent. And salam in it is not permissible by count due to disparity. Translation: And salam sale in salted fish with known weight and known type is permissible. Because its quantity is known, its description is well-defined, it is possible to deliver, because it is not intermittent. And salam in salted fish by count is not permissible, because its individuals are disparate. Explanation: The issue is that if fish is salted, then salam sale of it is permissible provided its weight is known and its type is stated. Because by stating weight its quantity becomes known, and by stating type its description becomes well-defined and known. And since salted fish is available at all times, never absent from the market, so the seller (muslam ilayh) has the ability to deliver it. And anything whose quantity is known, description well-defined, and ability to deliver exists, its salam sale is permissible. Therefore, salam in salted fish with known weight and known type is permissible. But if salam in salted fish is done by count, e.g., the subject matter is one hundred fish, then it is not permissible. Because fish individuals have great disparity in value, and it has passed earlier that things whose individuals are disparate, salam in them is not permissible. Hence salam in salted fish by count is not permissible.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Hidayah on salam in salted fish. The ruling states that salam (advance payment sale) in salted fish is valid only if the fish is specified by known weight and known type. The proof (talil) provided is threefold: (1) its quantity is known through weight, (2) its description is well-defined through type, and (3) it is deliverable because salted fish is always available and never runs out of the market. If these conditions are met, the contract is valid. However, if salam is specified by count (e.g., one hundred fish), it is invalid because individual fish vary greatly in size and value, leading to uncertainty (jahl) and potential dispute. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that salam requires the subject matter to be known in quantity, description, and deliverable. The commentary emphasizes that salted fish is continuously available, unlike fresh fish which may be seasonal. The key takeaway is that specification by weight and type removes ambiguity.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A sale with advance payment where the price is paid immediately and the goods are delivered later.
وزنا معلوما (waznan ma'luman): Specification by a known weight, removing ambiguity about quantity.
عددا (adadan): Specification by count, which is not allowed if the individuals are disparate.
متفاوت (mutafawit): Disparate individuals, differing in value, leading to uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because weight is more accurate than count.
B) Because fish individuals are disparate in value, causing uncertainty (jahl).
C) Because salted fish cannot be counted easily.
D) Because the contract requires the price to be known.

Key Takeaway
Salam in salted fish requires known weight and type to eliminate gharar; count is invalid because individuals are disparate.

Salam in Fresh Fish
Ruling on salam in fresh fish with talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid salam in fresh fish and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding large fish meat.

Core Idea
Salam in fresh fish is valid only in its season with known weight and type, or if the fish is always available.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the conditions for salam in fresh fish, focusing on the seasonal availability and the requirement of weight over count. It also records an additional view from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding large fish meat, based on analogy with meat salam. Understanding these conditions protects the contract from gharar (uncertainty) in delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the transaction being discussed? What is its default ruling?
Salam in fresh fish is permissible only conditionally.
2
Locate the conditional ruling
When is salam in fresh fish permissible? Identify the conditions: season, known weight, known type.
The exception: if in a place where fish never becomes intermittent, it is absolutely permissible.
3
Identify the dalil (reason)
Why is the seasonal condition imposed? The text says 'because it becomes intermittent in winter.' That is the effective cause (illa).
The illa is unavailability; if the illa is absent (always available), the restriction lifts.
4
Note the requirement of weight over count
Why must it be by weight, not by count? Because fish vary in size and value, creating uncertainty.
This was mentioned in a previous passage.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
What is Abu Hanifa's additional view? He disallows salam in the meat of large fish (cut pieces) by analogy with meat salam. Who disagrees?
The matn does not adopt this view; it is a riwaya. The two students likely allow it if described.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا خير في السلم في السمك الطرى الا فى حينه وزناً معلوماً وضرباً معلوماً لانه ينقطع في زمان الشتاء حتى لو كان في بلد لا ينقطع يجوز مطلقا وانما يجوز وزنا لا عددا لما ذكرنا وعن ابي حنيفة انه لا يجوز في لحم الكبار منها وهى التي تُقطع اعتبارا بالسلم في اللحم عنده
ترجمہ اور تازہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم میں کچھ بھلائی نہیں ہے مگر اس کے زمانے میں وزن معلوم اور نوع معلوم کے ساتھ ۔ کیونکہ تازہ مچھلی کی آمد سردی کے زمانے میں منقطع ہو جاتی ہے حتی کہ اگر عاقد ایسے شہر میں ہو جہاں تازہ مچھلی منقطع نہیں ہوتی تو مطلقاً جائز ہے۔ اور وزن کے ساتھ جائز ہے نہ کہ گنتی سے، اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ تازہ بڑی مچھلیوں کے گوشت میں سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور بڑی مچھلیاں وہ ہیں جو کاٹ کر ( فروخت کی جاتی ہیں ) ۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک گوشت کی بیع سلم پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے۔
تشریح امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ تازہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم اس کے موسم میں جائز ہے۔ بشرطیکہ اس کا وزن معلوم ہو اور نوع معلوم ہو لیکن بے موسم جائز نہیں ہے یعنی جس زمانہ میں تازہ مچھلیوں کی آمد برابر ہوتی ہے اگر اس زمانہ میں کسی خاص قسم کی مچھلی کو وزن معلوم کے ساتھ مسلم فیہ قرار دیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں مسلم ایک مسلم فیہ سپر د کرنے پر قادر ہے اور اب موسم میں اس لئے نا جائز ہے کہ مثلا سردی کے زمانہ میں پانی خشک ہو جانے کی وجہ سے مچھلیوں کی آمد بند ہو جاتی ہے، پس اگر سردی کے زمانہ میں مچھلی کی بیع سلم کی گئی تو چونکہ عقد کے وقت سے لے کر ادا ئیگی کے وقت تک مسلم فیہ موجود ہونے کی شرط فوت ہو گئی اور مسلم فیہ مقدور التسلیم نہ رہی اس لئے بے موسم بیع سلم نا جائز ہے۔ ہاں! اگر عاقدین ایسے ملک میں ہوں جہاں تازہ مچھلیاں کبھی منقطع نہیں ہوتیں بلکہ ہر زمانہ میں ان کی آمد ہوتی ہے تو وہاں ہر زمانہ میں تازہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ خیال رہے کہ تازہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم بھی وزن کے ساتھ تو جائز ہے لیکن گفتی سے جائز نہیں ہے اور اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے کہ مچھلی کے افراد چھوٹے بڑے ہونے کی وجہ سے مالیت میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں اور جس چیز کے افراد مالیت میں متفاوت ہوں اس کی بیع سلم عددا جائز نہیں ہے۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ تازہ بڑی مچھلیوں کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اور بڑی مچھلیاں وہ کہلاتی ہیں جن کو کاٹ کر فروخت کیا جاتا ہے۔ امام صاحب کی اس روایت کی دلیل قیاس ہے، یعنی جس طرح بکری وغیرہ کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح بڑی مچھلیاں جن کو کاٹ کر فروخت کیا جاتا ہے ان کی بیع سلم بھی جائز نہیں۔ اور ملت جامعہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح بکری وغیرہ کا گوشت چربی دارو غیر چربی دار ہونے کی وجہ سے مختلف ہوتا ہے اس طرح مچھلی کا گوشت بھی مختلف ہوتا ہے۔
He said: There is no good in salam in fresh fish except in its season, with known weight and known type, because it becomes intermittent in winter; even if it is in a place where it does not become intermittent, it is permissible absolutely. And it is permissible by weight, not by count, for the reason we have mentioned. And from Abu Hanifa: that it is not permissible in the meat of large ones, which are those cut (sold in pieces), by analogy with salam in meat according to him. (Urdu translation and commentary similarly explain the ruling, the seasonal condition, the permissibility by weight, and the analogy from Abu Hanifa regarding large fish meat being impermissible like meat.)
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on salam (advance payment sale) in fresh fish, with two main points: (1) The general ruling: salam in fresh fish is not permissible except in its season (when fish are plentiful) and only if specified by known weight and type. The reason (talil) is that fresh fish becomes unavailable (intermittent) in winter, making delivery uncertain. However, if the locality always has fresh fish (e.g., a coastal area with year-round supply), then salam is permissible at all times. (2) An additional view from Imam Abu Hanifa: he ruled that salam in the meat of large fresh fish (that are cut and sold in pieces) is not permissible, by analogy (qiyas) with the prohibition of salam in meat (of land animals) altogether. The commentary from Imam Muhammad in Al-Jami' al-Saghir clarifies the seasonal condition and the analogy. The passage also repeats that weight is required, not count, due to disparity. This ruling protects against uncertainty in delivery and quality.

Key Terms
السمك الطرى (al-samak al-tari): Fresh fish, as opposed to salted or preserved fish.
ينقطع (yanqati'): Becomes intermittent or unavailable; a condition that affects the validity of salam.
حينه (hinihi): Its season, the time when fresh fish is plentiful and available.
لحم الكبار (lahm al-kibar): Meat of large fish, sold cut in pieces, analogous to meat of land animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is salam in fresh fish permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only in winter when fish is scarce.
B) Only in its season and with known weight and type.
C) At any time if specified by count.
D) Only if the fish is large and cut.

Key Takeaway
Salam in fresh fish is valid only when the fish is available (season or continuous region) and specified by weight and type; the seasonal condition is based on the effective cause of intermittent supply.

Salam in Meat: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Students
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in meat with proofs and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on salam in meat, explain their proofs, and identify the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Salam in meat is impermissible in the Hanafi school because uncertainty in bone and fat cannot be resolved by description.

Salam (advance payment sale) requires precise description of the subject matter to avoid future disputes. Meat, however, varies in bone, fat, and seasonal condition. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa deems salam in meat impermissible, while his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, allow it if the meat is properly described. Understanding their proofs and the final tarjih will sharpen your ability to apply the principle of gharar in contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the disputed ruling: Is salam (advance payment sale) in meat permissible? Locate the explicit statements: Abu Hanifa says 'لا خير' (no good, i.e., impermissible), and the Sahibayn say it is permissible if a known part is described with a known description.
The Arabic 'لا خير' in Hanafi fiqh often indicates prohibition or severe dislike, rendering the contract invalid.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that meat is weighable (mawzūn) and can be well-defined by description, making it suitable for salam. They support this by noting that meat is guaranteed by weight (yudmanu bi al-mithl), can be borrowed by weight, and riba al-fadl applies – all indicators that weight eliminates uncertainty.
They distinguish bird meat, which cannot have a specified part described.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that meat is inherently unknown (majhūl) due to variation in bone quantity, fat content across seasons, and other factors. This excessive uncertainty (jahl) leads to disputes, making salam invalid. He refutes the Sahibayn's claim that weight eliminates uncertainty, stating that description alone cannot capture the variability.
This is a qiyās khafī (subtle analogy) – the ruling is derived from the principle that gharar fāhish invalidates contracts.
4
Examine the special case of deboned meat
The text mentions deboned meat (makhlu' al-'azm) separately, stating that it is not permissible according to the second view (Abu Hanifa's), which is the more correct (al-asahh). This reinforces that even without bones, the variation in fat and other qualities remains problematic.
This indicates that the bone issue is not the sole cause; the essential uncertainty persists.
5
Identify the tarjih and thamarah al-khilaf
The text declares the second view (Abu Hanifa's) as al-asahh (more correct), meaning the relied-upon view for fatwa. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, salam in meat is invalid; under the Sahibayn, it would be valid with proper description. The school adopts impermissibility.
Thamarah al-khilaf: the ruling that a contract made under the Sahibayn's view would be fasid (defective) according to the muftā bihī view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا خير في السلم في اللحم عند ابي حنيفة وقالا اذا وصف من اللحم موضعا معلوما بصفة معلومة جاز لانه موزون مضبوط الوصف ولهذا يُضمن بالمثل ويجوز استقراضه وزنا ويجرى فيه ربوا الفضل بخلاف لحم الطيور لانه لا يجوز وصف موضع منه وله انه مجهول للتفاوت فى قلة العظم وكثرته أو في سمنه وهر اله على اختلاف فصول السنة وهذه الجهالة مفضية الى المنازعة وفى مخلوع العظم لا يجوز على الوجه الثانى وهو الأصح والتضمين بالمثل ممنوع وكذا الاستقراض وبعد التسليم فالمثل اعدل من القيمة ولان القبض يعاين فيعرف مثل المقبوض به فى وقته اما الوصف فلا يكتفى به
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک گوشت کی بیع سلم میں کوئی بھلائی نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اگر گوشت کی معلوم جگہ ، صفت معلومہ کے ساتھ بیان کی ہو تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ گوشت وزنی ( اور ) وصف سے منضبط ہے اور اسی وجہ سے گوشت بالمثل مضمون ہوتا ہے اور وزان سے اس کا قرض لینا جائز ہے، اور ربوا الفضل جاری ہوتا ہے، برخلاف پرندوں کے گوشت کے کیونکہ پرند میں سے کسی جگہ کا بیان کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوشت ہڈی کے کم اور زیادہ ہونے کی وجہ سے یا سال کی مختلف فصلوں میں جانور کے مونا[؟]
He said: There is no good in salam in meat according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two students) said: If a known part of meat is described with a known description, it is permissible, because it is weighed, well-defined in description, and therefore it is guaranteed by weight, it is permissible to borrow it by weight, and riba al-fadl applies to it, unlike the meat of birds because it is not possible to describe a part of it. And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument: that it is unknown due to disparity in the amount of bone and its excess, or in its fatness and leanness according to the different seasons, and this ignorance leads to dispute. And in the case of meat with bone removed, it is not permissible according to the second (view), which is the more correct. And the guarantee by weight is denied, as is borrowing. And after delivery, the weight equivalent is more just than value, and because possession (qabd) is seen and the equivalent of that taken is known at its time, but description is not sufficient. (Urdu translation similarly explains the views.)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute concerning salam (advance payment sale) in meat. The ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that salam in meat is not permissible (no good in it). His reasoning is based on the inherent uncertainty (jahl) in meat: the amount of bone varies, the fat content varies with seasons, making it impossible to describe accurately. Such uncertainty leads to disputes. In contrast, the two students (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that if the meat is described by specifying a known part (e.g., a leg or shoulder) with a known description (e.g., size, weight), then it is permissible. Their proof is that meat is a weighed commodity with a well-defined description; it is guaranteed by weight (damān bi al-mithl), borrowing by weight is allowed, and riba al-fadl applies, all indicating that weight eliminates uncertainty. They distinguish meat from bird meat, which cannot be described because of varying parts. Abu Hanifa's refutation includes that descriptions cannot capture the variability, and the claim of guarantee by weight is contested. Regarding deboned meat (mukhlu' al-'azm), the text says it is not permissible according to the second (more correct) view (probably the view of Abu Hanifa). The final relied-upon position (al-asahh) is that salam in meat is impermissible, following Abu Hanifa. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of istidlal using qiyas and the principle of avoiding excessive uncertainty (gharar).

Key Terms
اللحم (al-lahm): Meat of land animals, considered here as a subject matter for salam.
يضمن بالمثل (yudmanu bi al-mithl): Guaranteed by weight equivalent; if damaged, the guarantor must return an equivalent weight of the same quality.
مخلوع العظم (makhlu' al-'azm): Deboned meat (meat from which bones are removed).
الأصح (al-asahh): The more correct view, the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, is salam in meat permissible?
A) Yes, if the part and description are specified.
B) No, it is not permissible due to uncertainty.
C) Yes, because meat is weighed and well-defined.
D) It depends on the season.

Key Takeaway
Salam in meat is impermissible in the Hanafi school because the inherent uncertainty in bone, fat, and seasonal condition cannot be eliminated by description, and this ruling is the relied-upon position.

Salam in Fresh Fish: Conditions of Season and Weight
Ruling on salam in fresh fish with conditions and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid salam contract in fresh fish and distinguish between permissible and impermissible scenarios based on season, weight, and count.

Core Idea
Salam in fresh fish is valid only when in season, weight and type known; out-of-season or by count is invalid due to uncertainty.

Salam (forward sale) is a special contract where payment is made in advance for a commodity to be delivered later. This lesson examines the specific ruling on salam in fresh fish as derived from Imam Muhammad's Jami' al-Saghir and explained in Al-Hidayah. The key is that the muslam fihi (the commodity) must be available and measurable with certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the basic ruling is according to Imam Muhammad. Subject: salam in fresh fish. Ruling: permissible only in season with known weight and type.
This sets the baseline.
2
List the conditions for validity
Extract the three conditions: (1) fish must be in season (naturally abundant), (2) weight must be specified, (3) type (species) must be specified. Out of season invalid because fish may not exist at delivery.
Also note the exception: if fish are available year-round in a particular country, season condition is waived.
3
Distinguish between weight and count
Understand why salam by weight is acceptable but by count is not: individual fish vary in size and value, so counting leads to uncertainty (gharar). The proof: it has been established that salam is not valid for goods whose individual units differ in value when sold by count.
Weight eliminates that uncertainty.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that prohibits salam in large fish meat (cut and sold). This is based on qiyas to goat meat, where variation in fat content causes uncertainty. Compare this to the general position (Imam Muhammad) which permits salam in fish by weight and in season.
This shows the Hanafi school's careful treatment of different types of fish.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Identify which ruling is operative for fatwa. The Hidayah upholds permissibility with conditions (weight, season, type). The narration from Abu Hanifa is noted but not actively adopted, thus the mufta bihi is the general permissibility.
Be aware of the ikhtilaf for large fish; caution may be advised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابی سلم پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ تازہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم اس کے موسم میں جانتا ہے۔ بشرطیکہ اس کا وزن معلوم ہو اور نوع معلوم ہولیکن بے موسم جائز نہیں ہے یعنی جس زمانہ میں تازہ مچھلیوں کی آمد برابر ہوتی ہے اگر اس زمانہ میں کسی خاص قسم کی مچھلی کو وزن معلوم کے ساتھ مسلم فیہ خبر ایا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں مسلم ایک مسلم فیہ سپر د کرنے پر قادر ہے اور اب موسم میں اس لئے نا جائز ہے کہ مثلا سردی کے زمانہ میں پانی خشک ہو جانے کی وجہ سے مچھلیوں کی آمد بند ہو جاتی ہے، پس اگر سردی کے زمانہ میں مچھلی کی بیع سلم کی گئی تو چونکہ عقد کے وقت سے لے کر ادا ئیگی کے وقت تک مسلم فیہ موجود ہونے کی شرط فوت ہو گئی اور مسلم فیہ مقدور التسلیم نہ رہی اس لئے بے موسم بیع سلم نا جائز ہے۔ ہاں! اگر عاقدین ایسے ملک میں ہوں جہاں تازہ مچھلیاں کبھی منقطع نہیں ہوتیں بلکہ ہر زمانہ میں ان کی آمد ہوتی ہے تو وہاں ہر زمانہ میں تازہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ خیال رہے کہ تازہ مچھلی کی بیع سلم بھی وزن کے ساتھ تو جائز ہے لیکن گفتی سے جائز نہیں ہے اور اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے کہ مچھلی کے افراد چھوٹے بڑے ہونے کی وجہ سے مالیت میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں اور جس چیز کے افراد مالیت میں متفاوت ہوں اس کی بیع سلم عددا جائز نہیں ہے۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ تازہ بڑی مچھلیوں کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اور بڑی مچھلیاں وہ کہلاتی ہیں جن کو کاٹ کر فروخت کیا جاتا ہے۔ امام صاحب کی اس روایت کی دلیل قیاس ہے، یعنی جس طرح بکری وغیرہ کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح بڑی مچھلیاں جن کو کاٹ کر فروخت کیا جاتا ہے ان کی بیع سلم بھی جائز نہیں۔ اور ملت جامعہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح بکری وغیرہ کا گوشت چربی دارو غیر چربی دار ہونے کی وجہ سے مختلف ہوتا ہے اس طرح مچھلی کا گوشت بھی مختلف ہوتا ہے۔
It is analogized to salam. Explanation: Imam Muhammad said in Jami' al-Saghir that salam in fresh fish is known in its season, provided its weight is known and its type is known. But out of season it is not permissible. That is, in a time when fresh fish are regularly available, if in that time a specific type of fish with known weight is made the muslam fihi, it is permissible because in that case the one paying the price is able to deliver the muslam fihi. Out of season it is not permissible because, for example, in winter due to water drying up, the arrival of fish stops. So if salam in fish is done in winter, then since the condition of the existence of the muslam fihi from the time of contract to the time of delivery is lost and the muslam fihi is not capable of delivery, out of season salam is not permissible. Yes, if the contracting parties are in a country where fresh fish never cease but are available at all times, then there salam in fresh fish is permissible in all seasons. The author of Hidayah says: It should be noted that salam in fresh fish with weight is permissible, but with count is not permissible, and its proof has passed earlier: that individual fish differ in value due to being small or big, and salam by count is not permissible for something whose individuals differ in value. A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa: Salam in the meat of fresh large fish is not permissible, and large fish are those that are cut and sold. The proof of this narration of Imam is analogy, i.e., just as salam in the meat of goat etc. is not permissible, similarly salam in large fish that are cut and sold is not permissible. And the collective opinion is that just as the meat of goat etc. differs due to being fatty or non-fatty, similarly the meat of fish differs.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on salam in fresh fish with proof from Imam Muhammad and the Hidayah. It explains that salam in fresh fish is permissible only when the fish are in season (i.e., available naturally) and their weight and type are known. Out of season, it is invalid because the muslam fihi may not exist at delivery time. The Hidayah adds that even in season, salam must be by weight, not by count, because fish differ in size and value. Finally, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits salam in large fish that are sold cut, analogizing it to meat where such salam is invalid due to variation in fat content. This shows the Hanafi school's careful treatment of uncertainty in salam contracts.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for a specified commodity delivered later.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The commodity that is subject to the salam contract, to be delivered at a future date.
موسم (mausam): Season when the commodity (fish) is naturally available and abundant.
وزن (wazn): Weight, a measure that eliminates uncertainty in salam contracts.
عددا (adadan): Count, a method of quantifying goods that is insufficient for salam when individual units vary in value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following scenarios is salam in fresh fish valid according to Imam Muhammad?
A) In winter when fish are scarce, but weight is known
B) In summer when fish are abundant, but only the count is specified
C) In the fish season, weight and type are specified
D) In any season as long as the fish is described generally

Key Takeaway
Salam in fresh fish is valid only when in season, with known weight and type; out-of-season or by count invalidates the contract.

Salam in Meat: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in meat with proofs and counter-proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on salam in meat and explain the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Core Idea
Meat's variability makes salam invalid according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn accept it if fully described.

This passage presents a classic intra-madhhab ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples disagree on whether salam (advance sale) in meat is valid. The disagreement hinges on whether meat can be specified sufficiently to avoid uncertainty (jihalah). Understanding this dispute illuminates how different assessments of a commodity's measurability lead to differing rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
In the source, Imam Abu Hanifa says 'la khayr' (no good) while the Sahibayn allow it with proper description. Identify both positions clearly.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue meat is mawzoon (weighed) and mazbut al-wasf (fixed in description). They support this with evidence: meat is compensable by like, borrowing by weight is valid, and riba al-fadl applies. Understand why these indicate measurability.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof and response
Abu Hanifa argues meat varies in bone, fat, and season — creating jihalah leading to disputes. The Sahibayn's evidence is countered: compensation by like and borrowing are not proven for meat. See how he responds to each of their points.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah)
The ruling difference: if a salam contract in meat is made, Abu Hanifa would invalidate it (fasid), while the Sahibayn would consider it valid with proper description. Also, note the ruling for de-boned meat.

The ruling on salam in meat... Statements of the jurists: He said: There is no good in salam in meat according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If a known place of the meat is described with a known description, it is permissible, because it is weighed and the description is fixed, and for this reason it is guaranteed by like measure, and borrowing it by weight is permissible, and riba al-fadl applies therein, unlike the meat of birds because it is not possible to describe a place from it. And for him (Abu Hanifa): It is unknown due to variation in the smallness and largeness of bone, or in its fatness and leanness according to the different seasons of the year, and this ignorance leads to dispute. And in the case of de-boned meat, it is not permissible on the second basis, and that is the most sound. And compensation by like measure is prohibited, and likewise borrowing. And after delivery (the reply is that) like measure is more equitable than value, and because possession is witnessed, so the like of the received item is known at its time. As for description, it is not relied upon.
Translation: According to Abu Hanifa, there is no good in salam in meat. And the Sahibayn said: If a known place of meat is described with a known description, it is permissible, because meat is weighed and fixed in description, and for this reason meat is guaranteed by like measure, and borrowing it by weight is permissible, and riba al-fadl applies, unlike the meat of birds because it is not possible to describe any place from a bird. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that meat varies due to the less or more of bone, or due to the different seasons of the year, the animal's fat or leanness, and this ignorance leads to dispute. And in de-boned meat, salam is not permissible on the second basis, and this narration is more correct. And compensation by like measure is prohibited, and likewise borrowing by weight is prohibited. And after delivery (the reply is that) like measure is more equitable than value, and because possession is witnessed, so the like of the received item is known at its time. As for description, it is not relied upon.
Explanation: To express the non-permissibility of salam in meat, Imam Abu Hanifa used the word 'la khayr' instead of the general word 'la yajuz'. Allamah Badr al-Din al-'Ayni writes two reasons for this. One is that Imam's purpose is to express non-permissibility in a hyperbolic manner, and 'la khayr' has hyperbole because 'khayr' is indefinite and falls under negation, and an indefinite under negation gives generality, so 'la khayr' by its generality negates all kinds of good, meaning there is no good in salam in meat, and this hyperbole is apparent. The second reason is that when a mujtahid derives a ruling by his own opinion, if it involves non-permissibility he says 'la khayr', and if it involves permissibility he says 'la ba's', and his purpose is to avoid giving a decisive and certain verdict in divine rulings. In any case, the issue of salam in meat is disputed. Thus, Imam Abu Hanifa holds non-permissibility, and the Sahibayn said: If the rabb al-salam specifies the genus, type, place of meat, and its description, it is permissible. For example, if he says: 'Two mans of meat from the thigh or chest of a fat, fresh, castrated two-year-old goat is the muslam fihi', then it is permissible.
The proof of the Sahibayn is that meat in common custom is weighed, i.e., the buying and selling of meat is by weight, and by mentioning the genus, type, and place of meat, its description becomes fixed. So when meat is weighed and its description is fixed, then its delivery is not impossible but possible. And the salam of a thing that is capable of delivery is permissible, so salam in meat is permissible. And because meat is weighed and fixed in description, if someone destroys someone's meat, he must pay compensation with the like weight. And borrowing meat by weight is permissible, and if meat is sold in exchange for the same kind of meat with an increase, that increase is haram and riba, and the cause of riba is weight with same genus. In any case, it is established that meat is a weighed thing, and by mentioning genus, type, and place like chest or thigh, its description becomes fixed and known. And a thing that is weighed and fixed in description is not impossible to deliver but possible, and salam in a thing that is within the power of the muslam ilayh to deliver is permissible. Therefore salam in meat is permissible. Yes, salam in the meat of birds is not permissible. The reason for non-permissibility is that birds have very little meat, so it is not possible to specify a place, like saying the meat is from the chest or something. And in the case of quadrupeds, because it is possible, salam in their meat is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa gave two reasons for non-permissibility. One reason is that meat varies due to the less or more bones, so it is unknown. The second reason is that meat varies according to seasons; in winter meat is fat and fresh, in summer and rainy season it is not as fat but lean. Due to this variation and difference, the muslam fihi is unknown. And in both mentioned cases...
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of salam (advance sale) in meat. The core disagreement is whether meat can be specified sufficiently to avoid uncertainty (jihalah). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it cannot, because meat differs in the amount of bone, fat content, and quality across seasons, leading to potential disputes. Therefore, he uses the emphatic phrase 'la khayr' (there is no good) to indicate strong disapproval bordering on prohibition. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow salam in meat provided the seller describes the genus (e.g., goat, cow), type (e.g., mutton), specific part (e.g., thigh, chest), and condition (e.g., fat, two-year-old). They argue that meat is a weighed commodity (mawzoon) and can be well-described, making it possible to deliver without uncertainty. They further support their view by noting that meat is subject to compensation by like weight (ta'diya bi al-mithl), borrowing by weight is valid, and riba al-fadl applies, all of which indicate it is a precisely measurable good. The Hidayah then notes that for de-boned meat (makhlu' al-'azm), the more correct view is non-permissibility, as the bone variation is eliminated but other uncertainties remain. The commentary also explains why Imam Abu Hanifa used 'la khayr' instead of 'la yajuz': either for hyperbole or to avoid giving a definitive ruling on Allah's laws.

Key Terms
لا خير (la khayr): There is no good; a phrase used by Imam Abu Hanifa to indicate strong disapproval or prohibition without claiming certainty.
موزون (mawzoon): A commodity sold by weight; meat is an example.
مضبوط الوصف (mazbut al-wasf): Fixed or well-defined in description, such that uncertainty is removed.
ضمان بالمثل (damān bi al-mithl): Compensation by delivering the same kind and measure (like weight) of the damaged item.
ربوا الفضل (ribā al-faḍl): Riba in exchange of like commodities with a surplus; applicable to weighed items of the same genus.
مخلوع العظم (makhlu' al-'azm): De-boned meat.
جہالت (jihālah): Uncertainty or ignorance about the subject matter that can lead to disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is salam in meat not permissible?
A) Because meat is not a weighed commodity
B) Because meat varies in bone and fat content across seasons, causing uncertainty
C) Because the Sahibayn prohibited it
D) Because it leads to litigation

Key Takeaway
The validity of salam in meat depends on whether jihalah is unavoidable; Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on this assessment.

The Choice of 'La Khayr' – Methodological Significance
Explanation of the phrase 'la khayr' and its methodological implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two reasons why Imam Abu Hanifa used 'la khayr' instead of 'la yajuz' for salam in meat.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa's use of 'la khayr' reflects either rhetorical hyperbole or a conscious avoidance of certainty in ijtihad.

In expressing his position on salam in meat, Imam Abu Hanifa did not use the common phrase 'la yajuz' (it is not permissible) but instead said 'la khayr' (there is no good). This choice is not arbitrary; it carries methodological weight. The commentators explain two possible reasons: one rhetorical, one epistemological. Understanding this deepens our grasp of how imams framed their rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its context
Locate where Imam Abu Hanifa says 'la khayr' and note the alternative phrase he could have used. The source states: 'He said: There is no good in salam in meat'.
2
Understand the first reason: hyperbole
'Khayr' is an indefinite noun under negation, which implies generality: no good at all. This emphasizes strong disapproval. Badr al-Din al-'Ayni's explanation: 'la khayr' by its generality negates all kinds of good, showing hyperbole.
3
Understand the second reason: avoiding certainty
When a mujtahid derives a ruling by personal reasoning (ijtihad), he may avoid absolute language to acknowledge the possibility of error. 'La khayr' avoids claiming shari'ah certainty. Similarly, 'la ba's' is used for permissible rulings.
4
Apply to other contexts
Identify other places in Hanafi fiqh where similar expressions like 'la ba's' (no harm) are used for permissibility. This shows a consistent method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گوشت کی بیع سلم کا حکم ... اقوال فقہاء 
 قال ولا خير في السلم في اللحم عند ابي حنيفة وقالا اذا وصف من اللحم موضعا معلوما بصفة معلومة جاز لانه موزون مضبوط الوصف ولهذا يُضمن بالمثل ويجوز استقراضه وزنا ويجرى فيه ربوا الفضل بخلاف لحم الطيور لانه لا يجوز وصف موضع منه وله انه مجهول للتفاوت فى قلة العظم وكثرته أو في سمنه وهر الة على اختلاف فصول السنة وهذه الجهالة مفضية الى المنازعة وفى مخلوع العظم لا يجوز على الوجه الثانى وهو الأصح والتضمين بالمثل ممنوع وكذا الاستقراض وبعد التسليم فالمثل اعدل من القيمة ولان القبض يعاين فيعرف مثل المقبوض به فى وقته اما الوصف فلا يكتفى به 
 ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک گوشت کی بیع سلم میں کوئی بھلائی نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اگر گوشت کی معلوم جگہ ، صفت معلومہ کے ساتھ بیان کی ہو تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ گوشت وزنی ( اور ) وصف سے منضبط ہے اور اسی وجہ سے گوشت بالمثل مضمون ہوتا ہے اور وزان سے اس کا قرض لینا جائز ہے، اور ربوا الفضل جاری ہوتا ہے، برخلاف پرندوں کے گوشت کے کیونکہ پرند میں سے کسی جگہ کا بیان کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوشت ہڈی کے کم اور زیادہ ہونے کی وجہ سے یا سال کی مختلف فصلوں میں جانور کے مونا
. اور دبلا ہونے کی وجہ سے متفاوت ہوتا ہے اور یہ جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ ہوتی ہے۔ اور ہڈی سے علیحدہ کئے ہوئے گوشت میں دوسری وجہ پر بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اور یہی روایت زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ اور گوشت کا بالمثل مضمون ہونا ممنوع ہے اور اسی طرح وزن سے قرض لینا بھی ( ممنوع ہے ) اور تسلیم کے بعد (جواب یہ ہے کہ ) مثل ، قیمت کی بہ نسبت برابری زیادہ کرنے والا ہے اور اس لئے کہ قبضہ مشاہد ہوتا ہے پس اپنے وقت میں مقبوض کی مثل شناخت ہو جائیگا۔ اور رہا وصف تو اس پر اکتفاء نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ 
 تشریح گوشت کی بیع سلم کے عدم جواز کو بیان کرنے کیلئے حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے لا یجوز کا عام لفظ چھوڑ کر لا خبر کا لفظ ذکر کیا ہے۔ علامہ بدر الدین مینی اس کی دو وجہیں لکھتے ہیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ حضرت امام صاحب کا مقصود گوشت کی بیع سلم کے عدم جواز کو علی سبیل المبالغہ بیان کرنا ہے، اور لا خیر میں مبالغہ اس طور پر ہے کہ خیر نکرہ ہے اور نفی کے تحت واقع ہے اور نکرہ تحت انھی عموم کا فائدہ دیتا ہے، پس لا خیر اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے تمام انواع خیر کی نفی کا فائدہ دے گا۔ یعنی گوشت کی بیع مسلم میں کوئی خیر نہیں اور اس میں مبالغہ ظاہر ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ مجتہد جب اپنی رائے سے کسی حکم کا استنباط کرتا ہے تو وہ اگر عدم جواز پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے تو اس کی تعبیر کرنے کیلئے لا خیر کہتا ہے اور اگر جواز پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے تو لا باس کا لفظ ذکر کرتا ہے اور اس کا مقصد احکام خداوندی میں اپنی رائے سے قطعی اور یقینی فیصلہ دینے سے گریز کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال گوشت کی بیع سلم کا مسئلہ مختلف فیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ عدم جواز کے قائل ہیں اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اگر رب السلم نے جنس، نوع اور گوشت کی جگہ اور اس کا وصف بیان کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ مثلاً یہ کہا کہ دو سالہ موٹے تازے خصی بکرے کے اٹھ یا سینہ کا دو من گوشت مسلم فیہ ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ 
 صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوشت عرف عام میں وزنی ہے، یعنی گوشت کی خرید و فروخت وزن کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، اور جنس ، نوع اور گوشت کی جگہ بیان کرنے سے اس کا وصف بھی منضبط ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب گوشت موزونی ہے اور کا وصف بھی منضبط ہے تو اس کا سپرد کر نامتعذر نہ ہوگا بلہ ممکن ہوگا۔ اور جو چیز مقدور التسلیم ہو اس کی بیع سلم چونکہ جائز ہوتی ہے اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ اور گوشت چونکہ موزونی اور مضبوط الوصف ہے اس لئے اگر کسی نے کسی کا گوشت تلف کیا تو اس کے مثل وزن سے تاوان اور ضمان لا زم ہوتا ہے۔ اور وزن سے گوشت کا قرضہ لینا جائز ہے اور اگر گوشت اس کے ہم جنس گوشت کے عوض کی زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کیا گیا تو یہ زیادتی حرام اور ر ہوا ہے، اور علت ربو اوزن مع الجنس ہے۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ گوشت ایک وزنی چیز ہے، اور جنس، نوع اور سینہ یا پٹھ وغیرہ جگہ بیان کر دینے سے اس کا وصف بھی منضبط اور معلوم ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور جو چیز وزنی ہو اور مضبوط الوصف ہو اس کا سپر د کرنا تعذر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مقدور ہوتا ہے اور جس چیز کا سپر ذکر نا مسلم الیہ کی قدرت میں ہو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ ہاں پرندوں کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ پرندوں میں گوشت چونکہ بہت کم ہوتا ہے اس لئے کسی جگہ کا بیان کرنا یعنی یہ کہنا کہ گوشت پرند کے سینہ کا ہو یا کچھ کا ہو یا ان کا ہو ممکن نہیں ہے اور چرند جانور میں چونکہ اس کا امکان ہے اس لئے اس کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے عدم جواز کی دوہ جنہیں بیان فرمائی ہیں۔ ایک وجہ تو یہ ہے کہ گوشت ہڈیوں کی قلت اور کثرت کی وجہ سے چونکہ متفاوت ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ مجہول ہو گا۔ اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ موسموں کے اختلاف سے گوشت مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ سردی کے زمانہ میں جانوروں کا گوشت خوب موٹا تازہ ہوتا ہے اور گرمی اور برسات کے زمانہ میں اس قدر موٹا تازہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ دبلا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس تفاوت اور اختلاف کی وجہ سے بھی مسلم فیہ مجہول ہوگی ۔ اور مذکور دونوں صورتوں میں اپنی
The ruling on salam in meat... Statements of the jurists: He said: There is no good in salam in meat according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If a known place of the meat is described with a known description, it is permissible, because it is weighed and the description is fixed, and for this reason it is guaranteed by like measure, and borrowing it by weight is permissible, and riba al-fadl applies therein, unlike the meat of birds because it is not possible to describe a place from it. And for him (Abu Hanifa): It is unknown due to variation in the smallness and largeness of bone, or in its fatness and leanness according to the different seasons of the year, and this ignorance leads to dispute. And in the case of de-boned meat, it is not permissible on the second basis, and that is the most sound. And compensation by like measure is prohibited, and likewise borrowing. And after delivery (the reply is that) like measure is more equitable than value, and because possession is witnessed, so the like of the received item is known at its time. As for description, it is not relied upon.
Translation: According to Abu Hanifa, there is no good in salam in meat. And the Sahibayn said: If a known place of meat is described with a known description, it is permissible, because meat is weighed and fixed in description, and for this reason meat is guaranteed by like measure, and borrowing it by weight is permissible, and riba al-fadl applies, unlike the meat of birds because it is not possible to describe any place from a bird. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that meat varies due to the less or more of bone, or due to the different seasons of the year, the animal's fat or leanness, and this ignorance leads to dispute. And in de-boned meat, salam is not permissible on the second basis, and this narration is more correct. And compensation by like measure is prohibited, and likewise borrowing by weight is prohibited. And after delivery (the reply is that) like measure is more equitable than value, and because possession is witnessed, so the like of the received item is known at its time. As for description, it is not relied upon.
Explanation: To express the non-permissibility of salam in meat, Imam Abu Hanifa used the word 'la khayr' instead of the general word 'la yajuz'. Allamah Badr al-Din al-'Ayni writes two reasons for this. One is that Imam's purpose is to express non-permissibility in a hyperbolic manner, and 'la khayr' has hyperbole because 'khayr' is indefinite and falls under negation, and an indefinite under negation gives generality, so 'la khayr' by its generality negates all kinds of good, meaning there is no good in salam in meat, and this hyperbole is apparent. The second reason is that when a mujtahid derives a ruling by his own opinion, if it involves non-permissibility he says 'la khayr', and if it involves permissibility he says 'la ba's', and his purpose is to avoid giving a decisive and certain verdict in divine rulings. In any case, the issue of salam in meat is disputed. Thus, Imam Abu Hanifa holds non-permissibility, and the Sahibayn said: If the rabb al-salam specifies the genus, type, place of meat, and its description, it is permissible. For example, if he says: 'Two mans of meat from the thigh or chest of a fat, fresh, castrated two-year-old goat is the muslam fihi', then it is permissible.
The proof of the Sahibayn is that meat in common custom is weighed, i.e., the buying and selling of meat is by weight, and by mentioning the genus, type, and place of meat, its description becomes fixed. So when meat is weighed and its description is fixed, then its delivery is not impossible but possible. And the salam of a thing that is capable of delivery is permissible, so salam in meat is permissible. And because meat is weighed and fixed in description, if someone destroys someone's meat, he must pay compensation with the like weight. And borrowing meat by weight is permissible, and if meat is sold in exchange for the same kind of meat with an increase, that increase is haram and riba, and the cause of riba is weight with same genus. In any case, it is established that meat is a weighed thing, and by mentioning genus, type, and place like chest or thigh, its description becomes fixed and known. And a thing that is weighed and fixed in description is not impossible to deliver but possible, and salam in a thing that is within the power of the muslam ilayh to deliver is permissible. Therefore salam in meat is permissible. Yes, salam in the meat of birds is not permissible. The reason for non-permissibility is that birds have very little meat, so it is not possible to specify a place, like saying the meat is from the chest or something. And in the case of quadrupeds, because it is possible, salam in their meat is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa gave two reasons for non-permissibility. One reason is that meat varies due to the less or more bones, so it is unknown. The second reason is that meat varies according to seasons; in winter meat is fat and fresh, in summer and rainy season it is not as fat but lean. Due to this variation and difference, the muslam fihi is unknown. And in both mentioned cases...
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of salam (advance sale) in meat. The core disagreement is whether meat can be specified sufficiently to avoid uncertainty (jihalah). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it cannot, because meat differs in the amount of bone, fat content, and quality across seasons, leading to potential disputes. Therefore, he uses the emphatic phrase 'la khayr' (there is no good) to indicate strong disapproval bordering on prohibition. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow salam in meat provided the seller describes the genus (e.g., goat, cow), type (e.g., mutton), specific part (e.g., thigh, chest), and condition (e.g., fat, two-year-old). They argue that meat is a weighed commodity (mawzoon) and can be well-described, making it possible to deliver without uncertainty. They further support their view by noting that meat is subject to compensation by like weight (ta'diya bi al-mithl), borrowing by weight is valid, and riba al-fadl applies, all of which indicate it is a precisely measurable good. The Hidayah then notes that for de-boned meat (makhlu' al-'azm), the more correct view is non-permissibility, as the bone variation is eliminated but other uncertainties remain. The commentary also explains why Imam Abu Hanifa used 'la khayr' instead of 'la yajuz': either for hyperbole or to avoid giving a definitive ruling on Allah's laws.

Key Terms
لا خير (la khayr): There is no good; a phrase used by Imam Abu Hanifa to indicate strong disapproval without claiming certainty.
لا بأس (la ba's): No harm; a phrase used for permissibility derived by ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is one reason Imam Abu Hanifa used 'la khayr' instead of 'la yajuz'?
A) To avoid giving a definitive ruling on a matter of ijtihad
B) To make the ruling more lenient
C) Because he was unsure of the evidence
D) To encourage people to engage in salam despite the uncertainty

Key Takeaway
The choice of wording in fiqh rulings reflects the mujtahid's methodological approach to certainty.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Imam Abu Hanifa's Prohibition of Salam in Meat
Imam Abu Hanifa's two reasons for salam in meat's invalidity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two reasons Imam Abu Hanifa gives for prohibiting salam in meat and explain why each leads to invalidity.

Core Idea
Salam in meat is invalid because inherent uncertainty leads to inevitable dispute.

Salam is an exception to the general rule against selling what one does not possess, but it requires that the subject matter be precisely known. Meat, however, has two sources of uncertainty: bone content and seasonal variation. Imam Abu Hanifa ruled that these uncertainties make salam in meat invalid, as they inevitably lead to dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. Here, the act is salam (advance sale) in meat, and Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling is that it is invalid (batil).
2
Locate the two reasons for impermissibility
Imam Abu Hanifa gives two reasons: (1) meat varies in bone content, making the quantity of meat uncertain; (2) meat varies with seasons (fat in winter, lean in summer), creating uncertainty about quality.
These are mentioned in the passage: 'meat varies due to the fewness and abundance of bones' and 'meat differs due to the difference of seasons.'
3
Understand how each reason creates jahala
Jahala (ignorance) occurs because at the time of contract, the exact meat to be delivered is unknown. For example, the buyer demands boneless meat, but the seller may deliver meat with many bones. Similarly, seasonal changes mean the meat may be lean instead of fat as stipulated.
4
Recognize that jahala leads to dispute
This jahala leads to dispute (niza') between the parties, which is the basis for invalidity. The passage states: 'this ignorance leads to dispute, and ignorance that causes dispute renders the sale invalid.'
5
Note the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Imam Abu Hanifa's view of impermissibility, as affirmed in Al-Hidayah and this commentary. The narration of Ibn Shuja'a is considered more correct.
Even though the Sahibayn differ, the fatwa is on the side of impermissibility.

باب السلم
اشرف الہدایہ جلد نہم . اور دبلا ہونے کی وجہ سے متفاوت ہوتا ہے اور یہ جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ ہوتی ہے۔ اور ہڈی سے علیحدہ کئے ہوئے گوشت میں دوسری وجہ پر بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے اور یہی روایت زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ اور گوشت کا بالمثل مضمون ہونا ممنوع ہے اور اسی طرح وزن سے قرض لینا بھی ( ممنوع ہے ) اور تسلیم کے بعد (جواب یہ ہے کہ ) مثل ، قیمت کی بہ نسبت برابری زیادہ کرنے والا ہے اور اس لئے کہ قبضہ مشاہد ہوتا ہے پس اپنے وقت میں مقبوض کی مثل شناخت ہو جائیگا۔ اور رہا وصف تو اس پر اکتفاء نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح گوشت کی بیع سلم کے عدم جواز کو بیان کرنے کیلئے حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے لا یجوز کا عام لفظ چھوڑ کر لا خبر کا لفظ ذکر کیا ہے۔ علامہ بدر الدین مینی اس کی دو وجہیں لکھتے ہیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ حضرت امام صاحب کا مقصود گوشت کی بیع سلم کے عدم جواز کو علی سبیل المبالغہ بیان کرنا ہے، اور لا خیر میں مبالغہ اس طور پر ہے کہ خیر نکرہ ہے اور نفی کے تحت واقع ہے اور نکرہ تحت انھی عموم کا فائدہ دیتا ہے، پس لا خیر اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے تمام انواع خیر کی نفی کا فائدہ دے گا۔ یعنی گوشت کی بیع مسلم میں کوئی خیر نہیں اور اس میں مبالغہ ظاہر ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ مجتہد جب اپنی رائے سے کسی حکم کا استنباط کرتا ہے تو وہ اگر عدم جواز پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے تو اس کی تعبیر کرنے کیلئے لا خیر کہتا ہے اور اگر جواز پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے تو لا باس کا لفظ ذکر کرتا ہے اور اس کا مقصد احکام خداوندی میں اپنی رائے سے قطعی اور یقینی فیصلہ دینے سے گریز کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال گوشت کی بیع سلم کا مسئلہ مختلف فیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ عدم جواز کے قائل ہیں اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اگر رب السلم نے جنس، نوع اور گوشت کی جگہ اور اس کا وصف بیان کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ مثلاً یہ کہا کہ دو سالہ موٹے تازے خصی بکرے کے اٹھ یا سینہ کا دو من گوشت مسلم فیہ ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوشت عرف عام میں وزنی ہے، یعنی گوشت کی خرید و فروخت وزن کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، اور جنس ، نوع اور گوشت کی جگہ بیان کرنے سے اس کا وصف بھی منضبط ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب گوشت موزونی ہے اور کا وصف بھی منضبط ہے تو اس کا سپرد کر نامتعذر نہ ہوگا بلہ ممکن ہوگا۔ اور جو چیز مقدور التسلیم ہو اس کی بیع سلم چونکہ جائز ہوتی ہے اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ اور گوشت چونکہ موزونی اور مضبوط الوصف ہے اس لئے اگر کسی نے کسی کا گوشت تلف کیا تو اس کے مثل وزن سے تاوان اور ضمان لا زم ہوتا ہے۔ اور وزن سے گوشت کا قرضہ لینا جائز ہے اور اگر گوشت اس کے ہم جنس گوشت کے عوض کی زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کیا گیا تو یہ زیادتی حرام اور ر ہوا ہے، اور علت ربو اوزن مع الجنس ہے۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ گوشت ایک وزنی چیز ہے، اور جنس، نوع اور سینہ یا پٹھ وغیرہ جگہ بیان کر دینے سے اس کا وصف بھی منضبط اور معلوم ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور جو چیز وزنی ہو اور مضبوط الوصف ہو اس کا سپر د کرنا تعذر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مقدور ہوتا ہے اور جس چیز کا سپر ذکر نا مسلم الیہ کی قدرت میں ہو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ ہاں پرندوں کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ پرندوں میں گوشت چونکہ بہت کم ہوتا ہے اس لئے کسی جگہ کا بیان کرنا یعنی یہ کہنا کہ گوشت پرند کے سینہ کا ہو یا کچھ کا ہو یا ان کا ہو ممکن نہیں ہے اور چرند جانور میں چونکہ اس کا امکان ہے اس لئے اس کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے عدم جواز کی دوہ جنہیں بیان فرمائی ہیں۔ ایک وجہ تو یہ ہے کہ گوشت ہڈیوں کی قلت اور کثرت کی وجہ سے چونکہ متفاوت ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ مجہول ہو گا۔ اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ موسموں کے اختلاف سے گوشت مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ سردی کے زمانہ میں جانوروں کا گوشت خوب موٹا تازہ ہوتا ہے اور گرمی اور برسات کے زمانہ میں اس قدر موٹا تازہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ دبلا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس تفاوت اور اختلاف کی وجہ سے بھی مسلم فیہ مجہول ہوگی ۔ اور مذکور دونوں صورتوں میں اپنی
جہالت ہے جو جھگڑا پیدا کرتی ہے۔ چنانچہ رب السلام ایسے گوشت کا مطالبہ کرے گا جس میں ہڈیاں نہ ہوں اور مسلم الیہ ایسا سپر دکرے گا جس میں خوب ہڈیاں ہوں۔ اسی طرح گر رب اسلم نے موٹا تازہ گوشت ہونے کی شرط لگائی اور اتفاق سے میعادا ایسے زمانہ میں پوری ہوئی جب کہ جانور ڈبلے ہوتے ہیں تو رب السلم موٹے تازے گوشت کا مطالبہ کرے گا اور مسلم الیہ اپنی لاچاری اور مجبوری کا اظہار کرے گا اور جو اس کے پاس موجود ہو گا اس کو سپرد کرنے کی کوشش کرے گا۔ بہر حال دونوں صورتوں میں ایسی جہالت ہے جو جھگڑا پیدا کرتی ہے جو جہالت جھگڑے کا باعث ہو وہ بیچ کو فاسد کر دیتی ہے، اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم فاسد اور نا جائز ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر ہڈی علیحدہ کئے ہوئے گوشت کی بیع سلم کی گئی تو بھی نا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں عدم جواز کی دوسری وجہ یعنی موٹا اور دبلا ہونے کا تفاوت موجود ہے۔ نیز اگر موٹے تازے جانور کے گوشت کی شرط لگائی اور میعادا ایسے زمانہ میں پوری ہوئی جب کہ جانور انتہائی لاغر اور ڈبلے ہوتے ہیں تو عقد سلم کے وقت سے لے کر ادا ئیگی کے وقت تک مسلم فیہ موجود ہونے کی شر ہیں پائی گئی ، اس لئے بھی اس صورت میں بیع سلم نا جائز ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بڑی علیحدہ کئے ہوئے گوشت کی بیع سلم کا وجہ ثانی کی وجہ سے ناجائز ہونا یہی زیادہ صحیح روایت ہے۔ اسی کو ابن شجاع نے حضرت امام صاحب سے روایت کیا ہے۔ اگر چہ حسن کی روایت کے مطابق ہڈی علیحدہ کئے ہوئے گوشت کی بیع
سلم جائز ہے۔ والتضمين بالمثل ممنوع سے صاحبین کے قول کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ گوشت چونکہ موزونی ہے اس لئے تلف کرنے کی صورت میں اس کا ضمان بالمثل واجب ہوتا ہے اور وزن کے ساتھ اس کا قرضہ لینا جائز ہے ، غلط . ہے۔ یہ بات ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے بلکہ گوشت تلف کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے عمان بالمثل واجب نہیں ہوتا اور اس طرح وزن کے ساتھ قرضہ لینا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ بہر حال جب یہ دونوں باتیں تسلیم نہیں ہیں تو ان سے استدلال کرنا بھی صحیح نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر یہ تسلیم بھی کر لیں کہ تلف کی صورت میں گوشت مضمون بالمثل ہوتا ہے تو اس سے گوشت کا وزنی ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا، جیسا کہ حضرات صاحبین نے سمجھا ہے، بلکہ اصل یہ ہے کہ جب کوئی چیز تلف کر دی جائے تو تلف کرنے والے پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے اور ضمان کے اندر اصل مماثلت ہے اور تلف شدہ چیز کا مثل واجب کرنے میں صورۃ بھی مماثلت پائی جاتی ہے اور معنی بھی مماثلت موجود ہے۔ اور قیمت واجب کرنے میں فقط مماثلت پائی جاتی ہے صورۃ مماثلت نہیں پائی جاتی۔ اور یہ بات اظہر من الشمس ہے کہ صورت اور معنی دونوں طرح مماثلت پائے جانے کی صورت میں تلف شدہ چیز کے ساتھ مساوات اور برابری زیادہ ہوتی ہے بہ نسبت مثل معنوی یعنی قیمت واجب کرنے کے۔ اس لئے گوشت کا ضمان بالمثل واجب کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور اس مصلحت سے ممان بالمثل واجب کرنے سے گوشت کا وزنی ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوتا ، اور وزن سے قرضہ لینے کی صورت میں قبضہ چونکہ فوری ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ مشاہد اور آنکھوں کے سامنے ہوگا۔ اور جب قرضہ کے اندرشی مقبوض محسوس اور مشاہد ہے تو اس کو اپنے وقت میں مقبوض کے مثل شناخت کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور جب قرضہ میں مقبوض کا مثل معلوم ہے تو جہالت دور ہو جائے گی اور جب جہالت دور ہو گئی تو وزن سے قرضہ لینا بھی جائز ہوگا ، اور عقد سلم میں فوری قبضہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ محض مسلم فیہ کا وصف ذکر کیا جاتا ہے اور محض وصف سے چونکہ پوری شناخت نہیں ہو سکتی اسلئے وصف پر اکتفاء نہ ہوگا اور گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Chapter of Salam. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9. And due to being lean it becomes disparate, and this ignorance leads to dispute. And for meat separated from bone, salam sale is not permissible due to the second reason, and this narration is more correct. And meat being guaranteed by its like is prohibited, and similarly taking a loan by weight is (prohibited). And after acceptance (the response is that) the like is more equal compared to price, and because possession is witnessed, so at its time the like of the possessed will be known. And as for description, it will not be relied upon.
Commentary: To express the impermissibility of salam sale of meat, Imam Abu Hanifa left the general word 'la yajuz' and mentioned the word 'la khair'. Allama Badr al-Din al-'Ayni writes two reasons for this. One is that Imam's purpose is to express the impermissibility of salam sale of meat in an exaggerated manner, and in 'la khair' exaggeration is such that 'khair' is indefinite and falls under negation, and an indefinite under negation gives generality, so 'la khair' due to its generality negates all kinds of good. That is, there is no good in salam of meat, and the exaggeration is apparent. The second reason is that when a mujtahid derives a ruling from his opinion, if it involves impermissibility he says 'la khair' to express it, and if it involves permissibility he says 'la ba's', and his purpose is to avoid giving a definitive and certain decision from his own opinion regarding the commands of Allah. In any case, the matter of salam sale of meat is disputed. Thus Imam Abu Hanifa holds impermissibility, and the Sahibayn said that if the buyer specifies the genus, type, place of meat, and its description, then it is permissible. For example, he said: 'Two maunds of meat from the thigh or breast of a two-year-old fat fresh castrated goat is the subject of salam,' then it is permissible.
The proof of the Sahibayn is that meat in common custom is weighed, i.e., buying and selling of meat occurs by weight, and by specifying the genus, type, and place of meat, its description is also regulated. So when meat is weighed and its description is regulated, its delivery will not be impossible but possible. And salam of something that is capable of being delivered is permissible, so salam of meat will be permissible. And because meat is weighed and strongly described, if someone destroys another's meat, compensation and guarantee by its like weight is obligatory. And taking a loan of meat by weight is permissible, and if meat is sold with an increase in exchange for its own kind of meat, that increase is unlawful and usury, and the cause of usury is weight with genus. In any case, it is established that meat is a weighed thing, and by specifying the genus, type, and place such as breast or thigh, its description is also regulated and known. And delivery of something that is weighed and strongly described is not impossible but possible, and salam of something whose delivery is within the power of the deliverer is permissible. Therefore salam of meat will be permissible. Yes, salam of bird meat is not permissible. The reason for impermissibility is that in birds, since meat is very little, specifying a place—i.e., saying that the meat is from the bird's breast or thigh or wings—is not possible; and in quadruped animals, since it is possible, salam of their meat is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa stated two reasons for impermissibility. One reason is that meat varies due to the fewness and abundance of bones, so it becomes unknown. The second reason is that meat differs due to the difference of seasons. Thus in winter, animal meat is very fat and fresh, and in summer and rainy season it is not so fat and fresh but lean. So due to this variation and difference, the subject of salam becomes unknown. And in both mentioned cases there is ignorance that leads to dispute. Thus the buyer will demand meat without bones, and the seller will deliver meat with many bones. Similarly, if the buyer stipulated fat fresh meat and the term coincidentally ended in a season when animals are lean, then the buyer will demand fat fresh meat, and the seller will express his helplessness and compulsion and try to deliver what he has available. In any case, in both cases there is such ignorance that leads to dispute, and ignorance that causes dispute renders the sale invalid, therefore salam sale of meat is invalid and impermissible.
The author of Hidayah says: If salam of meat separated from bone is made, it is still impermissible, because in this case the second reason—the variation of fat and lean—exists. Also, if the condition of fat fresh meat is made and the term ends in a season when animals are extremely lean and thin, then from the time of the salam contract until the time of delivery the condition of the subject being present is not found, so in this case too salam is impermissible. The author of Hidayah says that the impermissibility of salam of meat separated from bone due to the second reason is the more correct narration. This is what Ibn Shuja'a narrated from Imam. Although according to the narration of Hasan, salam of meat separated from bone is permissible. The statement 'and being guaranteed by its like is prohibited' is a response to the saying of the Sahibayn. The gist of the response is that the Sahibayn's saying that meat is weighed and therefore if destroyed its guarantee by like is obligatory and taking a loan by weight is permissible is incorrect. We do not accept this; rather, if meat is destroyed, its price is obligatory, not its like by weight, and similarly taking a loan by weight is impermissible. In any case, since these two matters are not accepted, deriving proof from them is also incorrect. And even if we accept that in case of destruction meat is guaranteed by its like, this does not prove that meat is weighed, as the Sahibayn thought. Rather, the principle is that when something is destroyed, the destroyer owes a guarantee, and in guarantee the principle is similitude, and in making the like of the destroyed thing obligatory, similitude is found both in form and meaning, while in making the price obligatory, only similitude in meaning is found, not in form. And it is clearer than the sun that when similitude in both form and meaning is found, equality with the destroyed thing is greater compared to making the price (i.e., only similar in meaning) obligatory. Therefore, meat is made to be guaranteed by its like. But making it guaranteed by its like due to this benefit does not prove that meat is weighed, and in the case of taking a loan by weight, since possession is immediate, it will be witnessed and before the eyes. And when in a loan the possessed is sensed and witnessed, its like can be known at its time. And when the like of the possessed is known in a loan, ignorance is removed, and when ignorance is removed, taking a loan by weight is permissible. But in a salam contract, immediate possession does not occur; only the description of the subject is mentioned, and since mere description cannot provide complete identification, description will not be relied upon, and salam of meat will not be permissible.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion on the chapter of salam (advance sale) focusing specifically on whether meat can be sold via salam. The text begins by noting that Imam Abu Hanifa deliberately used the phrase 'la khair' (no good) rather than 'la yajuz' (not permissible) to emphasize the prohibition and to avoid giving a definitive ruling from his own opinion. The commentator then explains that there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds salam in meat impermissible, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it permissible if the buyer specifies the genus, type, place (e.g., breast or thigh), and description of the meat. The Sahibayn's proof is that meat is customarily sold by weight, and specifying these aspects makes it sufficiently known and deliverable. They also argue that if someone destroys meat, they must pay a like weight (misl), and meat loans by weight are allowed, which shows it is a standard weighed commodity. Imam Abu Hanifa gives two reasons for impermissibility: (1) meat varies with the proportion of bones, causing uncertainty, and (2) meat quality changes with seasons, leading to potential dispute at delivery. The text then addresses the rebuttal: even if we accept the Sahibayn's proof about guarantee by like, that does not prove meat is a standard weighed good for salam because guarantee by like is based on the principle of full compensation (form and meaning), not on it being a standard weighed item. Furthermore, in a loan, immediate possession allows identification by sight, but in salam the delivery is deferred, and mere description cannot eliminate uncertainty. Therefore, the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa's) is that salam in meat is invalid due to inherent uncertainty leading to dispute. The text also notes that meat separated from bone is still impermissible because the seasonal variation remains. Ibn Shuja'a narrated the stronger opinion of impermissibility from Imam Abu Hanifa, although Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated a permissive view.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): An advance sale where the price is paid now and the goods are delivered later, with specific conditions.
جہالت (jahala): Ignorance or uncertainty about a material term of the contract, which can lead to dispute.
منازعہ (niza'): Dispute or conflict between contracting parties.
مضمون بالمثل (madmun bi al-mithl): Guaranteed by the like (weight or measure); compensation for destruction in kind rather than price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits salam in meat?
A) Meat is not a commodity
B) Meat varies due to bones and seasons, leading to jahalah that causes dispute
C) Meat cannot be described
D) Meat is not weighed

Key Takeaway
Salam in meat is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because inherent uncertainties in bone content and seasonal quality make the subject unknown and lead to dispute.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

10 min
The Sahibayn's View on Salam in Meat and the Hanafi Rebuttal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in meat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Sahibayn's argument for permissibility of salam in meat and the Hanafi rebuttal, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Although the Sahibayn permit salam in meat with sufficient description, the Hanafi school holds that description cannot overcome inherent uncertainty.

The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differed from Imam Abu Hanifa on the permissibility of salam in meat. They argued that meat is a weighed commodity and can be sufficiently described to remove uncertainty. This lesson presents their proof and the Hanafi response that ultimately prevails in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing school and their position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that salam in meat is permissible if the buyer specifies the genus, type, and part (e.g., breast or thigh) of the meat.
2
Follow their proof
Their proof: (1) Meat is customarily sold by weight; (2) specifying genus, type, and part makes the description regulated; (3) deliverability is possible; (4) if meat is destroyed, compensation is by like weight; (5) loans of meat by weight are allowed.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: (1) Guarantee by like is based on full compensation (similitude in form and meaning), not on meat being a standard weighed good; (2) loans involve immediate possession and identification by sight, while salam is deferred and solely dependent on description, which is insufficient.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Sahibayn, salam in meat with proper description is valid and enforceable. Under Abu Hanifa, it is invalid (batil). The fatwa follows Abu Hanifa.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position is impermissibility, as affirmed in Al-Hidayah and this commentary. The narration of Ibn Shuja'a (impermissibility even for bone-separated meat) is considered more correct.

صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گوشت عرف عام میں وزنی ہے، یعنی گوشت کی خرید و فروخت وزن کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، اور جنس ، نوع اور گوشت کی جگہ بیان کرنے سے اس کا وصف بھی منضبط ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب گوشت موزونی ہے اور کا وصف بھی منضبط ہے تو اس کا سپرد کر نامتعذر نہ ہوگا بلہ ممکن ہوگا۔ اور جو چیز مقدور التسلیم ہو اس کی بیع سلم چونکہ جائز ہوتی ہے اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ اور گوشت چونکہ موزونی اور مضبوط الوصف ہے اس لئے اگر کسی نے کسی کا گوشت تلف کیا تو اس کے مثل وزن سے تاوان اور ضمان لا زم ہوتا ہے۔ اور وزن سے گوشت کا قرضہ لینا جائز ہے اور اگر گوشت اس کے ہم جنس گوشت کے عوض کی زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کیا گیا تو یہ زیادتی حرام اور ر ہوا ہے، اور علت ربو اوزن مع الجنس ہے۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ گوشت ایک وزنی چیز ہے، اور جنس، نوع اور سینہ یا پٹھ وغیرہ جگہ بیان کر دینے سے اس کا وصف بھی منضبط اور معلوم ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور جو چیز وزنی ہو اور مضبوط الوصف ہو اس کا سپر د کرنا تعذر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مقدور ہوتا ہے اور جس چیز کا سپر ذکر نا مسلم الیہ کی قدرت میں ہو اس کی بیع سلم جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہوگی۔ ہاں پرندوں کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ پرندوں میں گوشت چونکہ بہت کم ہوتا ہے اس لئے کسی جگہ کا بیان کرنا یعنی یہ کہنا کہ گوشت پرند کے سینہ کا ہو یا کچھ کا ہو یا ان کا ہو ممکن نہیں ہے اور چرند جانور میں چونکہ اس کا امکان ہے اس لئے اس کے گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے عدم جواز کی دوہ جنہیں بیان فرمائی ہیں۔ ایک وجہ تو یہ ہے کہ گوشت ہڈیوں کی قلت اور کثرت کی وجہ سے چونکہ متفاوت ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ مجہول ہو گا۔ اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ موسموں کے اختلاف سے گوشت مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ سردی کے زمانہ میں جانوروں کا گوشت خوب موٹا تازہ ہوتا ہے اور گرمی اور برسات کے زمانہ میں اس قدر موٹا تازہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ دبلا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس تفاوت اور اختلاف کی وجہ سے بھی مسلم فیہ مجہول ہوگی ۔ اور مذکور دونوں صورتوں میں اپنی
جہالت ہے جو جھگڑا پیدا کرتی ہے۔ چنانچہ رب السلام ایسے گوشت کا مطالبہ کرے گا جس میں ہڈیاں نہ ہوں اور مسلم الیہ ایسا سپر دکرے گا جس میں خوب ہڈیاں ہوں۔ اسی طرح گر رب اسلم نے موٹا تازہ گوشت ہونے کی شرط لگائی اور اتفاق سے میعادا ایسے زمانہ میں پوری ہوئی جب کہ جانور ڈبلے ہوتے ہیں تو رب السلم موٹے تازے گوشت کا مطالبہ کرے گا اور مسلم الیہ اپنی لاچاری اور مجبوری کا اظہار کرے گا اور جو اس کے پاس موجود ہو گا اس کو سپرد کرنے کی کوشش کرے گا۔ بہر حال دونوں صورتوں میں ایسی جہالت ہے جو جھگڑا پیدا کرتی ہے جو جہالت جھگڑے کا باعث ہو وہ بیچ کو فاسد کر دیتی ہے، اس لئے گوشت کی بیع سلم فاسد اور نا جائز ہے۔
