سلم جائز ہے۔ والتضمين بالمثل ممنوع سے صاحبین کے قول کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ گوشت چونکہ موزونی ہے اس لئے تلف کرنے کی صورت میں اس کا ضمان بالمثل واجب ہوتا ہے اور وزن کے ساتھ اس کا قرضہ لینا جائز ہے ، غلط . ہے۔ یہ بات ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے بلکہ گوشت تلف کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے عمان بالمثل واجب نہیں ہوتا اور اس طرح وزن کے ساتھ قرضہ لینا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ بہر حال جب یہ دونوں باتیں تسلیم نہیں ہیں تو ان سے استدلال کرنا بھی صحیح نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر یہ تسلیم بھی کر لیں کہ تلف کی صورت میں گوشت مضمون بالمثل ہوتا ہے تو اس سے گوشت کا وزنی ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا، جیسا کہ حضرات صاحبین نے سمجھا ہے، بلکہ اصل یہ ہے کہ جب کوئی چیز تلف کر دی جائے تو تلف کرنے والے پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے اور ضمان کے اندر اصل مماثلت ہے اور تلف شدہ چیز کا مثل واجب کرنے میں صورۃ بھی مماثلت پائی جاتی ہے اور معنی بھی مماثلت موجود ہے۔ اور قیمت واجب کرنے میں فقط مماثلت پائی جاتی ہے صورۃ مماثلت نہیں پائی جاتی۔ اور یہ بات اظہر من الشمس ہے کہ صورت اور معنی دونوں طرح مماثلت پائے جانے کی صورت میں تلف شدہ چیز کے ساتھ مساوات اور برابری زیادہ ہوتی ہے بہ نسبت مثل معنوی یعنی قیمت واجب کرنے کے۔ اس لئے گوشت کا ضمان بالمثل واجب کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور اس مصلحت سے ممان بالمثل واجب کرنے سے گوشت کا وزنی ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوتا ، اور وزن سے قرضہ لینے کی صورت میں قبضہ چونکہ فوری ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ مشاہد اور آنکھوں کے سامنے ہوگا۔ اور جب قرضہ کے اندرشی مقبوض محسوس اور مشاہد ہے تو اس کو اپنے وقت میں مقبوض کے مثل شناخت کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور جب قرضہ میں مقبوض کا مثل معلوم ہے تو جہالت دور ہو جائے گی اور جب جہالت دور ہو گئی تو وزن سے قرضہ لینا بھی جائز ہوگا ، اور عقد سلم میں فوری قبضہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ محض مسلم فیہ کا وصف ذکر کیا جاتا ہے اور محض وصف سے چونکہ پوری شناخت نہیں ہو سکتی اسلئے وصف پر اکتفاء نہ ہوگا اور گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Chapter of Salam. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9. And due to being lean it becomes disparate, and this ignorance leads to dispute. And for meat separated from bone, salam sale is not permissible due to the second reason, and this narration is more correct. And meat being guaranteed by its like is prohibited, and similarly taking a loan by weight is (prohibited). And after acceptance (the response is that) the like is more equal compared to price, and because possession is witnessed, so at its time the like of the possessed will be known. And as for description, it will not be relied upon.
Commentary: To express the impermissibility of salam sale of meat, Imam Abu Hanifa left the general word 'la yajuz' and mentioned the word 'la khair'. Allama Badr al-Din al-'Ayni writes two reasons for this. One is that Imam's purpose is to express the impermissibility of salam sale of meat in an exaggerated manner, and in 'la khair' exaggeration is such that 'khair' is indefinite and falls under negation, and an indefinite under negation gives generality, so 'la khair' due to its generality negates all kinds of good. That is, there is no good in salam of meat, and the exaggeration is apparent. The second reason is that when a mujtahid derives a ruling from his opinion, if it involves impermissibility he says 'la khair' to express it, and if it involves permissibility he says 'la ba's', and his purpose is to avoid giving a definitive and certain decision from his own opinion regarding the commands of Allah. In any case, the matter of salam sale of meat is disputed. Thus Imam Abu Hanifa holds impermissibility, and the Sahibayn said that if the buyer specifies the genus, type, place of meat, and its description, then it is permissible. For example, he said: 'Two maunds of meat from the thigh or breast of a two-year-old fat fresh castrated goat is the subject of salam,' then it is permissible.
The proof of the Sahibayn is that meat in common custom is weighed, i.e., buying and selling of meat occurs by weight, and by specifying the genus, type, and place of meat, its description is also regulated. So when meat is weighed and its description is regulated, its delivery will not be impossible but possible. And salam of something that is capable of being delivered is permissible, so salam of meat will be permissible. And because meat is weighed and strongly described, if someone destroys another's meat, compensation and guarantee by its like weight is obligatory. And taking a loan of meat by weight is permissible, and if meat is sold with an increase in exchange for its own kind of meat, that increase is unlawful and usury, and the cause of usury is weight with genus. In any case, it is established that meat is a weighed thing, and by specifying the genus, type, and place such as breast or thigh, its description is also regulated and known. And delivery of something that is weighed and strongly described is not impossible but possible, and salam of something whose delivery is within the power of the deliverer is permissible. Therefore salam of meat will be permissible. Yes, salam of bird meat is not permissible. The reason for impermissibility is that in birds, since meat is very little, specifying a place—i.e., saying that the meat is from the bird's breast or thigh or wings—is not possible; and in quadruped animals, since it is possible, salam of their meat is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa stated two reasons for impermissibility. One reason is that meat varies due to the fewness and abundance of bones, so it becomes unknown. The second reason is that meat differs due to the difference of seasons. Thus in winter, animal meat is very fat and fresh, and in summer and rainy season it is not so fat and fresh but lean. So due to this variation and difference, the subject of salam becomes unknown. And in both mentioned cases there is ignorance that leads to dispute. Thus the buyer will demand meat without bones, and the seller will deliver meat with many bones. Similarly, if the buyer stipulated fat fresh meat and the term coincidentally ended in a season when animals are lean, then the buyer will demand fat fresh meat, and the seller will express his helplessness and compulsion and try to deliver what he has available. In any case, in both cases there is such ignorance that leads to dispute, and ignorance that causes dispute renders the sale invalid, therefore salam sale of meat is invalid and impermissible.
The author of Hidayah says: If salam of meat separated from bone is made, it is still impermissible, because in this case the second reason—the variation of fat and lean—exists. Also, if the condition of fat fresh meat is made and the term ends in a season when animals are extremely lean and thin, then from the time of the salam contract until the time of delivery the condition of the subject being present is not found, so in this case too salam is impermissible. The author of Hidayah says that the impermissibility of salam of meat separated from bone due to the second reason is the more correct narration. This is what Ibn Shuja'a narrated from Imam. Although according to the narration of Hasan, salam of meat separated from bone is permissible. The statement 'and being guaranteed by its like is prohibited' is a response to the saying of the Sahibayn. The gist of the response is that the Sahibayn's saying that meat is weighed and therefore if destroyed its guarantee by like is obligatory and taking a loan by weight is permissible is incorrect. We do not accept this; rather, if meat is destroyed, its price is obligatory, not its like by weight, and similarly taking a loan by weight is impermissible. In any case, since these two matters are not accepted, deriving proof from them is also incorrect. And even if we accept that in case of destruction meat is guaranteed by its like, this does not prove that meat is weighed, as the Sahibayn thought. Rather, the principle is that when something is destroyed, the destroyer owes a guarantee, and in guarantee the principle is similitude, and in making the like of the destroyed thing obligatory, similitude is found both in form and meaning, while in making the price obligatory, only similitude in meaning is found, not in form. And it is clearer than the sun that when similitude in both form and meaning is found, equality with the destroyed thing is greater compared to making the price (i.e., only similar in meaning) obligatory. Therefore, meat is made to be guaranteed by its like. But making it guaranteed by its like due to this benefit does not prove that meat is weighed, and in the case of taking a loan by weight, since possession is immediate, it will be witnessed and before the eyes. And when in a loan the possessed is sensed and witnessed, its like can be known at its time. And when the like of the possessed is known in a loan, ignorance is removed, and when ignorance is removed, taking a loan by weight is permissible. But in a salam contract, immediate possession does not occur; only the description of the subject is mentioned, and since mere description cannot provide complete identification, description will not be relied upon, and salam of meat will not be permissible.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion on the chapter of salam (advance sale) focusing specifically on whether meat can be sold via salam. The text begins by noting that Imam Abu Hanifa deliberately used the phrase 'la khair' (no good) rather than 'la yajuz' (not permissible) to emphasize the prohibition and to avoid giving a definitive ruling from his own opinion. The commentator then explains that there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds salam in meat impermissible, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it permissible if the buyer specifies the genus, type, place (e.g., breast or thigh), and description of the meat. The Sahibayn's proof is that meat is customarily sold by weight, and specifying these aspects makes it sufficiently known and deliverable. They also argue that if someone destroys meat, they must pay a like weight (misl), and meat loans by weight are allowed, which shows it is a standard weighed commodity. Imam Abu Hanifa gives two reasons for impermissibility: (1) meat varies with the proportion of bones, causing uncertainty, and (2) meat quality changes with seasons, leading to potential dispute at delivery. The text then addresses the rebuttal: even if we accept the Sahibayn's proof about guarantee by like, that does not prove meat is a standard weighed good for salam because guarantee by like is based on the principle of full compensation (form and meaning), not on it being a standard weighed item. Furthermore, in a loan, immediate possession allows identification by sight, but in salam the delivery is deferred, and mere description cannot eliminate uncertainty. Therefore, the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa's) is that salam in meat is invalid due to inherent uncertainty leading to dispute. The text also notes that meat separated from bone is still impermissible because the seasonal variation remains. Ibn Shuja'a narrated the stronger opinion of impermissibility from Imam Abu Hanifa, although Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated a permissive view.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): An advance sale where the price is paid now and the goods are delivered later, with specific conditions.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the primary students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
مضمون بالمثل (madmun bi al-mithl): Guaranteed by the like (weight or measure); compensation for destruction in kind rather than price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference in the Sahibayn's proof compared to Imam Abu Hanifa's position?
A) The Sahibayn believe meat is not a commodity
B) The Sahibayn argue that specification of genus, type, and part removes uncertainty
C) The Sahibayn ignore seasonal variation
D) The Sahibayn consider meat as non-weighed

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in meat centers on whether specification can overcome inherent uncertainties; the relied-upon view is impermissibility.

Salam in Meat: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the invalidity of salam in meat due to jahl and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in meat, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute including the Sahibayn's argument, and apply the jahl principle to similar cases.

Core Idea
Salam in meat is invalid because uncertainty causes dispute; boneless meat fails too due to fatness variation.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on salam (advance payment sale) of meat. We will see why the school deems it invalid and how a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, is resolved. The key issue is whether meat can be specified enough to avoid the uncertainty (jahl) that voids a salam contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the passage rules on salam (forward sale) of meat. State the hukm: the contract is fasid (invalid).
Fasid means the contract is defective in its conditions; it is not entirely void (batil) but cannot be enforced as is.
2
Understand the ratio legis
Why is it invalid? The reason given is jahl (ignorance) about bone content and fatness that leads to dispute (munaaza'ah). This is the primary condition for valid salam: knowledge of the subject matter.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference within the Hanafi school. According to a narration from Abu Hanifa via Ibn Shuja', salam is invalid even for boneless meat. However, Hasan b. Ziyad narrates a permissive view. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is invalidity.
Hasan b. Ziyad's view is a nawadir transmission, thus weaker than the zahir al-riwayah.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's argument
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argued that meat is a weighed commodity (mawzun), so it can be subject to dhaman bi'l-mithl (liability in kind) and thus borrowed by weight; therefore salam should be permissible.
This is an argument by qiyas (analogy) to other mawzun goods like grain.
5
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes this: first, they do not accept that meat is mawzun for liability (instead, they say value is due). Second, even if dhaman bi'l-mithl applied, it does not prove mawzun for salam because in borrowing, immediate possession removes uncertainty, whereas salam lacks immediate possession.
This response preserves the principle that description alone is insufficient to eliminate jahl.

کے گوشت کی شرط لگائی اور میعادا ایسے زمانہ میں پوری ہوئی جب کہ جانور انتہائی لاغر اور ڈبلے ہوتے ہیں تو عقد سلم کے وقت سے لے کر ادا ئیگی کے وقت تک مسلم فیہ موجود ہونے کی شر ہیں پائی گئی ، اس لئے بھی اس تلف کرنے کی صورت میں اس کا ضمان بالمثل واجب ہوتا ہے اور وزن کے ساتھ اس کا قرضہ لینا جائز ہے ، غلط . ہے۔ یہ بات ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے بلکہ گوشت تلف کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے عمان بالمثل من الشمس ہے کہ صورت اور معنی دونوں طرح مماثلت پائے جانے کی صورت میں تلف شدہ چیز کے ساتھ مساوات اور برابری زیادہ ہوتی ہے بہ نسبت مثل معنوی یعنی قیمت واجب کرنے کے۔ اس لئے گوشت کا ضمان بالمثل واجب کیا اندرشی مقبوض محسوس اور مشاہد ہے تو اس کو اپنے وقت میں مقبوض کے مثل شناخت کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور جب قرضہ میں مقبوض کا مثل معلوم ہے تو جہالت دور ہو جائے گی اور جب جہالت دور ہو گئی تو وزن سے قرضہ لینا بھی جائز ہوگا ، اور عقد سلم میں فوری قبضہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ محض مسلم فیہ کا وصف ذکر کیا جاتا ہے اور محض وصف سے چونکہ پوری شناخت نہیں ہو سکتی اسلئے وصف پر اکتفاء نہ ہوگا اور گوشت کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Chapter of Salam. The ignorance that leads to dispute. Thus, the buyer of salam will demand meat without bones, and the seller will deliver meat with many bones. Similarly, if the buyer stipulates fat fresh meat and by chance the term ends when animals are lean, the buyer will demand fat fresh meat and the seller will express helplessness and try to deliver what he has. In both cases, there is ignorance that leads to dispute. Ignorance that causes dispute invalidates the sale, therefore salam in meat is fasid and impermissible. The author of Hidayah says that if salam is made of meat without bones, it is also impermissible because in that case the second reason, i.e., variation in fatness and leanness, exists. Also, if fat fresh animal meat is stipulated and the term ends when animals are extremely lean, then from the time of contract until delivery the subject matter is not available, so for this reason too salam is impermissible. The author of Hidayah says that the impermissibility of salam of meat without bones due to the second reason is the more correct narration. This is what Ibn Shuja' narrated from Imam (Abu Hanifa). Although according to Hasan's narration, salam of meat without bones is permissible. The statement 'and dhaman bi'l-mithl is prohibited' is the response to the saying of the Sahibayn. The summary of the response is that the Sahibayn's statement that meat is weighed, so if it is destroyed, dhaman bi'l-mithl is obligatory and it is permissible to borrow it by weight, is wrong. We do not accept that; rather, in case of destruction, its value is obligatory, not dhaman bi'l-mithl, and thus borrowing by weight is also impermissible. In any case, since these two points are not accepted, arguing from them is also incorrect. And even if we accept that in case of destruction meat is subject to dhaman bi'l-mithl, that does not prove that meat is weighed, as the Sahibayn thought. Rather, the principle is that when something is destroyed, the destroyer is liable, and in liability the original is likeness. In making the like obligatory, there is both formal and substantive likeness, whereas in making value obligatory there is only substantive likeness, not formal. It is clearer than the sun that when both formal and substantive likeness exist, equality with the destroyed item is greater than in the case of substantive likeness (value). Therefore, dhaman bi'l-mithl is obligatory for meat. And from this expedient of making dhaman bi'l-mithl obligatory, the fact that meat is weighed is not proven. In the case of borrowing by weight, since possession is immediate, it is observed and seen. And when the possessed item in borrowing is perceptible and observed, it can be identified as the like of the possessed item at that time. And when the like of the possessed item in borrowing is known, ignorance is removed. When ignorance is removed, borrowing by weight becomes permissible. But in the contract of salam, there is no immediate possession; only the description of the subject matter is mentioned. Since mere description does not provide complete recognition, relying on description is insufficient, and salam in meat will not be permissible.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on salam (advance payment sale) of meat. The commentator explains that salam in meat is invalid (fasid) due to ignorance (jahl) that leads to dispute. The reason is that meat can vary in bone content and fatness, making it impossible to deliver exactly what was contracted, leading to quarrels. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school. The author then considers an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the meat is without bones (i.e., boneless), there is a difference of narration. According to a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa via Ibn Shuja', it is still invalid because the problem of fatness/leanness remains. However, a narration from Hasan b. Ziyad (a Nawadir transmission) holds it permissible. The mufta bihi is the view of invalidity. Next, the commentator addresses an argument from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who claimed that since meat is a weighed commodity (mawzun), it can be subject to dhaman bi'l-mithl (liability in kind) and thus can be borrowed by weight, implying that salam in meat should be permissible. The Hanafi response, attributed to Imam Muhammad, refutes this: first, they do not accept that meat is liable in kind; rather, liability is by value (qima). Even if it were liable in kind, that does not prove it is a weighed commodity for the purpose of salam, because the underlying reason for dhaman bi'l-mithl is to ensure equivalence in form and meaning, not to establish that it is mawzun. Moreover, in salam, since delivery is not immediate, mere description cannot ensure complete identification of the meat, unlike borrowing by weight where immediate possession removes ignorance. Therefore, salam in meat remains invalid.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for a specified commodity to be delivered later.
جہالت (jahālat): Ignorance regarding the subject matter that leads to dispute, invalidating the contract.
ضمان بالمثل (ḍamān bi'l-mithl): Liability to compensate with a like thing (same species and quantity) when a fungible (mithli) is destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because meat is not a mithli commodity.
B) Because uncertainty (jahl) about bone content and fatness leads to dispute.
C) Because salam requires immediate delivery.
D) Because the Sahibayn said it is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Salam in meat is invalid because the inevitable variation in bone and fat content creates uncertainty that leads to dispute, despite a minority view among the Sahibayn.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Salam Sale Requires a Fixed Term: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains the necessity of a fixed term in salam and refutes Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the necessity of a fixed term in salam, explain each school's primary proof, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between the two views.

Core Idea
Salam without a fixed term is invalid because the concession for selling non-existent goods requires a known delivery date.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the salam contract. While both agree on the basic permissibility of salam as a concession, they diverge on whether a fixed term is a necessary condition. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate textual evidence and legal reasoning, especially when interpreting absolute versus restricted hadiths.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling given by Imam al-Quduri: salam is not valid except deferred (i.e., with a fixed term).
Note that the Hanafi school includes Imam Malik and Ahmad in agreement.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that salam is valid immediately (without a fixed term) based on the absolute permission in the hadith.
The Shafi'i argument: the hadith says 'He permitted salam' without any restriction.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith: 'He forbade selling what is not with you, but permitted salam.' They take this as absolute, allowing immediate delivery.
They argue that adding a term would be an unjustified addition to the text.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response provides two proofs: (1) a hadith explicitly requiring a 'known term', and (2) the underlying wisdom (illah) that salam is a concession for the needy, which only works with a term.
The absolute hadith is interpreted in light of the restricted one (takhsis).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi school invalidates any salam contract without a fixed term; Shafi'i school considers it valid.
This affects the validity of transactions in real life, e.g., paying for goods now for immediate delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السلم
قال ولا يجوز السلم الا مؤجلا وقال الشافعي يجوز حالا لاطلاق الحديث ورخص في السلم ولنا قوله عليه السلام الى اجل معلوم فيما روينا ولانه شرع رخصة دفعا لحاجة المفاليس فلابد من الاجل ليقدر على التحصيل فيه فيسلم ولو كان قادرا على التسليم لم يوجد المرخص فبقى على النافي

ترجمہ اور عقد سلم جائز نہیں ہوتا مگر میعادی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ حدیث و رخص فی السلم مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع سلم حالا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ہماری روایت کردہ حدیث میں فرمایا ایک میعاد معلوم تک ۔ اور اس لئے کہ عقد مسلم مفلسوں کی ضرورت دور کرنے کیلئے چونکہ رخصت کے طور پر مشروع کی گئی ہے، اس وجہ سے میعاد کا ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ اس میعاد میں مسلم فیہ حاصل کر کے سپرد کرنے پر قادر ہو سکے۔ اور اگر وہ بالفعل سپرد کرنے پر قادر ہو تو چونکہ رخصت دینے والا سب نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے اس کا حکم نفی کرنے والے پر باقی رہا۔

تشریح ہمارے نزدیک بغیر میعاد کے عقد سلم جائز نہیں ہے یہی مذہب امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز ہے مثلاً کسی نے کہا کہ میں نے ان دس در اہم کا عقد سلم ایک گندم (جس کی یہ صفات ہوں ) میں کیا فوری طور پر سپرد کرنے کی شرط لگاری یا میعاد نہ کی تو یہ عقد سلم ہمارے نزدیک نا جائز ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے انه نهى عن بيع ما ليس عند الانسان ورخص فی السلم ، اس حدیث میں رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیع سلم کو مطلقاً جائز قرار دیا ہے خواہ سلم میعادی ہو یا غیر میعادی ہو۔ پس اجل اور میعاد کی شرط لگا نا نص حدیث پر زیادتی کرنا ہوگا اور نص پر زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لیئے اطلاق حدیث کی وجہ سے سلم میعادی اور غیر میعادی دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول ہے " من اسلم منكم فليسلم في كيل معلوم و وزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم " اس حدیث میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جس طرح مسلم فیہ میں کیل معلوم یا وزن معلوم ہونے کی شرط بیان فرمائی ہے اسی طرح میعادی ہونے کی شرط بھی بیان فرمائی ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مسلم فیہ کا میعادی ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث مطلق و رخص في السلم کو اس حدیث پر محمول کیا جائے گا جو اجل کی قید کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیچ سلم ، مفلس اور غریب لوگوں کی ضرورت پورا کرنے کیلئے مشروع کی گئی ہے اور یہ ضرورت اُسی دلیل وقت پوری ہو سکتی ہے جب کہ مسلم فیہ ادا کرنے کیلئے ایک میعاد مقرر کی جائے تاکہ مسلم الیہ اس مدت میں مسلم فیہ حاصل کر کے رب اسلم کے سپرد کر دے۔ اور اگر مسلم الیہ فی الحال مسلم فیہ سپر د کر نے پر قادر ہو تو چونکہ اس صورت میں مرخص ( رخصت کا سبب ) یعنی ضرورت نہیں پائی گئی اس لئے حکم یعنی لا تبع ما ليس عندک کے مطابق ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ معدوم کی بیع باطل اور نا جائز ہوتی ہے لیکن مفلسوں کی ضرورت پورا کرنے کیلئے مسلم فیہ کے معدوم ہونے کے باوجود بیع سلم جائز قرار دی گئی ہے۔ مگر جب مسلم الیہ ، فی الحال مسلم فیہ سپر د کر نے پر قادر ہو تو یہ ضرورت متحقق نہ ہوگی ۔ اور جب بیع سلم کو جائز کرنے والی ضرورت متحقق نہیں ہوئی تو بیع سلم بھی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Chapter of Salam
He (al-Quduri) said: Salam is not valid except deferred. Al-Shafi'i said: It is valid spot (immediate) due to the absoluteness of the hadith 'He permitted salam.' Our proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'until a known term' as we have narrated. And because it is legislated as a concession to meet the need of the destitute, so a term is necessary to be able to obtain (the commodity) and deliver it. If he were able to deliver immediately, the concession would not exist, so it remains under the prohibition.

Translation: And the contract of salam is not valid except with a term. Imam al-Shafi'i said that due to the absoluteness of the hadith 'He permitted salam', salam is valid spot (immediate) as well. Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said in the hadith we narrated: 'until a known term.' And because the contract of salam is legislated as a concession to remove the need of the destitute, a term is necessary so that he can obtain the subject matter and deliver it within that term. If he is actually able to deliver, then the reason for the concession is not found, so its ruling remains with the prohibition.

Explanation: According to us, a salam contract without a term is not valid. This is also the madhhab of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is valid. For example, if someone says, 'I have made a salam contract for these ten dirhams for a wheat (with such attributes), stipulating immediate delivery or without specifying a term,' this salam contract is invalid according to us, but valid according to al-Shafi'i. Al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith: 'He forbade selling what is not with you, but permitted salam.' In this hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared salam absolutely permissible, whether deferred or spot. Imposing a term would be an addition to the text, and addition to the text is not allowed. So due to the absoluteness, both deferred and spot salam are valid. Our proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever among you gives salam, let him give salam with a known measure, a known weight, and until a known term.' In this hadith, just as the Prophet stipulated a known measure or weight, he also stipulated a known term. This shows that a term is necessary. The absolute hadith cited by al-Shafi'i is to be interpreted in light of this restricted one. The second proof is that salam is legislated to fulfill the need of the poor and destitute. This need can only be met if a term is set so that the seller can obtain the commodity and deliver it. If the seller is able to deliver immediately, then the reason for the concession (need) does not exist, so the ruling will be according to the prohibition: 'Do not sell what is not with you.' In conclusion, selling a non-existent thing is invalid and impermissible, but for the need of the destitute, salam is permitted despite the non-existence of the subject matter. However, if the seller can deliver immediately, this need is not realized, so salam is not valid.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the necessity of a fixed term in salam sales. The Hanafi ruling, stated by Imam al-Quduri, is that salam is only valid with a deferred term. Imam al-Shafi'i holds it valid immediately based on the absolute permission in the hadith. The Hanafi response provides two proofs: first, a hadith explicitly requiring a 'known term'; second, the wisdom behind salam as a concession for the needy, which necessitates a term to allow the seller time to acquire the goods. If the seller already possesses the goods, there is no need for this concession, so the general prohibition of selling non-existent items applies. The Hanafi position is supported by Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. The passage concludes that the Shafi'i hadith is to be interpreted in light of the explicit restriction. Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi view is that salam without a fixed term is invalid.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered at a future date, also called بيع السلم.
أجل (ajal): A fixed term or deadline for delivery of the subject matter in salam.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The buyer who pays the price in advance in a salam contract.
مسلم إليه (muslam ilayh): The seller who receives the price and is obligated to deliver the commodity at the term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on salam sale without a fixed term?
A) It is valid and permissible.
B) It is invalid because it lacks a necessary condition.
C) It is valid only if the seller is rich.
D) It is valid only for agricultural products.

Key Takeaway
Salam without a fixed term is invalid in the Hanafi school because it lacks the necessary condition for the concession of selling non-existent goods.

Known Term and Measure in Salam
Establishes conditions of known term and measure in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two mandatory conditions of a valid salam contract (known term and known measure) and explain why ignorance of the term invalidates the contract, noting the preferred minimum term of one month.

Core Idea
Salam requires a known term and standard measure; ignorance leads to dispute and invalidates.

Salam is a forward sale where the price is paid immediately and delivery deferred. The validity hinges on specifying a known term and using standard measures to prevent disputes. This lesson examines the proof from hadith and the reasoning behind these conditions, including an intra-Hanafi discussion on the minimum term duration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the central ruling: salam is only valid with a known term (ajal ma'lum) and a known measure (kayl/weight).
The text opens: 'Salam is not valid except with a known term.'
2
Locate the Dalil
Identify the primary proof: the hadith 'Whoever gives salam, let him give salam with a known measure, a known weight, and until a known term.'
This is a sunnah ahad, but its indication (dalala) is qat'i for obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the obligation: the imperative 'falyuslim' (let him give salam) combined with 'ila ajalin ma'lum' (to a known term) imposes the condition of a known term.
Ignorance of term leads to dispute (jahalah mufdiyan ila al-niza'), which invalidates the contract.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note the three opinions on the minimum term: one month, three days, more than half a day. Understand the basis for each.
First view (one month) draws analogy from oath rulings; second from khiyar al-shart; third from definition of immediate vs deferred delivery.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi view: one month, because it is a sufficient period to obtain the subject matter and is chosen by Al-Marghinani as asahh.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

باب السلم
قال ولا يجوز الا باجل معلوم لما روينا ولان الجهالة فيه مفضية الى المنازعة كما في البيع وأجل ادناه شهر وقيل ثلاثة ايام وقيل اكثر من نصف اليوم والاول اصح

ترجمہ اور بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے مگر میعاد معلوم کے ساتھ اُس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ میعاد کا مجہول ہونا مفضی الی المنازعہ ہوتا ہے، جیسا کہ بیچ میں اور میعاد کم از کم ایک ماہ ہے اور کہا گیا کہ تین روز ہیں ، اور کہا گیا کہ آدھے دن سے زیادہ ہو اور قول اول اصح ہے۔

تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جب عقد سلم میں میعاد کا شرط ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو یہ بیان کرنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ میعاد کا معلوم ہونا بھی شرط ہے اور اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی یعنی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول من اسلم منكم فليسلم في كيل معلوم و وزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ میعاد کا مجہول ہو نا مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو گا، بایں طور کہ رب السلم مدت قریبہ میں مطالبہ کرے گا اور مسلم الیہ مدت بعیدہ میں ادا کرنے کی کوشش کرے گا ۔ اور ایسی جہالت جو مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو مفسد ہوتی ہے، اس لئے میعاد کا مجہول ہونا بیع سلم کیلئے مفسد ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ بیع میں جہالت شمن اور جہالت صبح مفسد ہوتی ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ بیع سلم میں میعاد کی ادنی مدت کیا ہے؟ سواس بارے میں صاحب ہدایہ نے تین قول بیان فرمائے ہیں۔ پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ بیع سلم میں ادنی میعاد ایک ماہ ہے۔ دوسرا قول تین دن کا ہے اور تیسرا قول نصف یوم سے زیادہ کا ہے۔ پہلے قول کی دلیل کتاب الایمان کا یہ مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں تیرا قرضہ عاجلا ادا کر دوں گا، پھر ایک ماہ پورا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے ادا کر دیا تو اس شخص کی قسم پوری ہوگئی۔ اس مسئلہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک ماہ سے کم عاجل کے حکم میں ہے اور جب ایک ماہ سے کم عاجل کے حکم میں ہے تو ایک ماہ اور اس سے زائد آجل کے حکم میں ہوگا۔
دوسرے قول کی دلیل مدت خیار شرط پر ہے۔ تیسرے قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقتبل اس کو کہتے ہیں جس پر مجلس کے اندر قبضہ کر لیا جائے اور جس پر مجلس کے بعد قبضہ ہو اس کو مؤجل کہتے ہیں۔ اور عام طور پر مجلس نصف یوم تک باقی رہتی ہے، نصف یوم سے زائد باقی نہیں رہتی اس لئے اجل اور میعاد کی کم از کم مدت نصف یوم سے زائد ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فر ماتے ہیں کہ قول اول زیادہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ ایک ماہ کی میعاد ایسی مدت ہے جس میں مسلم فیہ کا حاصل کرنا ممکن ہے۔

ولا يجوز السلم بمكيال رجل بعينه ولا بذراع رجل بعينه معناه لا يُعرف مقداره لانه يتأخر فيه التسليم فربما يضيع فيودى الى المنازعة وقد مر من قبل ولابد ان يكون المكيال مما لا ينقبض ولا ينبسط
Chapter of Salam
He said: Salam is not valid except with a known term, due to what we have narrated, and because ignorance of it leads to dispute, as in sale. Its minimum term is one month. It was said: three days. And it was said: more than half a day. The first is more correct.

Translation: And salam is not valid except with a known term, due to the hadith we have narrated, and because ignorance of the term leads to dispute, as in sale. Its minimum term is one month. It was said: three days. And it was said: more than half a day. The first saying is more correct.

Explanation: Imam al-Quduri states that once it is established that a term is required, it must also be known. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever gives salam, let him give salam with a known measure, a known weight, and until a known term.' The second proof is that ignorance of the term leads to dispute, as the buyer will demand early delivery and the seller will seek delay. Such ignorance corrupts the contract, just as ignorance of price or commodity corrupts a sale. Regarding the minimum term, the author of Al-Hidayah mentions three views. The first is one month, the second three days, the third more than half a day. The first view's proof comes from the Book of Oaths: if someone swears to pay a debt promptly and pays within a month, the oath is fulfilled. This shows that less than a month is considered prompt, and a month or more is deferred. The second view's proof is based on the option period. The third view's proof is that immediate delivery is what is taken in the session; the session typically lasts half a day, so anything beyond half a day is a term. Al-Marghinani says the first view is most correct because a month is a period in which it is possible to obtain the subject matter.

And salam is not valid with the measure of a particular man nor with the cubit of a particular man, meaning its quantity is unknown. Because delivery would be delayed, and it may get lost, leading to dispute. This has been mentioned before. It is necessary that the measure be something that does not shrink or expand.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the conditions of salam, specifically that the term must be known. The author (al-Quduri) states that salam is only valid with a known term, citing the hadith that requires a 'known measure, known weight, and known term.' The reason is that ignorance of the term leads to dispute, which invalidates the contract, just as in ordinary sales ignorance of price or commodity is invalidating. The passage then discusses the minimum duration of the term. Three opinions are presented: (1) one month, (2) three days, and (3) more than half a day. The first opinion is considered most correct by the author of Al-Hidayah because a month is sufficient for the seller to acquire the subject matter. The proof for one month is drawn from the chapter on oaths: if someone swears to pay a debt 'promptly' and pays within a month, it counts as prompt, implying that a month or more is deferred. The second view leans on the option period (khiyar al-shart), and the third on the typical duration of a sitting (majlis). Finally, the text adds that salam is not valid using an individual's specific measure or cubit because that creates uncertainty in quantity, leading to potential disputes. The measure must be standard and non-variable. This completes the conditions for a valid salam contract: a known term and a known, standard measure.

Key Terms
أجل معلوم (ajal ma'lum): A term that is fixed and known to both parties, preventing dispute.
مكيال (mikyāl): A standard measure of volume, like a sa' or mud.
ذراع (dhirā'): A cubit, used for measuring length.
جهالة (jahālah): Uncertainty or ignorance of a necessary element that leads to dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One day
B) Three days
C) One month
D) More than half a day

Key Takeaway
A valid salam contract requires a known term (at least one month) and a standard, known measure; ignorance of either invalidates the contract.

Requirement of Known Fixed Term in Salam Sale
States ruling that salam requires known term and discusses minimum duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of a known term in salam and identify the minimum duration according to the relied-upon opinion.

Core Idea
Salam requires a known term; ignorance leads to dispute. The minimum term is one month.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a contract where the price is paid upfront but the commodity is delivered later. To prevent disputes, the delivery term must be known. This lesson explores the evidence and the minimum term required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'Salam is not valid except with a known term.' This is the core ruling. Understand that the term (ajal) is an essential condition.
2
Analyze the dalil
The evidence includes a prophetic hadith (command to specify known measure, weight, and term) and rational analogy: ignorance of the term leads to dispute, just as in ordinary sale.
The imperative 'فليسلم' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the minimum term debate
Three opinions exist: one month (Imam Abu Hanifa), three days, and more than half a day. Understand the reasoning behind each.
The one-month view is supported by an oath analogy: paying within a month is considered 'immediate'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The author declares the first opinion (one month) most correct because it provides sufficient time to procure the commodity and avoids dispute.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد - نیم
بیع سلم کیلئے اجل معلوم ضروری ہے
قال ولا يجوز الا باجل معلوم لما روينا ولان الجهالة فيه مفضية الى المنازعة كما في البيع والأجل ادناه شهر وقيل ثلاثة ايام وقيل اكثر من نصف اليوم والاول اصح
ترجمہ اور بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے مگر میعاد معلوم کے ساتھ اُس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ میعاد کا مجہول ہونا مفضی الی المنازعہ ہوتا ہے، جیسا کہ بیج میں اور میعاد کم از کم ایک ماہ ہے اور کہا گیا کہ تین روز ہیں ، اور کہا گیا کہ آدھے دن سے زیادہ ہو اور قول اول اصح ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جب عقد سلم میں میعاد کا شرط ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو یہ بیان کرنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ میعاد کا معلوم ہونا بھی شرط ہے اور اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی یعنی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول من اسلم منكم فليسلم في كيل معلوم و وزن
معلوم الى اجل معلوم
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ میعاد کا مجہول ہو نا مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو گا، بایں طور کہ رب السلم مدت قریبہ میں مطالبہ کرے گا اور مسلم الیہ مدت بعیدہ میں ادا کرنے کی کوشش کرے گا ۔ اور ایسی جہالت جو مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو مفسد ہوتی ہے، اس لئے میعاد کا مجہول ہونا بیع سلم کیلئے مفسد ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ بیع میں جہالت شمن اور جہالت صبح مفسد ہوتی ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ بیع سلم میں میعاد کی ادنی مدت کیا ہے؟ سواس بارے میں صاحب ہدایہ نے تین قول بیان فرمائے ہیں۔ پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ بیع سلم میں ادنی میعاد ایک ماہ ہے۔ دوسرا قول تین دن کا ہے اور تیسرا قول نصف یوم سے زیادہ کا ہے۔ پہلے قول کی دلیل کتاب الایمان کا یہ مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں تیرا قرضہ عاجلا ادا کر دوں گا، پھر ایک ماہ پورا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے ادا کر دیا تو اس شخص کی قسم پوری ہوگئی۔ اس مسئلہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک ماہ سے کم عاجل کے حکم میں ہے اور جب ایک ماہ سے کم عاجل کے حکم میں ہے تو ایک ماہ اور اس سے زائد آجل کے حکم میں ہوگا۔
دوسرے قول کی دلیل مدت خیار شرط پر ہے۔ تیسرے قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقتبل اس کو کہتے ہیں جس پر مجلس کے اندر قبضہ کر لیا جائے اور جس پر مجلس کے بعد قبضہ ہو اس کو یہ کہ جائےاور مؤجل کہتے ہیں۔ اور عام طور پر مجلس نصف یوم تک باقی رہتی ہے، نصف یوم سے زائد باقی نہیں رہتی اس لئے اجل اور میعاد کی کم از کم مدت نصف یوم سے زائد ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فر ماتے ہیں کہ قول اول زیادہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ ایک ماہ کی میعاد ایسی مدت ہے جس میں مسلم فیہ کا حاصل کرنا ممکن ہے۔
Salam is not valid except with a known fixed term, due to the hadith we narrated and because ignorance in it leads to dispute, as in sale. The minimum term is one month; it is said three days; it is said more than half a day. The first is most correct. (Then Urdu commentary explaining the proofs and the three opinions with their evidence.)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter of Salam (advance payment sale). The author states the first ruling: salam is not valid unless the delivery term is known. Two proofs are given: a prophetic hadith (with similar wording) and a rational argument that ignorance of the term leads to dispute, just as in ordinary sale where ignorance of price or measure invalidates the contract. The commentary then discusses the minimum length of the term. Three opinions are reported: one month (Imam Abu Hanifa's view, supported by a case from the Book of Oaths where paying within a month is deemed 'immediate'), three days, or more than half a day. The author declares the first opinion strongest because a month is sufficient time for the seller to procure the commodity.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A sale where the price is paid immediately and the commodity is delivered at a future date; also called salaf.
الأجل (al-ajal): The fixed term or deadline for delivery of the commodity in a salam contract.
الجهالة (al-jahālah): Ignorance or ambiguity about a material term of the contract that leads to dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum fixed term (ajal) for a valid salam contract according to the most correct view?
A) Three days
B) Half a day
C) One month
D) One year

Key Takeaway
Salam requires a known term; the Hanafi school holds the minimum is one month to ensure feasibility and avoid dispute.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Prohibition of Salam with Unknown Personal Measure
Clarifies that salam using an individual's unstandardized measure or yardstick is invalid due to uncertainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on salam using an unknown personal measure and identify the exception for compressible containers based on custom.

Core Idea
An unknown personal measure invalidates salam; only a known, rigid standard prevents dispute.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical concern in salam contracts: the measure used to quantify the deferred goods must be objectively known and physically stable. A personal measure that is unique or compressible creates uncertainty (jahalah) that can lead to disputes. The Hanafi school provides an exception for water skins, based on the customary practice of the people, as narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited measures and the reason
Locate the ruling that salam with a specific person's measure (mikyāl rajul) or yardstick (dhirā' rajul) is invalid. The reason given is that the quantity is unknown because delivery is deferred, and the measure might be lost leading to dispute.
The commentary clarifies that if the measure's capacity is known, the contract is valid.
2
Understand the condition of rigidity
The text states that the measure must not contract or expand (la yanqabid wa la yanbasit). Examples given are bowls (qaṣ'). This prevents manipulation by compressing or stretching the container.
Compressible containers like baskets and sacks are invalid due to the same potential for dispute.
3
Note the general ruling of invalidity
Based on the above, salam with an unknown personal measure or a compressible container is fasid (invalid) because it leads to dispute.
This is the default position from the zahir al-riwayah.
4
Recognize the exception for water skins
An exception is made for water skins (qirbah) despite being compressible. This is based on the narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, who relied on the widespread custom (ta'amul) of people trading water skins with such containers.
Custom ('urf) is given legal weight in Hanafi fiqh, especially in muamalat.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi difference
The general rule is from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, while Abu Yusuf allows the exception. Al-Marghinani presents the exception without rejecting it, indicating its acceptance as mufta bihi.
The exception demonstrates istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas.

Source Text

ولا يجوز السلم بمكيال رجل بعينه ولا بذراع رجل بعينه معناه لا يُعرف مقداره لانه يتأخر فيه التسليم فربما يضيع فيودى الى المنازعة وقد مر من قبل ولابد ان يكون المكيال مما لا ينقبض ولا ينبسط

باب السلم
اشرف الہدایہ جلد نم كالقصاع مثلا فان كان مما ينكبس بالكبس كالزنبيل والجراب لا يجوز للمنازعة الا في قرب الماء للتعامل فيه كذا روى عن أبي يوسف
ترجمہ اور بیع سلم کسی معین آدمی کے پیانہ اور معین آدمی کے گز سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے کیونکہ عقد سلم میں مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنا تاخیر سے ہوتا ہے ، پس بسا اوقات وہ مخصوص پیمانہ یا مخصوص گز ضائع ہو جائے گا تو جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا ، اور یہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔ اور ضروری ہے کہ پیمانہ نہ سکڑتا ہو اور نہ پھیلتا ہو جیسے مثلاً کا سہ ہے۔ پس اگر بھینچنے سے بھینچ جاتا ہو جیسے زنبیل اور تھیلا تو جھگڑے کی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے مگر پانی کی مشکوں میں کیونکہ اس میں لوگوں کا تعامل جاری ہے۔ ایسا ہی امام ابو
یوسف سے مروی ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کی معین شخص کا ایسا ذاتی پیمانہ ہو جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو یازاتی گز ہو جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہوتو اس پیمانہ اور گز سے بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بیع سلم میں مسلم فیہ کی سپردگی میعاد تک مؤخر ہوتی ہے اور اس عرصہ میں اس مخصوص پیمانے اور گز کا ضائع ہو ناممکن ہے۔ پس ضائع ہونے کی صورت میں مسلم فیہ سپر د کرتے وقت رب السلم اور مسلم الیہ کے درمیان جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا، باتیں طور کہ رب السلام پیمانے کے بڑا ہونے کا دعوی کرے گا اور مسلم الیہ چھوٹا ہونے کا مدعی ہوگا ۔ اور ایسی چیز جو جھگڑا پیدا کرے مفسد بیع ہوتی ہے، اس لئے ایسے مخصوص پیمانے اور مخصوص گزسے جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہ مسئلہ اول کتاب البیوع میں گذر چکا ہے۔ مذکورہ دلیل سے یہ بات واضح ہو جاتی ہے کہ اُس مخصوص پیمانے یا مخصوص گز کی اگر مقدار معلوم ہو تو بیع سلم جائز ہے کیونکہ مقدار معلوم ہونے کے بعد اگر وہ برتن اور پیمانہ ضائع بھی ہو گیا تب بھی جھگڑے کا کوئی امکان نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر اُس پیمانے کی مقدار تو معلوم نہ ہو مگر بیع کی سپردگی فوری ہے تو بھی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں پیمانہ کا ضائع ہونا انتہائی نادر ہے۔ اور جب اس مخصوص پیمانہ کا ضائع ہونا نا در ہے تو کوئی جھگڑا بھی پیدا نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ پیمانہ جس سے مسلم فیہ ناپنے کی شرط کی گئی ہے ربڑ کی طرح نہ سکڑتا اور نہ پھیلتا ہو بلکہ لو ہے یامٹی یا لکڑی یا اس کے مانند کسی ٹھوس چیز کا ہو جیسے پیالہ، بالٹی یا طشت کہ یہ چیزیں نہ سکڑتی ہیں اور نہ پھیلتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ پیمانہ اگر ایسا ہو جو بھینچنے سے بھینچ جاتا ہو اور پھیلانے سے پھیل جاتا ہو تو اس سے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی جھگڑا پیدا ہوگا، بایں طور کہ مشتری اور رب السلم مطالبہ کرے گا کہ پیمانہ کو خوب پھیلا کر بھرا جائے اور بائع اور مسلم الیہ کی آخری کوشش یہ ہوگی کہ اس کو ایسے انداز میں بھینچ کر بھرا جائے کہ مبیع کم سے کم آئے اور جھگڑا مفسد بیع ہے۔ اس لئے ایسے ظرف سے بیع کرنا فاسد اور نا جائز ہے۔ ہاں ! امام ابو یوسف کی روایت کے مطابق پانی کی مشکوں کی بیع جائز ہے باوجود یکہ مشک خوب تان دینے سے زیادہ بھرتی ہے اور دبانے سے کم بھرتی ہے۔ اس کی دلیل لوگوں کا تعامل ہے کیونکہ لوگوں کا یہ عمل برابر جاری ہے کہ وہ ستوں سے پانی کی مشکیں خریدتے ہیں ۔
Salam is not valid with the measure of a specific man nor with the yardstick of a specific man, meaning its quantity is not known because delivery is delayed and perhaps it will be lost leading to dispute, and it has passed before. And the measure must not contract nor expand, like bowls. If it is compressible like a basket or sack, it is not valid due to dispute, except in water skins because of mutual dealing (ta'amul). Thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf. (Then Urdu commentary explaining the ruling in detail.)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents a second ruling: salam cannot be executed using a particular individual's measure or yardstick whose standard size is unknown. The reason is that salam involves deferred delivery; if the unique measure is lost or damaged before delivery, the parties will dispute the actual quantity. This principle was already established earlier in the book of sales. The commentary further explains that if the measure's capacity is actually known (e.g., it is a standard container), then the salam is valid even if the utensil is lost, because no dispute arises. Similarly, if delivery is immediate (not salam), the risk of loss is negligible, so it is valid. The text also specifies that the measuring instrument must be rigid (not compressible/expandable) to avoid manipulation. However, an exception is made for water skins (qirbah) based on Imam Abu Yusuf's narration, because people customarily trade water skins by visual estimation regardless of compressibility, and this custom ('urf) is given legal weight.

Key Terms
المكيال (al-mikyāl): A measuring vessel used to determine volume, such as a bowl (qaṣ') or bucket.
الذراع (al-dhirā'): A linear measure (cubit) used for length; here specifically the personal cubit of an individual.
التعامل (al-ta'āmul): Customary practice or mutual dealing among people in a particular trade or location.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam with a specific person's measure (mikyāl rajul) invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is not a standard measure recognized by the market.
B) Because the measure might be lost before delivery, causing a dispute over quantity.
C) Because only the Prophet's measure can be used.
D) Because the seller's measure is always considered trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires a known, rigid measure; otherwise it is invalid, except where custom allows otherwise, such as water skins per Abu Yusuf.

6 min
Salam with a Specific Vessel: Ruling and Custom Exception
Explains the ruling on Salam sale with a specific vessel or yardstick of unknown measurement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salam sale using a specific person's unknown measuring vessel and identify the exception for water skins based on custom (ta'amul).

Core Idea
A Salam contract with a specific unknown vessel is invalid because it leads to inevitable dispute.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a buyer orders goods in a Salam contract but agrees to measure them using the seller's personal cup or yardstick. If that unique item is lost, the parties will inevitably dispute the actual quantity. The Hanafi school rules such a contract corrupt (fasid), but makes an exception for water skins due to widespread custom. Understanding the rational proof and the role of custom is essential for applying the rules of Salam correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a Salam sale where the subject matter is to be measured using a specific person's measuring cup or yardstick whose capacity is unknown. The ruling is that the sale is fasid (corrupt) and invalid.
This applies only when the vessel's capacity is unknown; if known, the sale is valid.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): Salam involves deferred delivery, and if the specific vessel is lost or damaged before delivery, the buyer and seller will dispute the quantity. Dispute (niza') invalidates the contract.
The proof is not from a text but from the principles of avoiding gharar and conflict.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: the vessel may be lost → no objective measure remains → parties cannot agree on quantity → dispute arises → dispute invalidates the sale. The causal link is the potential for dispute, which is a recognized cause of fasād in sales.
This logic also requires that the vessel itself must be non-deformable; compressible vessels allow manipulation and thus dispute.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) reportedly allowed Salam with water skins despite their compressibility, based on widespread custom (ta'amul). The general rule remains for other compressible containers.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi position follows the general prohibition except for water skins.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (as in Al-Hidayah) is that Salam with an unknown specific vessel is invalid, but water skins are excepted because of custom. The exception does not extend to other compressible containers like baskets or sacks.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah; the exception is narrated from Abu Yusuf and accepted by later scholars.

Source Text

باب السلم
اشرف الہدایہ جلد نم كالقصاع مثلا فان كان مما ينكبس بالكبس كالزنبيل والجراب لا يجوز للمنازعة الا في قرب الماء للتعامل فيه كذا روى عن أبي يوسف
ترجمہ اور بیع سلم کسی معین آدمی کے پیانہ اور معین آدمی کے گز سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے کیونکہ عقد سلم میں مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنا تاخیر سے ہوتا ہے ، پس بسا اوقات وہ مخصوص پیمانہ یا مخصوص گز ضائع ہو جائے گا تو جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا ، اور یہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔ اور ضروری ہے کہ پیمانہ نہ سکڑتا ہو اور نہ پھیلتا ہو جیسے مثلاً کا سہ ہے۔ پس اگر بھینچنے سے بھینچ جاتا ہو جیسے زنبیل اور تھیلا تو جھگڑے کی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے مگر پانی کی مشکوں میں کیونکہ اس میں لوگوں کا تعامل جاری ہے۔ ایسا ہی امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کی معین شخص کا ایسا ذاتی پیمانہ ہو جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو یازاتی گز ہو جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہوتو اس پیمانہ اور گز سے بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بیع سلم میں مسلم فیہ کی سپردگی میعاد تک مؤخر ہوتی ہے اور اس عرصہ میں اس مخصوص پیمانے اور گز کا ضائع ہو ناممکن ہے۔ پس ضائع ہونے کی صورت میں مسلم فیہ سپر د کرتے وقت رب السلم اور مسلم الیہ کے درمیان جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا، باتیں طور کہ رب السلام پیمانے کے بڑا ہونے کا دعوی کرے گا اور مسلم الیہ چھوٹا ہونے کا مدعی ہوگا ۔ اور ایسی چیز جو جھگڑا پیدا کرے مفسد بیع ہوتی ہے، اس لئے ایسے مخصوص پیمانے اور مخصوص گزسے جس کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہ مسئلہ اول کتاب البیوع میں گذر چکا ہے۔ مذکورہ دلیل سے یہ بات واضح ہو جاتی ہے کہ اُس مخصوص پیمانے یا مخصوص گز کی اگر مقدار معلوم ہو تو بیع سلم جائز ہے کیونکہ مقدار معلوم ہونے کے بعد اگر وہ برتن اور پیمانہ ضائع بھی ہو گیا تب بھی جھگڑے کا کوئی امکان نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر اُس پیمانے کی مقدار تو معلوم نہ ہو مگر بیع کی سپردگی فوری ہے تو بھی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں پیمانہ کا ضائع ہونا انتہائی نادر ہے۔ اور جب اس مخصوص پیمانہ کا ضائع ہونا نا در ہے تو کوئی جھگڑا بھی پیدا نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ پیمانہ جس سے مسلم فیہ ناپنے کی شرط کی گئی ہے ربڑ کی طرح نہ سکڑتا اور نہ پھیلتا ہو بلکہ لو ہے یامٹی یا لکڑی یا اس کے مانند کسی ٹھوس چیز کا ہو جیسے پیالہ، بالٹی یا طشت کہ یہ چیزیں نہ سکڑتی ہیں اور نہ پھیلتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ پیمانہ اگر ایسا ہو جو بھینچنے سے بھینچ جاتا ہو اور پھیلانے سے پھیل جاتا ہو تو اس سے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی جھگڑا پیدا ہوگا، بایں طور کہ مشتری اور رب السلم مطالبہ کرے گا کہ پیمانہ کو خوب پھیلا کر بھرا جائے اور بائع اور مسلم الیہ کی آخری کوشش یہ ہوگی کہ اس کو ایسے انداز میں بھینچ کر بھرا جائے کہ مبیع کم سے کم آئے اور جھگڑا مفسد بیع ہے۔ اس لئے ایسے ظرف سے بیع کرنا فاسد اور نا جائز ہے۔ ہاں ! امام ابو یوسف کی روایت کے مطابق پانی کی مشکوں کی بیع جائز ہے باوجود یکہ مشک خوب تان دینے سے زیادہ بھرتی ہے اور دبانے سے کم بھرتی ہے۔ اس کی دلیل لوگوں کا تعامل ہے کیونکہ لوگوں کا یہ عمل برابر جاری ہے کہ وہ ستوں سے پانی کی مشکیں خریدتے ہیں ۔
Chapter of Salam. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume no. ... Like bowls for example. If it is something that compresses upon pressing, like the basket and the sack, it is not permissible due to dispute, except in the case of water skins because of custom. Thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf. Translation: Salam sale is not permissible with a specific person's measuring cup or a specific person's yardstick. The meaning is that its quantity is not known because in a Salam contract, delivery of the subject matter is delayed. So sometimes that specific measuring cup or yardstick will be lost, then dispute will occur, and this has passed earlier. And it is necessary that the measuring vessel neither contracts nor expands, like bowls for example. So if it compresses when pressed, like a basket and a sack, it is not permissible due to dispute, except in water skins because people customarily deal with them. Similarly narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf. Commentary: The scenario is that if a specific person has a personal measuring cup whose quantity is unknown, or a personal yardstick whose quantity is unknown, then Salam sale with that cup and yardstick is not permissible. Because in Salam, delivery of the subject matter is deferred until the term, and during that period it is possible for that specific cup and yardstick to be lost. If they are lost, then at the time of delivery, dispute will arise between the buyer and the seller, for the buyer will claim the cup is large and the seller will claim it is small. And anything that leads to dispute invalidates the sale. Therefore, Salam is not permissible with such a specific cup or yardstick whose quantity is unknown. This issue has passed earlier in the first chapter of sales. From the mentioned reasoning, it becomes clear that if the quantity of that specific cup or yardstick is known, then Salam is permissible because after the quantity is known, even if the vessel or yardstick is lost, there is no possibility of dispute. Similarly, if the quantity of that vessel is not known but delivery is immediate, then the sale is also permissible because in that case, loss of the vessel is extremely rare, so no dispute would arise. The author of Hidayah says that the vessel with which the subject matter is to be measured should not contract or expand like rubber, but should be of iron, clay, wood, or similar solid substance, like a bowl, bucket, or tray, which neither contract nor expand. So if the vessel is such that it compresses when pressed and expands when stretched, then sale with it is not permissible because dispute would arise, as the buyer and the person ordering the Salam would demand that the vessel be filled while fully stretched, while the seller would try to fill it in a compressed manner so that the goods are less, and dispute invalidates the sale. Thus, sale with such a container is corrupt and impermissible. However, according to the narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, the sale of water skins is permissible even though a water skin can be filled more when stretched and less when pressed. Its proof is the custom of people, because people commonly buy water skins from water carriers.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and its proof regarding Salam sale using a specific person's measuring vessel or yardstick. It begins by stating the general rule: Salam is not valid with a specific person's cup or yardstick if its capacity is unknown. The reason is that Salam involves deferred delivery, and if that unique item is lost, the parties will dispute over the actual quantity. The passage then clarifies that the measuring vessel must be rigid, like a bowl, not compressible like a basket or sack, to avoid manipulation. However, an exception is made for water skins because of widespread custom—people routinely buy water skins using such vessels despite their variability. This exception is attributed to a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf. The commentary expands on the rationale: if the capacity of the specific vessel is known, or if delivery is immediate (so the vessel is unlikely to be lost), the contract is valid. The text also emphasizes that the vessel should not be stretchable, as that would lead to disputes over whether it was filled loosely or tightly. The Hanafi position is that the primary concern is the avoidance of conflict (niza'), which invalidates the contract. The relied-upon position is that Salam is impermissible with an unknown specific vessel, except for water skins due to custom (urf).

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance for goods to be delivered later.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The buyer in a Salam contract who pays the price in advance.
مسلم الیہ (muslam ilayh): The seller in a Salam contract who receives the price and must deliver the goods later.
نزاع (niza'): Dispute; a cause that invalidates the contract because it leads to uncertainty (gharar).
تعامل (ta'amul): Customary practice among people that can override a general ruling in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Salam sale with a specific person's measuring cup of unknown capacity invalid?
A) Because the cup might break
B) Because it leads to dispute if the cup is lost
C) Because Salam requires the goods to be measured by a standard measure
D) Because the cup may be stolen

Key Takeaway
A Salam contract using a specific person's measuring vessel is invalid unless its capacity is known and the vessel is non-deformable, except for water skins due to custom.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Salam in Specific Village Crops or Trees is Invalid
States the ruling and proof for Salam in specific sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salam in specific sources, apply the condition of guarantee of delivery, and distinguish between descriptive and specifying attributions.

Core Idea
Salam in a specific source is invalid unless the place name describes quality, not location.

Salam (forward sale) requires certainty of delivery at the due date. If the goods are tied to a unique source that could be destroyed, the contract becomes invalid due to risk. However, if a place name merely indicates a quality grade, the contract is valid. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and the critical distinction between specification and description.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: Salam (salam) in the produce of a specific village or the fruit of a specific tree. The ruling is that it is fasid (void).
The ruling is stated at the start of the passage.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about Salam in the fruits of a specific garden and replied with a rhetorical question about consuming a brother's wealth unlawfully if the fruit is destroyed.
The hadith is the primary proof (dalil naqli).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet's question implies that if the specific fruit is destroyed, the buyer's money is taken without return, making it unlawful. This establishes that Salam in a specific source is invalid because of the risk of total loss.
The reasoning (ta'lil) is the risk of calamity (afah) preventing delivery.
4
Identify the exception
Note the exception: if the attribution to a village is for describing quality (sifah), not specification (ta'yin), then the Salam is valid. Examples: 'Khushmarani wheat' means high-quality wheat, not necessarily from the village of Khushmaran.
This exception is crucial for practical contracts.
5
Apply the ruling to modern contexts
Consider modern Salam contracts in agriculture or commodities: specifying 'wheat from my field' is invalid, but 'Grade A Basmati rice' is valid even if named after a region.
The key is whether the source is uniquely identified or merely a quality marker.

معين گاؤں کے اناج معتین درختوں کے پھل میں بیچ مسلم جائز نہیں
قال ولا فى طعام قرية بعينها أو ثمرة نخلة بعينها لأنه قد يعتريه افة فلا يقدر على التسليم واليه اشار عليه السلام حيث قال أرأيت لو ذهب الله تعالى الثمر بم يستحل احدكم مال اخيه ولو كانت النسبة الى قرية لبيان الصفة لا بأس به على ما قالوا كالخُشمراني ببخارا والبساخى بفرغانة
ترجمہ اور کسی متعینہ گاؤں کے اناج یا متعینہ درخت کے پھلوں میں بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ کبھی اس پر آفت طاری ہو جاتی ہے تو وہ اس کو سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرح آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد فرمایا کہ دیکھو تو اگر اللہ تعالیٰ پھلوں کو ضائع کر دے تو تم میں سے کوئی آدمی کس چیز کے عوض اپنے بھائی کے مال کو حلال سمجھے گا اور اگر گاؤں کی طرف نسبت کرنا صفت بیان کرنے کیلئے ہو تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے جیسا کہ مشائخ نے کہا ہے جیسے بخارا میں شمرانی گندم یا فرغانہ میں، بساخی کہلاتے ہیں۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی متعینہ گاؤں کے اناج یا متعینہ درخت یا متعینہ باغ کے پھلوں کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلا دیو بند کے گندم یاد ہرہ دون کے چاول یا حامد کے باغ کے پھلوں کی بیع سلم کی تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ کبھی اس متعینہ گاؤں کے اناج یا متعینہ درخت کے پھلوں پر آسمانی آفت آکر اُس کو تباہ و برباد کر دیتی ہے اور وہ مخصوص گاؤں کا اناج یا مخصوص درخت یا مخصوص باغ کے پھل لوگوں کے ہاتھ سے منقطع ہو جاتے ہیں اور بازار میں دستیاب نہیں ہوتے ۔ اور جب یہ بات ہے تو مسلم الیہ مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہ ہوگا۔ اور چونکہ جس صورت میں مسلم الیہ مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو اس ی الیہ صورت میں بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہوتی، اس لئے متعین گاؤں کے اناج یا متعین درخت یا متعین باغ کے پھلوں کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرف رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اشارہ فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ مروی ہے انه سئل عن السلم في ثمر فلان فقال اما من ثمر حائط فلان فلا أرأيت اذهب الله الثمر بم يستحل احدكم مال احیه یعنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم سے فلاں آدمی کے پھلوں کی سلم کے بارے میں دریافت کیا گیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ فلاں آدمی کے باغ کے پھلوں کی بیع سلم تو جائز نہیں ہے، بھلا اگر اللہ تعالی نے فلاں آدمی کے پھلوں کو ضائع فرما دیا تو تم میں سے کوئی کس چیز کے عوض اپنے بھائی کے مال کو حلال سمجھے گا ؟ حاصل حدیث یہ ہے کہ متعینہ آدمی کے باغ کے پھلوں کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر وہ متعینہ باغ آفت سماوی کے نتیجہ میں برباد ہو گیا تو اپنے بھائی یعنی رب السلم کے راس المال کو کس چیز کے عوض حلال سمجھو گے۔ یعنی جب وہ متعینہ پھل ہلاک ہو جانے کی وجہ سے رب السلام کو حاصل نہ ہوئے تو مسلم الیہ کے واسطے رأس المال کس طرح حلال ہو گا۔ اس حدیث سے یہ بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ کسی متعینہ گاؤں کے اناج یا متعینہ درخت یا متعینہ باغ کے پھلوں کی بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر کسی گاؤں کی طرف نسبت کرنا صفت بیان کرنے کی غرض سے ہو، مثلا ملیح آباد کا آم جب بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے ملیح آباد متعینہ مقام مراد نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ ملیح آباد جیسے آم مطلوب ہیں خواہ ملیح آباد میں پیدا شدہ ہوں خواہ دوسری کسی جگہ میں پیدا شدہ ہوں۔ پس اگر گاؤں کی طرف نسبت محض صفت بیان کرنے کیلئے ہے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اس صورت میں بیع سلم جائز ہے، جیسے بخارا میں اُس گندم کو مسلم فیہ بنایا جو بخارا کے ایک گاؤں شمر ان کی طرف منسوب ہے، اور فرغانہ میں اُس گندم کو مسلم فیہ قرار دیا جو فرغانہ کے گاؤں پساخ کی طرف منسوب ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ بخارا میں عمدہ گندم خشمروان کا اور فرغانہ میں پساخ کا کہلاتا ہے۔ پس اگر خشمرانی یا بسانی گندم مسلم فیہ قرار دیا جائے تو اس سے ان متعینہ جگہوں کا گندم مراد نہیں ہوگا بلکہ یہ مراد ہو گا کہ گندم عمدہ ہو جیسے خشمران اور بساخ کا ہوتا ہے، خواہ وہ یہاں کا ہو یا دوسری جگہ کا۔
Salam in the crops of a specific village or fruits of specific trees is not permissible. He said: And not in the food of a specific village or the fruit of a specific palm tree, because it may be afflicted by a calamity, so he will not be able to deliver. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) indicated this when he said: 'Do you think if Allah takes away the fruit, how can anyone of you consume his brother's wealth lawfully?' And if the attribution to a village is for describing the quality, there is no harm, as they said, like al-Khushmarani in Bukhara and al-Basakhi in Farghana. Translation: Salam sale is not permissible in the crops of a specific village or fruits of a specific tree, because sometimes a calamity befalls them, so he will not be able to deliver. Similarly, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Look, if Allah destroys the fruits, how can any of you consider your brother's wealth lawful?' And if the attribution to a village is for describing the quality, then there is no harm, as the scholars said, like the wheat attributed to Khushmaran in Bukhara and to Basakh in Farghana. Commentary: Al-Quduri states that Salam is not permissible in the crops of a specific village or fruits of a specific tree or garden, for example, wheat from Deoband, rice from Dehra Dun, or fruits of Hamed's garden. The evidence is that sometimes a heavenly calamity strikes and destroys that specific village's crops or tree's fruits, and they become unavailable in the market. Then the seller will not be able to deliver. And since Salam is not valid when the seller cannot deliver, it is impermissible. The Prophet (peace be upon him) indicated this: He was asked about Salam in the fruits of a specific person, and he said: 'As for the fruits of so-and-so's garden, no. Do you think if Allah destroys the fruits, how can any of you consume your brother's wealth lawfully?' This hadith establishes the ruling. However, if the attribution to a village is merely for describing the quality, e.g., 'mango from Malihabad' means mangoes like those from Malihabad, not necessarily from that specific place, then it is permissible. Similarly, in Bukhara, the wheat attributed to Khushmaran is a description of high quality, not necessarily from that specific village.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its proof, specifically that Salam in the produce of a specific village or tree is invalid. The ruling is from the matn of Al-Hidayah, and the commentary expands with a hadith and reasoning. The key reason is that if the specific source is destroyed by a natural calamity, the seller cannot deliver the goods, rendering the contract void. The hadith about the Prophet (peace be upon him) being asked about Salam in the fruits of a specific garden directly supports this. However, an important exception is made: if the attribution to a place is merely a description of quality (e.g., 'Khushmarani wheat' meaning high-quality wheat, not necessarily from Khushmaran), then the contract is valid. This is because the purpose is to define the quality, not to restrict the source. The scholars of the Hanafi school, like the author, affirm that such descriptive naming is permissible. The commentary gives examples from Bukhara and Farghana where wheat is named after villages but used as a quality standard. Thus, the ruling balances the need to avoid risk of non-delivery with the practical reality of descriptive naming in commerce.

Key Terms
قرية (qaryah): A specific village; the source of the crop.
نخلة (nakhlah): A specific palm tree; the source of the fruit.
آفة (afah): A calamity that destroys the crop, preventing delivery.
نسبة (nisbah): Attribution to a place; can be for description or for specification.
صفة (sifah): Quality; when the place name indicates a type of quality, not a specific location.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is Salam in the produce of a specific village permissible?
A) When the village produces excellent crops
B) When the village name is used to describe the quality of the produce
C) When the village is large and prosperous
D) Never, because it always involves uncertainty

Key Takeaway
Salam in the produce of a specific source is invalid due to risk of non-delivery, but descriptive place names indicating quality are permissible.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Dispute on Conditions of Salam: Capital Quantity and Place of Delivery
Intra-Hanafi dispute on two conditions of salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions disputed between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in salam, and apply Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning to evaluate a scenario where counterfeit coins appear in the capital.

Core Idea
In salam, ignorance of capital quantity leads to ignorance of the subject matter, making the contract invalid.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents two conditions of salam over which Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ. The first is whether the quantity of the capital (ra's al-mal) must be specified when it is determined by pointing. The second is whether the place of delivery of the subject matter (muslam fih) must be specified when it is heavy and incurs transport costs. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a single fiqh issue can yield two valid yet conflicting rulings based on different analogies (qiyas) and juristic preferences (istihsan).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disputed conditions
Read the passage carefully and identify the two conditions of salam that Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on. Note that the first concerns the specification of the capital's quantity, and the second concerns the specification of the place of delivery.
The conditions are: (1) specifying the quantity of ra's al-mal when it is determined by pointing, and (2) specifying the place of delivery of the muslam fih when it has weight and transport cost.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The Sahibayn argue that pointing to the capital suffices because the purpose—delivery of the capital—is achieved by pointing. They analogize it to price (thaman) in a sale and hire (ujrah) in a lease, where pointing is valid without stating quantity. They also analogize it to a cloth (thawb), where mentioning cubits is merely a description and does not affect the contract's relation to quantity.
Key analogy: capital is like price—pointing achieves the contractual purpose.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his counter-proof
Abu Hanifa argues that ignorance of the capital's quantity leads to ignorance of the subject matter's quantity. His proof: if some dirhams turn out to be counterfeit (zuyuf) and are not exchanged in the same session, the total quantity must be known to determine how much of the muslam fih remains valid. Otherwise, the contract becomes fasid due to uncertainty (jahalah).
Counter-analogy: counterfeit coins reveal latent ignorance that cannot be resolved without knowing the full quantity.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to Abu Hanifa, if the capital's quantity is not specified (even if pointed to), the salam contract is fasid. According to the Sahibayn, it is sahih. Similarly, for the place of delivery, Abu Hanifa requires specification if the subject matter is heavy; the Sahibayn hold that delivery at the contract place suffices.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa for precaution, though the Sahibayn's view is also recognized.
5
Apply the ruling to a branch case
The passage mentions a branch: if someone makes salam in two types (e.g., two different commodities) and does not specify the capital for each, or makes salam of two types and does not specify the quantity of one, the same dispute applies. Apply Abu Hanifa's reasoning to such scenarios.
Branch rulings reinforce the principle that ignorance of capital quantity leads to invalidity.
