و لا يستبدل في المجلس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر مسلم الیہ نے دراہم زیوف کے بدلے اسی مجلس میں گھرے دراہم لے لئے جس مجلس میں در اہم زیوف واپس کئے گئے ہیں تو بیع سلم فاسد نہیں ہوتی ، حالانکہ ایسا نہیں، بلکہ اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ اگر نصف دراہم سے کم زیوف ہوں تو جس مجلس میں ان کو رب السلام کی طرف واپس کیا گیا ہے اگر اسی مجلس میں ان کے بدلے کھرے دراہم لے لئے تو بالا تفاق احناف بیع سلم درست ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر راس المال کے دراہم نصف سے زیادہ زیوف نکلے اور ان کو واپس کر کے اس مجلس میں کھرے در اہم لے لئے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بیع سلم فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب نصف راس المال سے زائد میں استبدال جائز قرار نہیں دیتے البتہ صاحبین کے نزدیک بیع سلم اس صورت میں بھی جائز ہو جائے گی۔ دوسری وجہ فساد یہ ہے کہ مسلم الیہ کبھی مسلم فیہ حاصل کرنے سے عاجز آ جاتا ہے، پس ایسی صورت میں مسلم الیہ پر رأس المال واپس
Salam. 36. Ashraf al-Bidaya, volume 9. He delivers it in the place of the contract. These are two issues. For them (the two companions) in the first: The purpose is achieved by pointing, so it resembles the price and the hire, and it became like a cloth. For him (Abu Hanifa): It may happen that some of them are counterfeit and are not exchanged in the session. If its quantity is not known, it is not known how much remains. Or perhaps he cannot obtain the subject matter, so he needs to return the capital. And the uncertain thing in this contract is like the certain because it is legislated with contradiction. Unlike if the capital is a cloth, because the cubits are a description in it, the contract does not relate to its quantity. Among its branches: if he makes salam in two types and does not specify the capital of each, or makes salam of two types and does not specify the quantity of one of them. Translation: And the quantity of the capital should be known while the salam contract is related to its quantity, like maquil, mawzuni, and ma'dudi. And specifying the place where he will deliver the muslam fih when the muslam fih has weight and expense. And the two companions said: There is no need to specify the capital when it is determined, and there is no need to specify the place of delivery, and he will deliver it in the place where the contract is made. So these are two issues. In the first issue, the proof of the two companions is that the purpose is achieved by pointing, so it resembles the price and the hire, and it became like a cloth. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that sometimes some dirhams turn out to be counterfeit and are not exchanged in that session. So if the quantity of the capital is not known, it cannot be known how much remains. Or sometimes the seller cannot obtain the muslam fih, so he needs to return the capital. And the uncertain thing in this contract is like the certain because it is legislated with the contradictory. Unlike when the capital is a cloth, because the mention of cubits is a description in it, the contract does not relate to its quantity. Among its branches is the issue that if he makes salam in two types and does not specify the capital of each, or makes salam of two types and does not specify the quantity of one of them. Explanation: This phrase explains two conditions regarding which Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions differed: 1. If the contract relates to the quantity of the capital, i.e., the parts of the muslam fih and the parts of the capital can be divided, for example the capital is from the category of maqilat, or mawzunat, or ma'dudat mutaqariba, then knowing its quantity by measure, weight, or count is necessary even if the capital is pointed to. This is the view of Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Shafi'i. (Mini) 2. If the muslam fih is something that has weight and there is expense in transferring it from one place to another, then specifying the place where he will deliver is also necessary. The two companions said that if the capital is determined by pointing, then specifying its quantity is not necessary, and specifying the place of the muslam fih is also not necessary; rather, he will deliver it in the place where the salam contract takes place. The author of Hidayah said that between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions, these two issues are disputed. In the first issue, the proof of the two companions is that the purpose of knowing the quantity of the capital is to be able to deliver the capital, and this purpose is also achieved by determining through pointing. So when the purpose is achieved by pointing, there is no great need to know the quantity of the capital by measure, weight, or count. And this resembles the price and the hire, i.e., just as in sale, pointing to the price without stating its quantity is sufficient, and in hire contract, pointing to the hire is sufficient, similarly pointing to the capital is sufficient; stating its quantity is not necessary. And it became like a cloth, i.e., if he points to a cloth and makes it the capital and does not specify the quantity of its cubits, it is valid. Similarly, if he determines a maqili, mawzuni, or ma'dudi item by pointing and makes it the capital, this is also valid even if its quantity by measure, weight, or count is not stated. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that ignorance of the quantity of the capital necessitates ignorance of the muslam fih, in that the seller spends the capital gradually, little by little. Sometimes after spending a portion of the capital, some dirhams turn out to be counterfeit and are not exchanged in the same session, i.e., in the same session where the seller returned the counterfeit dirhams to the buyer, the buyer does not take good dirhams in exchange. In such a case, to the extent of the counterfeit dirhams returned, the salam contract becomes fasid (invalid). And since the total quantity of the capital is not known, it cannot be known what portion of the capital the counterfeit dirhams constitute—a half, a third, or a fourth. And when this is not known, it will also not be known how much of the muslam fih has been voided and how much remains. From this, ignorance of the quantity of the muslam fih is apparent, and ignorance of the quantity of the muslam fih is unanimously a corruptor of salam. Therefore, in the mentioned case, the salam contract becomes fasid. And if the quantity of the capital is known, then by weighing the counterfeit dirhams it will be known how much of the muslam fih has been reduced and how much remains. For example, if the capital dirhams are one kilogram, and after spending some, some counterfeit dirhams appear, then these counterfeit dirhams will be weighed. For instance, if the counterfeit dirhams are 250 grams, then it is known that the good dirhams are 750 grams, i.e., three-quarters of the total capital remain, so one-quarter of the muslam fih is voided and three-quarters remain. So when the quantity of the capital is known, ignorance of the muslam fih is not necessitated, so the salam contract is valid. And when the quantity of the capital is unknown, ignorance of the muslam fih is necessitated, so the salam contract is fasid. And from the phrase 'and are not exchanged in the session' it appears that if the seller takes good dirhams in exchange for the counterfeit ones in the same session in which the counterfeit dirhams were returned, then the salam contract does not become invalid. But that is not the case; rather, the detail is that if the counterfeit dirhams are less than half of the capital, then if in the same session he takes good dirhams in exchange after returning them, then by consensus of the Hanafis the salam contract is valid. And if the counterfeit dirhams from the capital amount to more than half and he takes good dirhams in exchange in that session, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the salam contract becomes fasid, because Imam does not consider exchange (istibdal) permissible for more than half of the capital. However, according to the two companions, the salam contract is valid in this case as well. The second reason for invalidity is that the seller may become unable to obtain the muslam fih, so in that case the seller must return the capital.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about two conditions for a valid salam contract. The first condition concerns whether the quantity of the capital (ra's al-mal) must be specified when it is determined by pointing. The second condition concerns whether the place of delivery of the subject matter (muslam fih) must be specified when the subject matter is heavy and incurs transport costs. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that pointing suffices for the capital, analogous to price in a sale or hire, and that the place of delivery is the place of contract. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that ignorance of the capital's quantity leads to ignorance of the subject matter's quantity, especially when some of the capital may turn out to be counterfeit and cannot be replaced in the same session, or when the seller cannot deliver the subject matter. The passage also includes a branch ruling about when the capital consists of two different types. It further elaborates on a detail regarding counterfeit dirhams: if they constitute less than half and are replaced in the same session, the contract remains valid; if more than half, Abu Hanifa rules it invalid while the two companions uphold validity.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for specific goods to be delivered later.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital paid in advance by the buyer in a salam contract.
مسلم فيه (muslam fih): The subject matter to be delivered in the future in a salam contract.
صاحبين (al-sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two chief disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa.
زيوف (zuyuf): Counterfeit or defective dirhams that are not acceptable as valid currency in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is it necessary to specify the quantity of the capital in a salam contract even if it is indicated by pointing?
A) Because pointing is not a valid method of specification in contracts.
B) Because counterfeit coins may appear and without knowing the total quantity, it is impossible to determine how much of the subject matter is voided.
C) Because the two companions said so.
D) Because the Quran commands it.

Key Takeaway
In salam, the quantity of the capital must be specified even if pointed to, because otherwise uncertainty arises from potential counterfeit coins, leading to invalidity—a ruling preferred by Imam Abu Hanifa over the Sahibayn's more lenient view.

Specifying Capital by Pointing in Salam: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on capital specification in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa requires known quantity of capital in salam and evaluate the Sahibayn's counterargument based on analogy to cloth.

Core Idea
Pointing to capital is insufficient when its quantity is integral to the contract.

The passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether pointing to the capital without stating its quantity suffices in a salam contract. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that unknown capital quantity leads to unknown muslam fihi, invalidating the contract, while the Sahibayn analogize to cloth where pointing suffices. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What exactly is disputed? Is pointing to capital sufficient without stating quantity?
The dispute is about capital that is measured, weighed, or counted.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
They analogize to cloth, price, and wage where pointing suffices.
Analogy (qiyas) to cloth: pointing to a piece of cloth without stating yards is valid.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and two proofs
He argues that unknown capital quantity leads to unknown muslam fihi due to (1) defective coins and (2) inability to deliver.
These are rational proofs (dalil aqli) based on potential future events.
4
Analyze the response to the objection
Objection: these are hypothetical matters; salam is a concession, so hypotheticals should not be considered. Response: salam is contrary to analogy, so caution is required, and hypotheticals are treated as certain.
This ihtiyat (caution) is unique to salam.
5
Evaluate the response to the Sahibayn's analogy
Abu Hanifa responds that in cloth, the contract is not attached to the number of yards, whereas in measured/weighed/counted capital, the contract is attached to quantity. Thus the analogy is qiyas ma'a al-fariq.
This distinction is key: attachment to quantity changes the ruling.

بخلاف اذا كان رأس المال ...... الخ سے صاحبین کے قیاس و صار کالثوب کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر راس المال کپڑے کا ایسا تھان ہو جس کے گڑوں کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو تو بیع سلم اس لئے جائز ہے کہ کپڑے کے اندر گزوں کا بیان ایک وصف ہے جس کی مقدار کے ساتھ عقد متعلق نہیں ہوتا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر گز بیان کردہ مقدار سے زائد ہوئے تو زیادتی مشتری کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور اگر کم نکلے تو کمی کی وجہ سے ثمن میں سے کچھ کم نہیں ہوتا۔ بہر حال گزوں کی مقدار کے ساتھ عقد متعلق نہیں ہوتا۔ اور ہمارا کلام ایسے راس المال میں ہے جس کی مقدار کے ساتھ عقد متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے کپڑے کے تھان پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔
Chapter of Salam. The intended object (capital) is also attained by specifying through pointing. So when the intended object is attained by pointing, the need to know the quantity of capital by measurement or weight or number is not necessary. And this becomes similar to the price and the wage: just as in sale, pointing to the price without stating its quantity is sufficient, and in the contract of hire, pointing to the wage is sufficient, similarly, pointing to the capital is sufficient; stating its quantity is not necessary. And this becomes like a piece of cloth: if one points to a piece of cloth and makes it the capital, and the quantity of its yards is not stated, it is permissible. Similarly, if one specifies a thing measured by measurement, weight, or count by pointing and makes it the capital, this is also permissible, even if its quantity is not stated by measurement, weight, or number. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the unknownness of the quantity of capital necessitates the unknownness of the muslam fihi, in that the muslam ilayh gradually spends the capital amount little by little. Sometimes it happens that after spending a portion of the capital, some dirhams turn out to be defective, and they are not exchanged in the same session. That is, in the session in which the muslam ilayh returned the defective dirhams to rabb al-salam, if rabb al-salam did not take sound dirhams in exchange for them in that same session, then in that case, to the extent of the defective dirhams returned, the salam contract becomes invalid. And since the total quantity of capital is not known, it cannot be known what portion of the capital the defective dirhams constitute: half, one-third, or one-quarter. And when this cannot be known, it will not be known in how much of the muslam fihi the salam contract has been reduced and in how much it remains. And from this, the unknownness of the quantity of muslam fihi is apparent, and the unknownness of the quantity of muslam fihi is, by consensus, a nullifier of salam. Therefore, in the mentioned case, the salam sale becomes invalid. And if the quantity of capital is known, then by weighing the defective dirhams, it will be known in how much muslam fihi the salam contract has been reduced and in how much it remains. For example, the dirhams of capital are one kilogram, and after spending some, some dirhams turn out defective. Then those defective dirhams will be weighed. For instance, if the defective dirhams are 250 grams, it becomes known that the sound dirhams are 750 grams, i.e., three-quarters of the total capital remains. So one-quarter of the muslam fihi's salam becomes invalid, and for three-quarters it remains valid. Thus, when the quantity of capital is known, since the unknownness of muslam fihi is not necessitated, in that case the salam sale is valid. And when the quantity of capital is unknown, since the unknownness of muslam fihi is necessitated, in that case the salam sale is invalid. From "and he does not exchange in the session" it is understood that if the muslam ilayh takes sound dirhams in exchange for the defective dirhams in the same session in which the defective dirhams were returned, the salam sale does not become invalid. However, that is not the case; rather its detail is that if the defective dirhams are less than half of the capital, and in the session in which they were returned to rabb al-salam, if he takes sound dirhams in exchange for them in that same session, then by the consensus of the Hanafis, the salam sale becomes valid. And if the defective dirhams of the capital exceed half, and they are returned and sound dirhams taken in that session, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the salam sale becomes invalid, because Imam Sahib does not permit substitution (istibdal) for more than half of the capital. However, according to the Sahibayn, the salam sale becomes valid in this case as well. The second cause of invalidity is that the muslam ilayh sometimes becomes incapable of obtaining the muslam fihi. In such a case, it becomes necessary for the muslam ilayh to return the capital, and since the quantity of capital is unknown, returning the capital becomes impossible. And when returning the unknown quantity of capital is impossible in the case of inability to deliver the muslam fihi, it is necessary that the quantity of capital be known. And when it is necessary that the quantity of capital be known (for the purpose that return be possible in case of inability), then when the quantity is unknown, the salam sale becomes invalid. If it is objected that the emergence of some defective dirhams in the capital or the muslam ilayh's inability to obtain the muslam fihi is a hypothetical matter, and a hypothetical matter is not considered, especially in a place whose basis is on concession. And since the basis of salam sale is on concession, no hypothetical matter is considered in salam sale. And when the mentioned hypothetical matter is not considered, then the salam sale will not become invalid due to the unknown quantity of capital. The answer to this is that in salam, a hypothetical matter is treated like certainty, because salam has been legislated despite being contrary to analogy and contrary to sale, because in salam, the muslam fihi (the object) is non-existent, and the non-existence of the sold item is contrary to permissibility, and when something is legislated contrary to analogy, caution (ihtiyat) becomes obligatory. Therefore, in salam sale, out of caution, the hypothetical matter is placed in the rank of certainty and existence, and the salam sale is ruled invalid. "Contrary to when the capital is..." etc. is the answer to the Sahibayn's analogy and its becoming like cloth. The gist of the answer is that if the capital is a piece of cloth whose quantity of yards is unknown, then the salam sale is permissible because the statement of yards within the cloth is a description with which the contract is not attached. This is why if the yards exceed the stated quantity, the excess belongs to the buyer, and if they are less, nothing is reduced from the price. In any case, the contract is not attached to the quantity of yards. And our discussion is about a capital whose quantity the contract is attached to. So with this difference, analogy to the piece of cloth is analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether pointing to the capital suffices in a salam contract. The author begins by stating the general ruling: pointing to the capital is sufficient, just like pointing to the price in sale or wage in hire. An analogy is drawn to a piece of cloth where the number of yards is not stated; the contract is valid. However, Imam Abu Hanifa argues that unknown capital quantity leads to unknown muslam fihi due to two possibilities: (1) emergence of defective coins, and (2) inability of the muslam ilayh to deliver. For the first, if defective coins appear and are not exchanged in the same session, the contract becomes invalid to the extent of the defective portion, but without knowing the total capital, one cannot determine what fraction of the muslam fihi is affected. For the second, if the muslam ilayh becomes unable to deliver, he must return the capital, which is impossible if its quantity is unknown. An objection is raised that these possibilities are hypothetical and salam being a concession should not consider hypotheticals. The response is that salam is a contract contrary to analogy (non-existent object sold); thus caution (ihtiyat) is required, and hypothetical matters are treated as certain. The Sahibayn analogize to cloth, but the author responds that in cloth, the contract is not attached to the number of yards, whereas in capital subject to measurement/weight/count, the contract is attached to quantity; thus the analogy is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital in a salam contract, which is paid in advance.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The object to be delivered in the future in a salam contract.
دراہم زیوف (darahim zuyuf): Defective or counterfeit dirhams that are not acceptable as valid currency.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): Analogy with a difference; a type of invalid analogy where there is a significant distinction between the original and the analogized cases.
استبدال (istibdal): Substitution, here referring to exchanging defective dirhams for sound ones in the same session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why does an unknown quantity of capital invalidate a salam contract?
A) Because the capital must be handed over immediately.
B) Because it leads to unknown muslam fihi due to possible defective coins or inability to deliver.
C) Because the contract is not a sale.
D) Because the capital must be in dirhams only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if the capital in a salam contract is of a type that requires known quantity, simply pointing to it is insufficient; the contract is fasid per Abu Hanifa.

Salam with Two Commodities and Unknown Capital Allocation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam with unknown capital allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a salam contract with two muslam fihis and a single unallocated capital, and explain the proof for each.

Core Idea
In salam, unallocated capital between commodities is invalid per Abu Hanifa but valid per Sahibayn.

This lesson explores a branch issue from Al-Hidayah: a salam contract where the capital is not explicitly allocated among multiple muslam fihis. Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on the ruling, each supported by distinct reasoning. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how unknownness (jahalah) affects contract validity in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) a single capital for two muslam fihis, (2) two currencies for one muslam fihi where one currency quantity is unknown. Note the common element: unknown allocation of capital.
2
State the dispute for each scenario
For each scenario, note that Imam Abu Hanifa rules the contract invalid (fasid), while the Sahibayn rule it valid (sahih).
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa argues capital is divided by value (estimated → unknown). Sahibayn argue pointing to specific items suffices. Understand the methodological difference: determinacy vs. estimation.
4
Consider the principle of safqah
In the second scenario, Abu Hanifa invokes the principle that if part of a single bargain is invalid, the whole is invalid. Sahibayn reject this because pointing achieves determinacy.
5
Note the practical consequence
If you follow Abu Hanifa, such contracts must be repudiated; if you follow Sahibayn, they are binding. The passage gives no tarjih, so the mufti must weigh the evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین رحمہم اللہ کے مابین اختلاف کے فروع میں سے ایک یہ مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر ایک سو در اہم کا، ایک گر گندم اور ایک گر جو میں عقد سلم کیا یعنی ایک گر گندم اور ایک گر جو کو مسلم فیہ قرار دیا اور ایک سود را ہم کو راس المال قرار دیا اور ان دونوں میں ہر ایک کا راس المال علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہیں کیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہو جائے گی۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک سو در اہم گندم اور جو پر قیمت کے اعتبار سے تقسیم کئے جائیں گے اور قیمت کی معرفت چونکہ اندازے سے ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے راس المال کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہوگی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معین شئی کی طرف اشارہ کرنا جواز عقد کے لئے کافی ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا گیا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بیچ مسلم جائز ہو جائے گی ۔ یا دو جنسوں کا عقد سلم کیا اور ان میں سے ایک کی مقدار بیان نہیں کی ،مثلاً در اہم اور نا نیر کا ایک گر گندم میں عقد سلم کیا اور دراہم اور دنا نیر میں سے ایک کی مقدار معلوم ہوگئی اور دوسرے کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہوئی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ بیع سلم نا جائز ہوگی ، کیونکہ جب ایک کی مقدار مجہول ہے تو اس کے حصہ میں عقد مسلم باطل ہو جائے گا اور جب اس کے حصہ میں عقد مسلم باطل ہو گیا تو دوسرے کے حصہ میں بھی عقد مسلم باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ صفقہ ایک ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ اشارہ پایا گیا بایں طور
The author of Hidayah says: Among the branches of the difference between Imam Sahib and the Sahibayn (may Allah have mercy on them) is this issue: If one makes a salam contract for one hundred dirhams for one karr of wheat and one karr of barley, i.e., he makes one karr of wheat and one karr of barley the muslam fihi, and makes one hundred dirhams the capital, and does not state the capital for each separately, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this salam sale is not permissible, and according to the Sahibayn, it is permissible. The proof of Imam Sahib is that the one hundred dirhams will be divided over the wheat and barley according to value, and since value is known by estimation, the quantity of capital for each of them will not be known. The proof of the Sahibayn is that pointing to a specific thing is sufficient for the permissibility of the contract, and that has been achieved. So in this case, the salam sale is permissible. Or if one makes a salam contract of two currencies (goods) and the quantity of one of them is not stated, for example, one makes a salam contract of dirhams and dananir for one karr of wheat, and the quantity of one of the dirhams and dananir becomes known and the quantity of the other is not known, then according to Imam Sahib, this salam sale is not permissible, because when the quantity of one is unknown, the salam contract becomes invalid in its portion, and when the salam contract becomes invalid in its portion, it also becomes invalid in the other portion, because the transaction is one. And according to the Sahibayn, it is permissible, because pointing has been achieved, in this manner...
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents a branch issue arising from the earlier dispute on specifying capital. Two scenarios are given: (1) A single capital of 100 dirhams is used to purchase two muslam fihis (1 karr each of wheat and barley) without separately allocating the capital to each. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that this is invalid because the capital must be distributed by value, which is estimated and thus unknown. The Sahibayn rule it valid because pointing to the specifics suffices. (2) Two currencies (dirhams and dananir) are used as capital for one muslam fihi (1 karr wheat), but the quantity of one currency is known and the other unknown. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the contract is invalid because the unknown portion renders the whole transaction invalid (since it is one bargain). The Sahibayn rule it valid because pointing to each is achieved. The text ends mid-sentence, likely continuing with the Sahibayn's proof.

Key Terms
صر فقہ (safqah): The transaction or bargain; a single contract, treating the entire exchange as one unit.
قیمت (qimat): Value; the market price of the goods, used to allocate the capital proportionally.
دنا نیر (dananir): Plural of dinar; gold coins used as currency or capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the branch issue, why does Imam Abu Hanifa rule the salam invalid when a single capital is used for two muslam fihis without allocating?
A) Because the muslam fihi must be of the same type.
B) Because the capital must be handed over in full at the time of contract.
C) Because the capital share for each muslam fihi is unknown due to division by estimated value.
D) Because the contract is not a valid salam since the capital is not in dirhams.

Key Takeaway
In salam, unknown allocation of capital between multiple muslam fihis leads to invalidity per Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn hold that pointing to specific items suffices.

Necessity of Knowing Capital Quantity in Salam
Ruling with proof on capital quantity in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school requires the capital quantity in salam to be known and refute the Sahibayn's analogy to cloth.

Core Idea
In salam, hypothetical possibilities are treated as certain because the contract is contrary to qiyas.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses a key condition for the validity of a salam contract: the capital (ra's al-mal) must be known in quantity. The author explains why unknown quantity invalidates the contract, how an objection regarding hypothetical matters is answered, and why the Sahibayn's analogy to cloth is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The ruling is that salam is invalid (fasid) if the quantity of capital is unknown. The basis: if the seller cannot deliver the goods, the capital must be returned; unknown quantity makes return impossible.
2
Understand the objection and the Hanafi response
Objection: the possibility of defective dirhams or inability to deliver is hypothetical and should not be considered, especially since salam is a license. Response: because salam is contrary to qiyas, caution is required, so hypothetical matters are treated as certain.
This is istihsan.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's analogy and its refutation
Sahibayn analogize capital to a cloth where yards are unknown, arguing salam is permissible. Refutation: in cloth, the yard measurement is a description not attached to the contract (excess belongs to buyer, shortfall doesn't reduce price). Capital quantity is directly attached, so analogy is qiyas ma'a al-fariq.
4
Extract the legal principle
In rulings established contrary to qiyas (like salam), caution requires treating hypothetical matters as certain to protect the contract's validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السلم
كرنا ضروری ہوگا اور راس المال کی مقدار چونکہ مجہول ہے اس لئے راس المال واپس کرنا بھی متعد ر ہوگا۔ اور جب مسلم فیہ ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہونے کی صورت میں مجہول المقدار رأس المال کا واپس کرنا معد ہو گیا تو ضروری ہے کہ راس المال کی مقدار معلوم ہو۔ اور جب رأس المال کی مقدار کا ( اس غرض سے کہ عاجزی کی صورت میں واپس کرنا ممکن ہو ) معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے تو مقدار جہول ہونے کی صورت میں بیع سلم فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اگر یہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ راس المال کے بعض در اہم کا زیوف لنکلنا یا مسلم الیہ کا مسلم فیہ حاصل کرنے سے عاجز آجانا ایک امر موہوم ہے اور امر موہوم معتبر نہیں ہوتا خاص طور پر ایسی جگہ جس کا مدار ہی رخصت پر ہو۔ اور بیچ مسلم کا مدار چونکہ رخصت پر ہے اس لئے بیع سلم میں کسی امر موہوم کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا اور جب مذکور د امر موہوم معتبر نہیں ہے تو راس المال کی مقدار مجہول ہونے سے بیع سلم بھی فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بیع سلم میں امر موہوم تحقیق کے مانند ہوتا ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم خلاف قیاس، منافی بیع ہونے کے باوجود مشروع کی گئی ہے، اس لئے کہ بیع سلم میں مسلم فیہ یعنی میچ معدوم ہوتی ہے اور مبیع کا معدوم ہونا جواز کے منافی ہے اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس مشروع ہو اس میں احتیاط واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے بیع سلم میں احتیاطاً امر موہوم کو تحقیق اور موجود کے مرتبہ میں اتار کر بیع سلم کو فاسد قرار دیا گیا۔
بخلاف اذا كان رأس المال ...... الخ سے صاحبین کے قیاس و صار کالثوب کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر راس المال کپڑے کا ایسا تھان ہو جس کے گڑوں کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو تو بیع سلم اس لئے جائز ہے کہ کپڑے کے اندر گزوں کا بیان ایک وصف ہے جس کی مقدار کے ساتھ عقد متعلق نہیں ہوتا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر گز بیان کردہ مقدار سے زائد ہوئے تو زیادتی مشتری کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور اگر کم نکلے تو کمی کی وجہ سے ثمن میں سے کچھ کم نہیں ہوتا۔ بہر حال گزوں کی مقدار کے ساتھ عقد متعلق نہیں ہوتا۔ اور ہمارا کلام ایسے راس المال میں ہے جس کی مقدار کے ساتھ عقد متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے کپڑے کے تھان پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔
The chapter of Salam... it will be necessary to do, and since the quantity of the capital is unknown, returning the capital will also be difficult. And when in case of inability to deliver the salam goods, returning the unknown-quantity capital becomes difficult, it is necessary that the quantity of the capital be known. And when knowing the quantity of the capital is necessary (for the purpose that it may be returned in case of inability), then in the case of unknown quantity, the salam sale will become fasid (invalid). If it is objected that the existence of defective dirhams in some of the capital or the salam party's inability to obtain the salam goods is a hypothetical matter, and a hypothetical matter is not considered, especially in a matter that is based on license (rukhsah). And since the salam sale is based on license, no hypothetical matter will be considered in salam, and when the aforementioned hypothetical matter is not considered, then the salam sale will not become invalid due to the unknown quantity of capital. The answer to this is that in salam, a hypothetical matter is treated like certainty, because salam, contrary to qiyas and contrary to the nature of sale, has been legislated. For in salam, the salam goods (muslam fihi) is non-existent, and non-existence of the sold item is contrary to permissibility. And when a thing is legislated contrary to qiyas, caution (ihtiyat) becomes obligatory. Therefore, in salam, out of caution, a hypothetical matter is brought down to the level of certainty and existence, and thus the salam sale is declared invalid. Contrary to the case when the capital... etc. This is the answer to the analogy of the Sahibayn that it becomes like cloth. The essence of the answer is that if the capital is a piece of cloth whose yards are unknown in quantity, then salam is permissible because the mention of yards in cloth is a description that is not attached to the contract with respect to quantity. For this reason, if the yards exceed the specified amount, the excess belongs to the buyer, and if they are less, nothing is deducted from the price. In any case, the quantity of yards is not attached to the contract. And our discussion concerns a capital whose quantity is attached to the contract. Therefore, with this difference, analogizing to a piece of cloth is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the Hidayah addresses the necessity of knowing the quantity of the capital (ra's al-mal) in a salam contract. The author states that if the capital is unknown in measure, the salam is invalid because if the seller cannot deliver the goods, the capital must be returned, but if its quantity is unknown, return is impossible. An objection is raised: the possibility of defective dirhams or inability to deliver is hypothetical and should not be considered, especially since salam is a concession (rukhsah) contrary to qiyas. The author replies that because salam is established contrary to qiyas (selling non-existent goods), caution is required, so hypothetical possibilities are treated as certain. The passage then addresses the Sahibayn's analogy comparing unknown capital to cloth where yards are unknown. The author refutes this by noting that in the cloth case, the yard measurement is merely a description not integral to the contract (if yards differ, the price adjusts), whereas in the capital case the quantity is directly tied to the contract. Therefore, the analogy is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Key Terms
راس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital or price paid in a salam contract, which must be known in quantity to allow return if needed.
امر موہوم (amr mawhum): A hypothetical or improbable matter that is not normally considered in law.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because there is a material difference between the original and the new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why is a salam contract fasid if the quantity of capital is unknown?
A) Because the capital must be divisible into shares.
B) Because if the seller cannot deliver, the capital must be returned, and return is impossible if its quantity is unknown.
C) Because the buyer might not have the full amount.
D) Because the salam contract is a form of gambling.

Key Takeaway
In a salam contract, the capital must be known in quantity; otherwise, the contract is fasid, because return in case of seller's inability becomes impossible.
